After I have completed the book for you, sons, which is the last in the knowledge of medicine with its supplement, and having reached the end in it, through expositions of it, and its declarations, it seemed to me to complete it for you with this Treatise, which is a part of operation, that is, surgery, with hand.
Since operation with hand is laid low in our region, and at our time entirely deprived of it; perhaps until the knowledge of it has perished and its trace has vanished, and only small descriptions remain in ancient books which have been changed by hands, and error and hesitation occurred, so that the intentions have been closed and the will was dispersed; It seemed to me that I should revive it with this Treatise according to the way of expositions, declarations, and abbreviation, and also that I come with the forms of iron tools of Cautery and the rest of the instruments of work, with the addition of declarations and the need for it.
The reason why a good craftsman of this art with his hand is not found in this time is that the art of medicine is long and its author must be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, which Galen described, until he knows the remedies for the limbs and their shapes, and their conjunction and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, muscles, their number, and their exits, and the vessels of pulsation, quiet ones, and their locations.
And for this reason, Hippocrates said that much is the name with its name, but little is the work, and especially in the art of hand.
We have indeed said about it at the beginning of this book.
Because he who is not knowing what we have said about anatomy, is not purged from already falling into error, in which men are slain: as I have seen many of those who are formed by this science, and boast themselves about it without knowledge, and without experience.
Because I have seen a foolish physician follow an aposteme (boil) on the neck of a woman, and cut some arteries in her neck: wherefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead in his hands.
And I have seen another physician presume to extract a stone from an old man, which had grown, and the stone was large. Therefore he came to him, and extracted it with a piece of bladder. Wherefore the man died on the third day.
And indeed I had already been summoned to extract it; and I saw from the size of the stone, and the condition of the patient, that he would die.
And I have seen another physician receiving a fee from some Duke of our land because of medicine; and a black eunuch was with him, who had a fracture near the heel of his leg: and the physician in his ignorance, bound up the fracture on a wound with awls and strong needles, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he cured him according to his own devices. Afterwards he sent him away for some days and commanded him not to loosen the bandage; and it stood thus until there was an abscess on his leg, and his foot, and it reached its destruction.
I was then summoned to him; and I hastened to loosen the bandage; and there came peace, and he was delivered from his pains.
Nevertheless corruption had already been confirmed in the member; and I could not arrest it.
Apply [the ointment] so that the corruption may stop spreading in the member until it perishes.
And I saw another physician who pierced a malignant apostema; and it became ulcerated for days, until the wickedness of it was manifested with its lord.
Because when the cancer is pure due to black bile, then it should not be approached with iron at all unless it is in a member that can endure it, so that the whole of it may be cut off.
And because of that which is said in O Filii, it is necessary for you to know that the operation is divided into two divisions: namely, the operation associated with safety; and the operation where danger is present in many arrangements.
And I have already aroused myself in every place of this book, wherever there comes an operation where there is fear and dread.
Therefore it is necessary for you to be cautious of that and to separate it: so that the foolish may not find a way to speak about it and shameful things.
Take therefore the measurement with caution and protection, and your sick ones with ease and firmness, and make use of a better way leading by the grace of God to salvation and praiseworthy succession: and leave behind terrible illnesses that are difficult to heal; and separate yourselves from what makes you fear, so that hesitation in faith and comfort may not enter upon you.
For it is more becoming for your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your ranks.
Galen indeed said so in some of his warnings. Do not treat an evil disease; lest you be called a bad physician.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters. Â¶
First Chapter.
On Cautery with fire, and Cautery with sharp medicine, is treated, and ordered from head to foot, and forms of the instruments, and tools for Cautery: and all that is necessary in the procedure.
De Arte Circumcisionis, sive Preputiorum Sectionis.
On the Art of Circumcision, or Preputial Section.
Chapter third.
On restoration, displacement, and treatment of twisting and similar cases: a chapter arranged from head to foot and forms of instruments.
Before I remind you of the operation with it, it is necessary to say the quality of its remedies and its harms, and in what composition it should be displayed.
I say therefore, that the discourse on the quality of the remedy of the cautery, and its harm, is a long, subtle, knowledge, and secret hidden matter.
Also there was a multitude of wise men who spoke about it and disagreed on it; and for me enough is said from their discourses, fearing prolongation.
I say therefore, that the cautery applies universally to all compositions, which are with matter and without matter; except for two compositions, which are a hot composition without matter and a dry composition without matter.
In a hot and dry composition with matter, they disagreed. Some said that the cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the opposite, that is, that the cautery is not suitable in the disease which is of heat and dryness; because the nature of fire is heat; and it is inconvenient to heal from a hot and dry disease with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite said that the cautery is beneficial in every hot and dry disease which occurs in the bodies of humans; because when you compare the body of a man and its humidity to the composition of fire, you find the body of a man cold.
And I myself say by his speech: because I have often seen that proven to me.
However, it is not necessary for that to come up, unless the one who has been proven and experienced in the exercise of the final chapter on cautery, and knows the diversity of human complexions, and the disposition of diseases in themselves, and their causes and accidents, and the space of time of those diseases.
From the remaining compositions there is no fear for you: and particularly in diseases that are cold and moist. For they all agree among themselves on these [matters]: and they do not disagree on the use of cautery with them.
And know, my sons, that from the secret of healing by cautery with fire, and its goodness over the cautery with medicine burning, it is because fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the member which is being cauterized: and it does not harm another member joined to it, unless by slight damage.
But the action of burning medicine reaches to that which extends from the members: and perhaps it causes difficulty in healing disease in the member, and perhaps it kills.
Fire, however, on account of its subtlety and goodness of substance, does not do that unless it is excessive.
But now it has become clear to us by means of experiment, because of the length of service and diligence with the art, and because of its firmness in matters of truth: and for that reason I excuse myself from the length of discourse.
And if it were not forbidden to this book of mine, I would bring to you the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies, by which it expels diseases through philosophical demonstration, which would become clear to your minds.
And know, my sons, that they themselves differ in time when it is appropriate to make a cautery, and they put the better time in truth.
And I say that a cautery is appropriate at any time: because damage occurring due to time is submerged in the benefit, which is attracted by the cautery. And particularly if a cautery is for pains from necessary pains, strong, sharp ones which cannot tolerate delay: because it is feared that what happens will be greater evil than slight damage due to time.
And let it not enter your minds, my sons, that which is not believed except by the vulgar and foolish physicians, namely that there is no return for the sickness which is cured by cauterization, and they put forth this consequence, but things are not as they think: therefore because cauterization is not, except in place of medicine, which alters complexion, and removes humidities which are the causes, why pains occur.
Cauterization is unnecessary over medicine on account of the swiftness of its health, and the power of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion: and it is possible that sickness may return at some hour according to the complexion of the sick, and the location of the sickness, and the power of the sickness: and what is prepared in the body from accumulation of superfluities in it, and what reaches it in acquisition from food, and similar things from causes, unless sickness occurs, in which cauterization is administered.
A subtle sickness in a member of small superfluities and humidities, as cauterization of a tooth, due to pain, and similar things, it is possible that that pain will not return in him. But this happens in few cases.
However, the speech of the vulgar is true again, that cauterization is the last medicine, it is a correct speech, not in what they intend by it: because they believe that there is no cure which gives with medicine, nor with anything after the falling away of cauterization.
But things are contrary to theirs, and their intention, that cauterization is the last medicine, is not, except that when we administer modes of cure in any sickness, and they do not give those medicines: then we administer caution at the end, and it gives: then it comes about that cauterization is the last medicine, not according to the intention which the vulgar and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that a cautionery with gold is better than one with iron; and they did not say this, if not for the equality of gold, and the loftiness of its substance; and they said that it does not cause pus at the site of the cautionery. That is not entirely true; for I have proven that it does not do so in certain bodies without others.
And a cautionery with it is good, and better than one with iron, as they said. However, when you make the cautionery with fire from gold, it is not apparent to you when lit according to the amount that you wish, due to the redness of gold; and when it reaches the same, and if you add more heat to it, it liquefies in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls into trouble from this; and because of that, we use cautionery with iron more quickly and closely in our operations, for its accuracy.
And I myself have organized this chapter according to the cautery, following the chapters; and I have arranged it from top to bottom, so that those seeking it may find what they want from it.
Chapter II.
Here the cauterization is applied for the dominion of humidity and coldness upon the brain: these two are the causes of soda, and the flow of abundance of fluids from the head to the parts of eyes and ears, and abundance of sleep, and pain in teeth, and pain in throat: and universally all sickness, which occurs due to coldness, such as paralysis, sodae (an ailment), epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar ailments.
The method of cauterization is that you instruct the patient: to evacuate in the first instance with dissolved medicine purifying the head for three or four nights, according to the strength of the patient, and his age, and his custom.
Then instruct him (the patient) to make heat on his head with a hot stone. Then make him sit between your hands in square form, so that he now places his hands upon his chest.
Then place the palm of your hand on top of his nose root between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger comes to be, mark that place with an unburned (area).
Then heat the cautery iron with oil: this is its shape.
Then put it on the marked place without burning, while gradually pressing your hand down and you turn it (the cautery). Then lift your hand quickly, and look at the spot.
If you see that a piece of bone of the skull or vegetable matter has been uncovered, then lift your hand. And if not, keep putting your hand with the iron or with another until it becomes cold; until you see the bones that I have told you about.
Then take something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and immerse the cotton in it, and place it on the spot; and leave it for three days.
Then place on top of him a woolen cloth soaked in butter, and let it remain on the spot until the burn is destroyed by fire. Then treat that with four-ingredient ointment until it heals.
It has been said that the longer an open wound remains, the more it discharges pus; therefore, it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone; and hold the cautery until something of the bone's thickness is burned.
Then grind down the bone after it has been burned, then treat it.
Others say that when the cautery is applied to the end, it should make an impression on the bone for as long as the bone falls out, so that it becomes like a pierced hole: or an instrument that women put in place with a small amount of alphabet solution: and they think that vapors from the head are exhaled through this place; and the open wound is left for a long time.
Then it is treated until it hardens.
But these two types of cautery do not seem to me at all effective except in some people according to the way of fear.
And let it be released from there, it is better for his health with me.
For the head is weakened by the continuous solution of its own; as we have testified in other members; and especially when the head is naturally weak and frail; and the first type of cautery is safer and better for me, and I use it: so work with it for safety.
Chapter III.
When a chronic pain occurs throughout the head and it persists in an unwell person, and they use honey, vinegar, cupping glasses, oil, and plasters. And particularly if the head has already been burnt with a cautery once as we have mentioned, and none of those things help him, then consider it. If the head of an unwell person is strong by nature and not weak, and it finds a very intense cold, then burn it with another cautery slightly. Then burn the entire horn of his own head with a cautery, so that the skin is not penetrated and the amount of bone exposed, as we have mentioned. Burn the entire head with one cautery at the occiput of his own head, at a place called the "was", and it is a place where the bladder is placed; and squeeze your mother's milk into this, and do not expose the bone. For the sick person finds a very intense pain there due to that, and different from the pain of all the other cauterizations of the head.
And I say that this cautery should be in its place, and it must be a cautery with which the horns of the head are burnt, and the occiput more subtly with the cautery with which the middle of the head is burned.
Chapter 4.
When pain occurs in part of the head and it swells or spreads to the eye, and the head is treated with cleansing medicines and the rest of the treatment, as I have said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve altogether, then cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either cauterization with a burning medicine or with iron.
The cautery with burning medicine is, that you receive one tooth of garlic, peel it and cut off its ends from both sides. Then cut the painful location at the time with a broad leech, until there is a place under the skin where the tooth can be captured.
Insert it into the same under the skin until it is hidden; then bind it over it with a decent bandage and leave it for fifteen hours, then dissolve it, and remove the garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days; afterwards place a hot iron submerged in butter on it until a pus is formed; then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do that with certain burning medicines which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise on poisons.
However, cauterizing it with iron is as follows. The form of the burning iron is as follows.
It is called a Clavilus, because the shape of its head resembles that of a nail, in which there is some sharpness, and in the middle of it there is a small protuberance.
Then place it on the location and hold your hand; and you rotate the iron slowly with speed; and let the quantity that is burned be of the thickness of the skin, just like half of it. And lift your hand so that an artery, which is below, is not burned and there is a blood flow.
Then immerse the iron in brine water, and place it on the location, and leave it for three days; then immerse the iron in butter; afterwards care for it with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicania (hemiplegia) with the second part of the Cautery cutlery. caution against cutting an artery during this hemicrania (not the ancient one specifically)
On the method of cauterization in the ancient hemicrania.
When treating hemicrania as previously mentioned in treatment and as stated in the division of ailments, and treatment is not effective; and you observe from the disease that what was said about cauterization with the first cautery or cauterization with fire does not suffice for him, then it is necessary to use an iron cautery, until it becomes white after marking the place of pain with a line, whose length is half the digit, or approximately so; and place your hand instead, and press it tightly until you cut the artery, and reach the bone.
But it is necessary that you be careful to avoid the continuous jaw movement during chewing, so as not to burn the side or the nerve that moves it, in order to prevent a spasm.
And let there be caution and care regarding the flow of blood from the cut artery. Indeed, fear arises in its incision, especially for those who do not know what is being done and are not attentive or experienced; and above all, they abandon the procedure first.
And I shall come with a reminder about the management of bleeding from the cut artery according to its own method and in its proper place within this book.
If you observe from the disease that this iron cautery does not suffice for him, and if you see a weak body tolerating the cautery in the middle of the head as we have said, then treat the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the cautery as we have said in the chapter on artery extraction with a cautery having two blades. Cauterization is indeed better this way and more suitable.
On the method of cauterizing in ear pain.
When there is pain in the ear due to coldness, and it is treated with solutions, and the rest of the treatment as we said in division, and the pain does not subside, then cauterization with fire: this is what is called Punctum, whose form is as follows.
Then, after burning the punctum around the entire ear as it is rolled, or around both sides if pain is present on both sides. And extend the cautery from the root of the ear slightly after marking the spots with wax; let the amount of cauterization be ten punctae for the entire ear, and approximately so.
Then, care for the areas until they heal.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in Torture.
Chapter VII.
Treatment with cauterization for tortures only pertains to those types that arise from phlegm, as we discussed in the division of diseases.
And avoid cauterization for the type that arises from exhaustion and muscle spasm.
If the treatment of this type of torture with herbs, purges and gargles does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the sick person with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, and the second a little below its time, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
Place your cautery on the weaker side (of the body). Since softening does not occur unless in the healthy part.
And the shape of cauterization is to cauterize oneself with the cautery along the extreme tip of the upper edge of the ear lobe, slightly below the skull's horn; and in another place at the time, whose length should be similar to that of a thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until the quantity of half the thickness of the skin is burnt.
And this is the form of the cautery and it belongs to the species of a knife, whose shape was given earlier; but it should not be too fine, as you can see; and it is necessary that the knife has a little excess coarseness in it.
Then treat the locations with what was previously mentioned until healed.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for apoplexy (ancient).
If the apoplexy is ancient and the treatment with what was said does not help, and the sick person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on all of his skull's horn, and with a cautery in the middle of his head, as was said, and with a cautery at the back of his head according to what was previously mentioned; and the method of cauterization should be as previously described.
Also cauterized on the face of the stomach with a Cautery; and it is more extreme.
Then it is cured with what preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in drink there be first of all large amounts of hysso and brain-purifying pills.
Then shave the head of the sick person entirely, and place upon his occiput an ointment from synapse as described in the treatise on ointments; and apply it frequently.
For this is the method of cautery; and do this in accordance with the same order as I stated there.
If therefore he is cured by it, that is good. If not: then make three cauteries in the back part of his head, which extend from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye; and place between each cautery a thickness equal to a finger.
Then care for the cautery, with what preceded.
If you wish an additional measure, and the sick person can endure it; then make a cautery in the middle. If you wish an additional measure: then cauterize him on both horns.
Then care for him until he is cured; let the cautery be anointed in the manner as stated before.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed with the mundification of the head with hyson, and with what I said.
Then scrape the head of the sick person: afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery over the entire horn of the head, and with a cautery over the back of it, and three over the spine of the neck.
If, however, you need softening of the body with more of these [substances], and the person is weak and the illness is strong: then cauterize it with four cauteries over the spine of the back, and the last one with a cautery, until it burns through most of its skin, and loosen your hand. Then take care of him until he is well: and in this way cauterize with oil.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
A epileptic is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you clean the brain of him first with hyssop, and also with the remedy that we have said in the division when the sick person is severe or tolerant to medication.
If it is a child who does not tolerate medications, then administer gargarisma, and cleaning mouthwash for the brain, before that many days with good food purification.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize him with one cautery on the middle of the skull as previously described; and another cautery on the back of his head, and over all the horn of his skull with cautery. If the sick person is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with cauteries as previously mentioned in the presence of paralysis, and soften the body on the spine of the neck, and the spine of the back; and let the cautery be oiled according to the previous method.
If the sick person is a child, then place the subtle cautery in this manner:
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with cauteries as we have said for paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of declivities leading to melancholy and the body of the sick person is damp, then give him a drink that cleans his brain as previously mentioned in the division; then shave the head of the sick person, and make a properly centred bandage of linen like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the skull; and the sick person sitting squarely should be held from all sides.
Then present the liniment. And it is more fitting from ancient goat butter. And heat it over a gentle fire with measured heating that the finger can bear when introduced into it. Then evacuate it from the middle of its head in a circle, and let it cool down.
Do this to the sick person once a week with good care otherwise, until it is cured.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small punctures in it, provided that you hold the hand with a cautery; it should be fragrant.
For this type of cauterization moistens the brain with its nature.
Then place it on top of a cotton cloth soaked in goat butter or chicken fat.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for falling water on the eye.
Chapter 13.
When you are informed of the start of water in the eye through the signs that I mentioned in the division, then begin and rinse the sick one, with it to clean his head.
And keep him away from all moistnesses, and make him sit in a bath for several days in fasting.
Then order him to shave his head, and brand him in the middle of his head. Then brand him on both temples with two brands, if there is an obstruction of water flow in both eyes at once: or from one side, if there is an obstruction of water in one eye: and cut with the cauterization all veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the brands be long in the width of the temples: and avoid bleeding.
If you see something from him (the patient), then cut it off immediately with any medicine that is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and cutting them off, and caution against bleeding.
And sometimes he (the patient) should be branded on the neck, under two bones, with two brands brought to their extremities.
Chapter on ancient methods of branding in tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and constant: and they are over veins, and arteries that are manifest on the outside of the head, it is verified that this is from excesses of cold, phlegmatic fluids: then brand with a cauterization as I described in the obstruction of water flow, branding in the middle of the head, and with two brands on both temples, and with two brands on the neck under two bones. And if it is necessary to add something, then brand him carefully on all sides of the eye with a small brand at the edge of the eyebrow.
Method of cauterizing in the stench of the nose.
When you treat it, as we said in division, and the medication does not help: then rush, and for three nights give to drink infirmocochia: then shave its head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with the cautery oiliver. Then cauterize it with two cauteries and a claw-shaped cautery on top of the eyebrows slightly below the hairline.
And be careful not to cut the artery.
And this is the form of the claw-shaped cautery.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for swelling of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is swollen due to illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery using this crescent-shaped cautery.
If you wish, cauterize it above both eyebrows with two cauteries in all places; let them extend from the temples and have a length equal to that of the eyebrows; do not place your hand with the cautery at the very edge but rather according to the amount that is being cauterized, the third eyelash.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for eyelashes growing into the eye causing pain.
The cautery is in it according to two modes: either a cautery with fire; or a cautery with a burning medicine.
In the cautery with fire, order the patient to shave before it, if he is among those who shave, until they are extended and matched. If they prick him at its root: then bind his eyes with a plaster, so that they do not move until it grows out.
When they grow out and are matched, then place the head of the patient in your lap: afterwards mark on the eyelids of his eyes with wax, marking that it is in the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a wetted dish on sheep's wool or on flaxseed mucilage over the eye.
Then heat the cautery, whose shape is this.
Then burn the cautery gradually on multiple places until the surface of the skin, which is like a myrtle leaf shape, appears entirely.
And the mark of your health is that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting and the hairs growing up at the prick of the eye.
Lift up your hand then: and let it go for three days.
Then place a dish with butter on it until the eschar is removed. Afterward care for him with an ointment until he is healed.
If any hair returns after an hour and the eyelid softens: then repeat the cautery on that place as you did at first.
If there are hairs below it: then burn it until the hair grows out to its natural place and matches so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is to be ordered for the sick one that he lets grow and trims his hair until they extend and match. Make from cloth of linen a shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take some known soap and undyed chalk from one or the other pound weight, about that much; then grind them together well with good grinding, and make it quickly, so as not to cool it. Then from this compound spread it on the cloth that you have made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it upon the eyelid of one eye or both. And place under the eye a cup filled with yolk of egg, and let the head of the sick person be in your lap.
And place your index finger upon the medicine and press it slightly. And you move it as often as the sick person feels a bite of the medicine; because its bite is like fire.
While it thus continues to bite as the sick person feels, then release the medicine and move it with your finger. When the bite ceases, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
Then observe if the eyelid rises as it rises under contraction with fire or incision, this is good; and if not, then repeat over the same place from the medicine where the medicine does not press, and does not darken, until your operation is equal and the eye contracts.
Then place it upon the cup with butter, until the skin of the burn is removed. Then treat him with an ointment like diaphine or another one, until he is cured.
And it is necessary for you at the operation that you keep the last guard, lest something from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid becomes softened after days and something fights from hairs within the eye, then repeat the medicine on that place which has become softened from the eyelid, as you did first. Then treat it until it is healed.
And this is the form of myrtle leaf.
And know that human eyes vary in size and shape. Therefore according to this your consideration should be: and the path of rightness for him who is devoted to this art should not be hidden.
[Chapter Title] On the method of cauterization in lacrimal fistula.
When you treat the fistula, if your treatment does not improve as we have said in the divisions of diseases, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Command the sick man to place his head in your lap, and have one of his attendants hold his head thus, so that it is not moved or shaken with his head.
Then place the cotton soaked in alcohol or psyllium mucilage over his eye: then take the hot iron cautery, whose form is this.
It should be concave, like the shape of a goose feather quill from one end, with which the cautery is made: and if you wish it to penetrate to the other end, and if you wish it to be extended upwards in this way.
However, this concave form is better for your work.
Then squeeze the fistula if it is open and extract the pus from it, and excise it: and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then place the hot cautery on it.
And hold your hand near the cautery for a short time close to the eye, near the nose, so that your hand does not wander or the sick person is disturbed: and place the cautery on the fat of the eye and break it.
If therefore you reach at the beginning of your cautery until the bone, it will be well. And if not: then repeat the cautery once, or twice if necessary; and leave it for three days.
Then place a piece of wool with butter, and care for it with an ointment made from dry resins, until it heals.
If it exceeds forty days and does not heal: then apply a sharp corrosive medicine on it until the bone is exposed; and shave it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cautery for a fistula, which some of the first ones said. Direct yourself to the place of the fistula, and cut it; then put a fine camel's-hair probe into the fissure, that is, a fine probe, whose shape this is. Pour into it a quantity of lead melted as a drachma, and hold your hand with good retention on the probe, and let it not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run or reach the eye.
It is necessary that you place a warm woolen cloth over the weak eye or in water.
For lead burns the place of the fistula and heals it with marvelous healing.
If the fistula heals as we said by cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to open the nose passage and redirect the fistula to the nasal passages, according to what comes in its proper place.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in lips' cracks.
Multiple splits occur in the Lip, which are called Pilae, and particularly in the lips of boys.
When you take care of these splits, as I said earlier for the division of diseases, and the treatment does not help, then use a small cautery, shaped like this.
And let its hollow be shaped according to the subtlety of a knife.
Then place it (the cautery) quickly into those splits until the cautery reaches the depth of the splits.
Then care for it with pitch until it heals.
Method of Cauterizing a Mouth Split.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or at the roots of teeth: then pus forms and bursts; later it becomes old and the pus runs and it becomes a split; then care for it and treatment does not help in this case, then one must use fire cauterization according to the size that can fit into the split. Then insert the fire into the hole of the split and hold your hand until the iron becomes hot to its depth and end; do this once or twice.
Then care for it after that, as I said earlier about treatment, until it is cured.
If the pus separates and heals, it will be good. And if it does not, then it is necessary to expose the place, and remove the corrupt bone according to what comes in its head.
Method of Cauterizing in Softened Gums and Teeth.
When the gum becomes soft due to moisture and the teeth move, and care for it with medicine but it does not help; then put the head of the sick person on your chest.
Then place the cautery, whose shape will come later, on the tooth; and introduce in it the heated cauterium hastily; and hold your hand for a while, until the weak feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And move your hand (away); then repeat the cautery several times, as you wish.
Then let the weak fill his mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour; and spit it out.
For the tooth moved strengthens (itself), and the gums, softened, are tightened, and moisture is dried out.
[Title: Method of Cauterizing Tooth Pain]
When the tooth pain is due to coldness, or there is coldness in itself, or worms, and the treatment with medicines does not help; then the cautery should be used on it according to two methods: either with butter [and charcoal] or with fire.
The cautery with butter is such that you receive freshly churned butter, and boil it in an iron cauldron or a copper one. Then take a linen cloth and fold it over the tip of the wound. Then immerse it in melted butter and place it quickly on the painful tooth and hold it until it becomes cold; then repeat this several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or cloth in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth; then put iron heated red-hot over it until the heat of the fire reaches to the hollow of the tooth.
However, cauterization with fire is to be done using a pipe made of brass or iron. And let there be some swelling in the body so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the weak bone.
Then take a hot firebrand of the shape that will come; and place it on that tooth and hold your hand until the firebrand becomes cold.
Repeat this often for the pain to be removed, either on the same day or another day.
And when applying the impression of the cautery, the weak bone should be filled with good butter and held for an hour; then spit it out.
And this is the shape of the firebrand.
Use any end of the cautery as possible; and this is the form of the pipe.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing bladder stones.
When Worms are with phlegm, and from cold moistures, and not obedient to digestion by medicines, and desire digestion quickly: then, to the concave Cautery, whose shape is this.
Having two open ends so that the smoke leaves the cautery from one end: and place it heated upon the ulcer once, and again, if needed, until it reaches the depth of the ulcer.
If the ulcer is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the ulcer.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a cup filled with butter, until what the fire burned is removed.
Then care for it with tooth ointment, until the form of the cannula heals.
[Paragraph about the method of cauterization in throat swelling and constriction of breathing.]
When moistures press upon the windpipe, and especially when it is with coldness of complexion: then a sick person must be evacuated first with loose medicines.
Then cauterize it at the root of the throat in a hollow place depressed: and beware not to come with the cautery to the throat, nor on the skin, unless something of its substance.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the joint of the neck at the end of the last rib of that side: and let the cautery be a nail in accordance with the method which was previously mentioned.
Then care for it with what has been previously mentioned, until it is healed.
[Paragraph about the method of cauterization in diseases of the lungs and cough.]
When cough and disease of the lungs are from cold moistures, and a sick person does not have a fever, nor consumption, and the disease is old: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the clavicle at hollow, easy, vacant places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between two breasts: and let the cautery be in the shape of a tube as described before.
And if your cauterization is by pricking with a cautery named Punctum, whose shape was described before in the piercing of ear pain; let these punctures be thirty or more.
Then care for it as was described before, until it heals.
And let the cautery have three branches; according to this shape. Therefore, when you use a cautery in its place instead of three cauteries.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the arm is dislocated due to assistance and it does not recover within an hour after its displacement, until this becomes a habit for it, then it should be dislocated slightly, as described previously, then you must reduce the dislocation first. Then the sick person lies on his back on his own back or on the healthy side. Then scrape the skin that is inside Titillico towards the upper part with your left hand fingers; and if it is dislocated towards the internal parts.
Then take a cautery with two holes. Its shape is as follows.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the shape of the cauterization will be as described with four cauteries.
And sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery having three holes, therefore the shape of the cauterization becomes that of six cauteries; and there are holes according to the fineness of the attempt.
And this is the shape of the cautery with three holes.
And sometimes one more is added to this method, therefore there are eight cauteries.
Then place a hot iron (cautery) over squeezed leeks with salt. Then make the sick person quiet and still so that a limb is not moved at any time until it is healed.
If the dislocation is towards the upper part (shoulder), which rarely happens, then cauterize it with a hook-shaped iron or several needles puncturing.
For joining strengthens and removes moisture, and the sick person is healed.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and much moisture appear in the stomach until it is removed from its composition, and catarrhs multiply towards it, and persistent methods of treatment do not help; then the sick person should lie on his back, extend his legs, and stretch out his arms. Then cauterize with three irons: one hook-shaped iron of the size of a finger under the concavity of the chest and another hook-shaped iron, and two smaller irons below the sides of the single iron, until the figure of the cautery is triangular. And stretch it apart so that they do not join together when pus appears.
The depth of the cautery should be equal to two thirds the thickness of the skin.
The figure of the cautery should be in this shape without any additions; and if you wish to cauterize with a large iron in the center of the stomach in this shape, then let the iron that forms this cautery be one circular in shape according to this form.
The stomach is cauterized by pressing it with the cautery and making marks on it according to the desired size with encaustic; then cauterize it with the iron of that point; then care for it with the treatment that preceded until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing an earlobe with cold cautery.
When there is pain in the shoulder from cold and dampness, or from a thick wind that has not been expelled by its natural discharge, and the sick person cannot recover with what was said earlier: then the sick person should lie on his neck and mark three places on his earlobe with hot cautery according to this shape, and the same amount below the hips, where a man's elbow reaches: and let the space between each cautery be as wide as a finger's width: and let the cautery be as long as the body straight: and do not press your hand tightly with the cautery.
And let the amount that is burned be according to the thickness of the skin, half its width not added: and let the sick person stand on his feet.
If he is not standing, then he should be lying down, who has already stretched out his legs and raised his arms.
This is the shape of the cautery.
And it is possible for you to use these cauteries with a small cautery when skill and wisdom are with you in the art.
Be careful that you do not burn the entire thickness of the skin in cauterization, for the body is burned in its entirety, and it reaches the intestines: because the skin there is thin, know this.
On the method of cauterizing abscesses in the shoulder.
When it comes out and you want to know if the abscess is in the shoulder muscle or its sheath: then if it is in the shoulder muscle, pain and heaviness without sharpness appear: and if it is in the shoulder sheath, with pain there is strong sharpness: and you see that the treatment of this has exhausted the doctors.
The sick person should lie with his head on his chest. Then the place of the boil must be shaped like a caustic (with) encaustic: then heat the cautery that resembles a rod. And this is its shape. And cauterize (it) with one cautery until the whole skin is burned and reaches the subcutaneous tissue, until all pus comes out: then care for it by treating it with ointments until it heals.
And one should not use this cauterizing method unless his devotion to the art of medicine has been prolonged; and whose hands these diseases often accompany along with experience: then he may dare to perform such an operation.
But it is better for me to let it be (as it is).
Chapter on the method of cauterization for pleurisy.
The ancients said, cautery with roots of Aristolochia for a cold pleurisy, according to this method. And it is, to receive from the dried roots of Aristolochia, one longer root, which can be found among them, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil, and set it alight in fire. Then cauterize with one hot iron on that which is between the union of the collar-bone and the neck, and with two small irons near the area under the chin.
And with two more irons on that which is between the fifth and sixth ribs, slightly towards the back, and with another iron in the middle of the chest, and one above the stomach. And with three more irons from behind: one on that which is between the two scapulae; and with two more irons from the sides of the chest, with the lower iron being between the two scapulae.
And it is not necessary that you press your hand with the iron, rather let it be clearly smell of skin.
And certain ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery made of iron similar to a ray, and they burn it and insert it into that which is between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess, and pus comes out: as we said in the case of an abscess in the liver.
But in this perforation with the iron there is a fear, that either the sick person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, which has no healing.
Chapter 32: On the method of cauterizing the spleen.
When you treat the sickness of the spleen, as we said in the treatment of diseases, and your remedy does not work, then there is a need for cautery in it according to three methods, which are all correct.
One of them is to make three or four cauteries, extending along the length of the spleen according to the shape of the cauteries of the liver, whose previous figure it follows.
And let each cautery be of the thickness of a finger or more or less.
Let the mode of cauterizing, as I have said in the cauterization of the liver, be equally distributed.
And do not press your hand with the cautery; let it be weak and lying on its back on its own back.
Another method of cauterizing is: holding the cautery with two prongs, as we have said in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder; and scrape off the skin which is directly on the spleen where the arm of the weak person reaches; and let your scrapping be according to the width of the body so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert two prongs very hot until they penetrate the skin on the other side; then withdraw the cautery; thus there will be four cauteries.
And if you want to cauterize with a cautery having three prongs.
Then take care of the cautery after you release it to emit pus for many days; for this is more beneficial than the rest which have come before in treatment.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in hydropsy (edema).
A cautery does not fall in hydropsy unless it is specifically the head.
When you are treating hydropsy with the methods of treatment that we have mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary to cauterize the person with four cauteries around the navel, and one over the stomach, and another over the liver, and another over the spleen, and two behind the back between the vertebrae, and one on the front of the chest, and another on the front of the stomach; and let the depth of the cautery be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then let the open cautery emit pus for a long time.
Do not evacuate the sick after cauterization with it: this must be done so that two intentions are applied to him, and healing will hasten towards it with God's help.
The form of the cautery used to cauterize the abdomen should be clavilis, as has been described before; and the one used for cauterizing the back should be olive-shaped, as has been described before.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing feet and legs.
When amputated in hydropicus and filled with citrine water: it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot at the navicular bone, which is between the auricular and annular; then lift your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it; then lift your hand again, and do not touch it at all.
The citrine water will evaporate, and let the cautery be in this shape.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be of the form of a short knife at its end; let the cautery on the thigh be long, one below the knee, and the other lower than that, about halfway down the leg; and over the whole hip make two cauterizations; let the cautery remain open without treatment for a long time to allow some water to evaporate, then cure it as we have said.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in the resolution of the abdomen.
Chapter 35.
When the abdominal solution is due to cold and moisture, until it weakens the powers of retention and digestion in the stomach and intestines; when this is cured according to the methods of treatment but does not heal; if you see a sick person tolerating an excessive cautery, then cauterize the abdomen with a large cautery on the stomach, as has been described before for cauterizing the stomach with a circular cautery and four subtle cauteries around the umbilicus with a fine clavile cautery; and with a large cautery or two cauteries over the alcatin above the hips.
If you see excessive moisture and a weak patient enduring it, then cauterize him with the cautery on the forehead and on all of his buttocks; and perhaps add two small cauteries near the stomach.
The treatment is progressing successfully, whose benefit does not stray.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter 36.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, either one and they are composed of thick, cold or corrupted fluids, and have been treated as described in the division, but the cure does not improve: then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower part of the buttocks slightly below the almoidate triangularly, and with a cautery under the navel about two fingers.
And if you consider that his stomach is chilled and his food is not digested, and you see his face pallor, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery as described earlier; and cauterize on his liver and another on his spleen along with a cautery in the loins: and leave the open cautery for some time; then care for him until he is cured.
Chapter 37.
When you remove althelul, then heat the cautery similar to a rod. Then introduce the heated cautery into the removed althelul; and hold your hand last until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which the blood flows: do this once or twice.
If there are many althelul, then cauterize each one with a cautery as described earlier. Then care for them with the aid of the ointment that is suitable for them until they are cured.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery upon oil, it is more final in its benefit.
On the method of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter XXXVIII.
When the weak [patient] does not obey cutting and surgery as we have described earlier, and fears it, perhaps he can heal with cautery.
When a fistula occurs and becomes old, pus flows from it, and corrupt humors. Therefore, as is fitting, one should examine it with a thin probe. Then determine the depth of its size with a probe.
Then heat the cautery, which resembles a rod.\] Si autem humectatum sit, calefac, donec sint in eo If it is wet, heat the cautery, until [the cautery] is hot.\] Then insert yourself, heated, into the fistula and measure the depth up to which the claw has entered.
And repeat the cautery on it until all the corrupted bodies are burned, once, twice, or three times, according to your need.
And beware of burning the nerve or major vein if it is present; or if the fistula goes to the bladder or the intestine, then beware of these places altogether.
Do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy place; and remember that it does not penetrate.
Then take care of the place until it heals.
If the place is sealed and the matter is cut away from it and remains for a long time, then you will know that it has healed completely.
If the matter is not cut away from it, then you will know that it is penetrating, or that there is rotten bone deep within it, or like that of those [other cases] whose memory will come back to its place.
On the method of cauterizing the kidney.
In what cases and for what reasons should a clyster be applied? When there is pain in the kidneys due to cold or because of thick effusion, and it decreases due to illness of the body, then you must cauterize it on a coal-bed over the kidneys, with a cautery over the entire kidney along with the cautery hook, whose preceding explanation has been mentioned earlier.
And perhaps we should cauterize it again at the second time on the same coal-bed. Why do three lines appear? Therefore, they will be more beneficial in the end.
On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
In what cases and for what reasons should a clyster be applied in the bladder? When there is weakness or softening of the bladder due to cold and moistness, and it does not retain urine, then you must cauterize it on the lower part of the back near the bladder, where the hair of the beard begins, and with a cautery from the right side of the back, and another from the left; and let the length of the cauterization be according to the size of the knuckle of the little finger; and you must cauterize it with a cautery on the lower part of the back or with two cauteries if necessary, as was previously explained with the cautery hook.
On the method of cauterizing the uterus.
In what cases and for what reasons should a clyster be applied to the uterus? When there is coldness and moisture in the womb, which prevents conception, and its menstruation is corrupted and their provocations are delayed, and pain occurs near their arrival, then you must cauterize it with three cauteries around the navel as was said for the bladder, and with a cautery below on the lower part of the back or with two cauteries; and use the cautery hook.
On the method of cauterizing an ankle in dislocation.
If the tibia is broken and the ankle joint has been dislocated, when mucosal fluids flow towards the plaster on the ankle, and this causes it to come out of its place: and a sign of this is that the leg extends beyond the other side when they are compared with each other: and the location of the dislocation is found to be empty in this case.
Therefore it is necessary to burn the weak spot on the plaster of the ankle with a similar cautery in the shape of a circle: after you mark with pitch around the plaster, as described above: and let the plaster fall into the center of the circle.
If this cautery is not present to you, then burn the same spot with three cauteries, using a deep cautery made of oil and with a depth according to the thickness of the entire skin.
Then take care of it until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
If sciatica is in the hip joint, and when a pain occurs on the ankle plaster and the cause of this is cold and fluids: and it is treated according to what has been said above for dislocation, but treatment does not help, and the condition worsens: then it is necessary to dissolve the weak spot with foul pills or artificial pills and similar ones. Then burn the same spot.
The method of cauterization is as follows, in two ways: either with a cautery with medicines accompanying it or with fire.
The cautery with fire is according to many methods.
One [of these] is to cauterize upon the bladder stone with three triangular cauteries according to this shape. Make a good or bad depth for them. Let the space be between each cautery of the size of a finger; and let the cautery be anointed with oil.
Sometimes, however, the cautery is made in the middle of the bladder stone itself. Why are there four cauteries?
If you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded the cauterization of the bladder stone displacement, one: so that the circle contains the whole bladder stone.
Burn the thickness of the skin all over.
This is the method of cautery for sciatica, when pain is attached to the bladder itself, and does not extend to the hip and leg.
But if it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize the same on the hip with two cauteries at the place where the sick person indicates, where there is pain; and cauterize your knife four fingers deep into the outer part: let the cautery be a small knife.
Let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the sick person indicates that pain extends almost to the toes, then cauterize it there where he indicates with a pointed cautery, three, or four, or more if necessary.
If he indicates that pain is turned towards the leg below the knee, then cauterize it there with a small knife cautery.
Take care of yourself in all your cauteries, so as not to burn the nerve or large artery, and attract harm or contraction through it onto the sick person.
And I myself have seen one and another of those who cauterized on the shin, and burned too much in their cautery, and the leg swelled until it reached the foot, and was pierced through, and the entire foot rotted; then there follows loosening of the abdomen, and death after that.
If pain is in two parts simultaneously, cauterize each one according to this method.
Some wise men have said in cauterization of anus (a rectum), this is the method of cauterizing it. Make a similar iron tool (cautery) whose diameter is half of a palm; and it should be at the orifice according to its size, equal to the circumference of a finger's knuckle, or slightly less; and within that iron tool, there should be another smaller iron tool.
And let the space between all iron tools be equal to the size of the knuckle of a thumb; and let these iron tools be open at two sides; and their height should be equal to or slightly more than a knuckle, or two knuckles; and make a handle from iron suitable for holding in these iron tools.
Then it is heated in fire until it glows and sparks; then it is placed on the pillow of the anus (a rectum), leaning weakly on a healthy side. Therefore, cauterize him with three rounded iron tools at once.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards, apply ointment with butter; and let the open wound remain for many days. Then care for him with an ointment until he is healed.
Says Albucasis, with this shape of the cautery, we have used it insufficiently because of its terrifying appearance; and therefore, because few are found who dare to use it.
Nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries for him who endures it, and it finds its place with him.
But cautery with drugs is to be made by you into two iron tools having a perforated strap, on which descends the key of its door from brass or iron, whose length is equal to the height of the walls; and in their height, there should be two knuckles, or as if they themselves.
And let the space be that which is between each quantity of finger thickness, and let it be open below and above; and let it contain one another, according to this form.
Then place it on the boxwood plank, with the weak side lying on the healthy side. And press your hand upon the boxwood plank hard. Then pour between two circles of warm water, which has been slightly heated by fire, and hold it for the length of an hour; let the weak one endure its bite and its burning, for he finds the bite as a fire does, until the biting stops.
Then clean your hand with the instrument, and wash the whole boxwood plank with warm water and sweet water; then let it be for three days.
And place butter on it until the soot of burning is removed; and let it be for some days, and pus will flow out from it. For it is the final remedy.
Then treat it with ointments, until it heals.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg, make a splint for him in which there is water, as you made for the boxwood plank equally.
And this is the method of hot water; and I have already written about it in the tract on the correction of medicines. Take lime and unburnt chalk of equal parts; grind each of them well, and put them into a new pot whose lower part is perforated with a small hole, according to the quantity that enters the radius; and place another earthenware pot below it; and pour over the lime and chalk from sweet water, so that both are submerged by one finger; then press them with your hand firmly; and let the pot be until the acid water descends in the lower part of the earthenware pot.
Then gather all that water and throw it over another limb; and let it coagulate until it returns.
For indeed, it will then be very strong and sharp, which is administered in many operations of medicine, and also in the cauterization of other members. Because it performs the operation of fire itself.
And among the medications are those with which the ulcers are cauterized, also like teesie, and honey of cardamom, and chalk with soap, so that both are mixed together. Â¶
And Galen indeed reported the cure of a certain man from ancient times, who was cured of the pain of an ulcer and sciatic vein; and he highly praised its effect. And he said that no other treatment was necessary for him, and that he was cured from the disease in one day until he reported that perhaps he himself had gone into a bath, and came out of it already well.
It is to be taken from the green seitaragi; and if it is not found, dry one should be taken, fresh: and grind a great deal with some fat, and place it over the ulcer, where there is pain, or leg, or hip: and bind it, and leave for a quantity of three hours, or until the weak feel the sensation of burning. Then introduce it into the bath.
When his body becomes hot, introduce him onto a bed. For the pain disappears and is cured.
And know that it is not necessary for anyone to use cautery with these medications, unless after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides himself said that the droppings of goats, when it is cauterized with the sciatic vein, give to it; and it becomes a cautery in this way. Take flax, and immerse it in old oil, and place it on a deep place which is between the big toe of the foot and the ball of the foot, and is closer to the ball of the foot.
Then take dry goat's dung, and heat it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the flax, and let it burn out. Then repeat this process. Therefore do not stop doing this until sensation reaches the edge through it and the pain ceases.
And this method of cauterization is called cautery of the cow hoof.
Section on the Cauterization of Back Pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back due to various causes such as accidents, blows, excessive evacuation and similar conditions caused by the injection of cold and wet matter; and cauterization does not apply except in this one case which is done through the injection of cold and wet matter.
Therefore after the evacuation of the sick with foul pills and similar substances, three lines should be drawn on the back where there is pain, according to the width of a palm leaf, after marking them with encaustic in each line five times or more according to the amount that comes from the tolerance of the sick person; and cauterization should be done with cautery points.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries along with the medial nail cautery, in this manner.
Section on the method of cauterization for hump-shaped growths.
This illness often occurs in small children.
The sign of this hump-shaped growth in children is that it occurs on the child when a stridor occurs during elevation and movement; and you will find at the end of the spine of the back and the nodes of it, which has already begun to protrude above the other spines.
When therefore you see that thing and wish to do it, then cauterize it with a cautionery which is in the shape of a circle.
And let the cautionery catch over all the mussel-shell equally; and if you wish to cauterize around the mussel-shell with a pointed cautionery, let there be two or three points, and they should be close to one another.
Then take care of the place until it heals as we have said.
And beware, do not administer the cautionery on a swelling which is caused by a muscle spasm.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for gout and for joint pains.
When the joint pains are caused by cold moistness that spreads to any part of the body, then when they occur in the feet, it is customary among doctors to call it gout properly.
When the treatment for cold-caused gout has been used without relief of pain, then the cautionery removes them.
And it is that you should cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the foot with many cautioneries; and let the cautionery be Olivary.
And if you need to make points on the sole of the foot, then do it with a pointed cautionery. If the pain ascends to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize it over all the knee with three or four cautioneries from all sides, with the same clavicular cautionery.
If you need more of this cautionery, then cauterize it. And do not immerse your hand with the cautionery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin.
If the pain ascends to the knees and back, then administer what was said in its chapter.
If the pains are only in the hands, then make punctures around the joints of the fingers, as two lines are rolled up.
If pain persists in the fingers, then make punctures over every nodule and on the back of the hand.
If the pain rises after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both from all sides.
And do not evacuate a sick person through good regimen and administration of medicine. For if the diet is good, and phlegm is evacuated, it will be cured with this cautery by the help of God.
Chapter on the mode of cauterizing in ruptures.
When rupture occurs in the groins and the intestine or zirbu (a term for a diseased testicle) descends towards the testis, and it begins to be near: then it is necessary that you order the sick man to abstain from food on his own day. And he should use laxatives so that stool passes from his bowels.
Then let him sit on your hands upon his back: and command him to hold his breath until it comes out, or the hernia appears, or the intestine.
Then reduce him with your fingers, and make a mark with hot iron under the hernia on his neck, with the mark whose end is similar to half of a circle above the body.
Then heat the cautery of this shape until it turns white and throw sparks. Then reduce the hernia or the intestine to its hollow. Then let the assistant place his hand on the spot to prevent the intestine from coming out: and you have already opened between the legs of the sick person, and placed a stone under him, and another servant is serving over his thighs, and another over his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery upon the mark, with your hand holding the cautery straight. And hold him until you reach the bone with it: or do it again with another blow, if you have not reached the bone with it in the first instance.
And be careful to observe the exit of the intestine during your cautery, lest you burn him and bring harm upon him or great evil.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, the operation is not effective.
And it must be that the cautery of children should be subtle, according to their measure.
Then care for him with ointments until he is well again.
And let the sick person lie on his back for forty days until the wound is healed.
And it must be that you place his food in length according to the time of his treatment, so that it softens his stomach; so that no hernia may come out during attempts and evacuations.
Then when he wishes to rise after forty days, then administer a belt made properly, and let him hold it for another forty days.
And let it (the wound) be diminished by work, and filled with food and drink, and with strong voices.
When this regimen is used, the cure is complete healing.
And I shall say the cure for ruptures with incision in its own chapter.
If ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen and they are starting and do not want to heal, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and that which is cauterized should be like the third part of it from that time on. Then take care of it as I said: do not increase (the incision).
And some have said that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery according to this shape.
After it is signed with wax, and a line is placed that goes across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery claw.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for pain due to injury or blow.
Chapter LVIII.
If pain occurs in certain members due to injury or blow, and the pain persists for a long time and does not help with medication, then it should be cauterized with a puncture cautery.
And the puncture cautery should be of the size and part of the member, its weakness, its strength, its location of twisting, and the pain from it.
If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good. If not: then repeat the cautery over it.
Because it is customary for these pains to change from one member to another that is nearby. Therefore, it is necessary that you follow them with a cautery until the sick one is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in leprosy.
Leprosy is sometimes helped by a great cautioning. And particularly the type of leprosy that occurs due to putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: when considering burning it itself.
If leprosy is beginning and you have treated it with what was said in the division, but it does not subside nor stay: fear for the weak one, lest corruption spread over his entire complexion; then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head known, and second lower toward the forehead at the end of hairline, and two above the horns, and one behind on the back of the neck.
And finally put your hand with the cautery a little bit, until it makes an impression on the bone smaller, and the cortexes come off from it; so that the expiration of gross vapors from it is relieved, and cauterize also with the cautery on the spleen according to what preceded.
If leprosy has already spread over the weak one and is apparent: then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries which were said in the head, and with a cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on the cheeks, and two cauteries on the hips of the neck, and six on the hips of the back, and one large one on alhahosos near the tail and one above it, in the almeidat; and two over the ankles: namely over the whole ankle with one, and two over knees, and two over shoulders, and two over elbows, and two over the tendons of the chest; and cauterize on all the joints of his fingers of his hands and feet, and on all the heels of his feet, and on the soles of his hands.
Be careful to spare the nerves that are on top of the last heel bone, so as not to burn them.
And sometimes it is burned with a cautery upon the cheek bone, and upon another upon the forehead, and upon another upon the nose.
Know that the more you add to the cautery, the greater is the help and the better it is.
Know that an ill person does not find pain in the cautery, as a healthy person does: for this reason, because his body is already numb.
It must be that the cauteries are of suitable size and shape according to the limbs and joints: in accordance with which they were preceded by types of iron tools.
Then treat the burn with flour of herbs and honey, and the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter on Cauterization in Fainting.
When some part faints and is treated with medicines, oils, plasters, and does not heal, then cauterize the numbed part with cauteries, according to the size or smallness of the member.
And let your cautery penetrate only a little into the thickness of the skin. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes it is burned for some fainting that happens to the hand and foot, at the joints of the back near the exit of nerves that move that member, and the fainting disappears.
But do not presume to apply it there unless he who is wise in the anatomy of the limbs and the exits of nerves moving the body knows.
Chapter LI.
When the ulcer becomes old and nothing of medicine helps in it: then cauterize over it with a deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the white disappears and its color changes.
Then take care of it with the flour of herbs, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and blood of a dove, and blood of a crane: each should be one part: mix all these together, and apply on cloth, and let it adhere to the place until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in Cancer.
When Cancer is beginning, and you want to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, as is rotated.
But the wise have said, that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
To me, however, it does not seem so: because I fear that it may burn, and I have already seen that many times.
And it is correct, that it should be cauterized around it with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
On the method of cauterizing in Adubelati.
When someone has Adubelati, and it slows down in maturation, either because of an excess causing it or because of age and weakness, or when there are few blood vessels remaining, or because time is needed and you want to hurry the maturation of Adubelati: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking. Then let it rest. For itself will hasten when it has matured.
If you want to pierce it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, whose form is this: (Here follows a description of the shape of the cautery)
Place it in the middle of Adubelati; let it penetrate the skin; and let the cautery be weakened from that which follows, so that the course of the pus may be relieved.
Then care for it until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in a cancerous case.
Chapter LIV.
A cancer is not anything but corruption walking in a member and consuming it, like fire consumes dry wood.
If you see a cancer in a place that can bear the cautery with fire, then use much cauterization, small and large nails according to what suits the place where the cancer is.
Then cauterize it from every part until you have eradicated the entire corruption and there remains nothing of it beneath.
Then leave it for three days and place over the cauterized areas sulphur pulverized with oil until all scabs and all corruption are eradicated.
Then care for it with unguents that generate flesh.
If you see that after three days flesh is born by healthy generation in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places.
A cancer is sometimes treated with an acute medication. It arises in the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is more swift in its help; and I have already said that the cauterization of it with an acute medication is in division (surgery); so take it whenever you need it there.
On the method of cauterizing in nails and verrucas (warts).
Chapter V.
This illness often occurs in the lower parts of the feet; it is a swelling, filled with matter, which injures the foot.
The cautery is indeed in them according to two modes: the cautery with fire, and the cautery with hot water.
As for the one with fire, it should be shaped like a hollowed-out raven's feather; made of iron according to its size, which contains a nail from all sides; and it should have fine edges.
Then place the heated one on the nail. Then turn the hand with the cautery around the nail, until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail; and leave it for three days, until it begins to emit pus. Then apply salve made of wild herbs crushed with salt; and leave the salve on it at night. It will be uprooted from its roots.
Then treat the place with a fine ointment for the skin until it heals.
If they are not cured and keep recurring on the body surface, especially in hands and feet; then administer cautery with hot water. It is to be noted that you will take a cannula made of brass or iron or raven's feather; and place it on the nail or althea root. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the cannula; hold your hand and turn it with a slight pressure, so that the tip of the cannula is pressed against the root of the nail, and let the hot water find its way to the depth, to the root of the nail; and wait for an hour for the weak patient under the burning sensation of hot water.
Then release it, as the nail will be uprooted along with its roots.
Do this to them one after another until you have treated all who are affected by them on the body.
Then treat them after they are uprooted, with a fine ointment for the skin.
Method of Cauterizing in a Shaking Manner.
When the bones are broken and perforated:
The tremor ceases with cautery oiling, and hastens the health's recovery from cold disease.
On the method of cauterization, Albatheer.
Chapter LVII.
Sometimes, Albathir expels foul things from the body, that is, pustules which are caused by corrupted matters.
Therefore, it is necessary first, when they appear, to cauterize on every pustule head with a subtle cautery together with myrtle wood, whose tip is set alight with fire. Or with the root of long aristolochia. Or with a lenticular cautery.
And sometimes they are cauterized, at the beginning of their expulsion, according to this method: and they do not increase: and the surplus is broken, making them, and it heals from them.
However, it must be done afterwards with phlebotomy.
On the method of cauterizing in bleeding from an artery at a wound.
Often it happens that blood flows from an artery which is cut near a wound, which occurs externally, or at the incision of a boil, or of cautery on a limb, and similar things: and it is difficult to separate him.
When this happens to someone, then hurry with your hand to the artery's orifice, and place your forefinger on it: and press him strongly, until the blood is held under your finger, and nothing escapes from it.=*/ When such a thing happens to someone, then quickly go with your hand to the orifice of the artery, and place your index finger upon it; and press it very hard, until the blood is held under your finger, and nothing comes out of it.
