Then place a small oil-filled cautery on fire, and many large ones with numerous ones: and blow on them until they are very hot.=*/ Place a small oil-filled cautery on fire, and many large ones with numerous ones; and blow on them until they become very hot.
Then take one of them (the heated irons), either small or large, according to the wound and the place where the broken artery is, and place the cautery on that vein; afterwards remove your finger quickly: and hold the cautery until the blood is severed.
If it is expelled along with withdrawing the finger from the artery's opening and extinguishing the cautery, then take another cautery quickly, from those which are prepared in the fire.
Therefore, do not stop doing that with one after another until the blood is severed.
And beware, lest you burn the nerve that is there, and other evil happens to the already weakened person.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, then it is not possible to sever it; particularly since the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or with a cautery, as we have said. Or by extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it is drawn out, the ends contract and the blood is severed. Or it will be tied with a strong thread. Or medicine from the property for severing blood is placed upon it and it is tightened with a decent ligature press.
But he who performs the severance with a ligament and a tightening with fabric or with substances that burn and similar, does not fully help him unless rarely.
If that happens to someone and he is not present with the doctor or medicine, then begin by placing the index finger over the opening of the vein as we have said, and constrict it very tightly, until the blood is obstructed from above the wound and on the artery. And the finger is not to be removed from above it with cold water of intense cold until the blood clots and thickens and is severed.
And meanwhile, consider in him what requires cautery or medicine.
On incision, perforation, and phlebotomy in wounds and similar cases.

And before I begin that, you must know, my sons, what is found in this chapter from the terror of that which was in the first chapter about cautery.
And therefore it is necessary for there to be greater caution because, in the operation that is in this chapter, evacuation often falls out with blood, with which life stands during opening of a vein, or incision over an abscess, or opening of an exit wound, or treatment of a wound, or extraction of an arrow, or incision over a stone, and similar things: from all of which tremor, fear, and death occur in many.
And I warn you that this should not happen to you, for at times people of this art fall into these conditions with the weaknesses of men. For there is one who becomes angry with his illness and is light as far as death is concerned: because of the vehemence that comes from his weakness and the length of his wickedness. And when illness is due to fear, it signifies death.
And there is one who gives you false hope and deceives you with it, hoping for health, but the illness of this one is deadly.
Therefore, it is not appropriate that you agree to him who comes to you from those whose manner is such. Let your caution be more intense than your greed and avarice. And do not presume about anything from that, unless after certain knowledge, which is verified among you as to the matter that has reached a praiseworthy outcome.
And use in the treatment of all your sick, prediction and direction concerning that to which it is appropriately healthful.
For there is assistance for you in the matter of acquiring reputation and glory, memory and praise.
May God inspire you, O son, His understanding, and not deprive you of guidance and inspiration, for that is in His hand.

Chapter on Treatment of Water that is Collected in the Heads of Children.
Chapter I.
Know that this affliction often occurs in boys during childbirth: either when the midwife tightens the boy's head without ease.
And it sometimes occurs also for hidden reasons that are not known.
And I myself have not seen this affliction in others than in boys: and to every one of them whom I have seen, death has followed: for that reason, it seemed to me that I should refrain from the operation on it.
And I myself have seen a boy whose head was filled with water, and his head swelled up every day until he could not sit on himself due to the size of his head; and the moisture increased until he died.
And this moisture, it may accumulate between the skin and the bone: or it may accumulate under the bone above the forehead.
And the operation on him, if there is moisture between the skin and the bone, and the abscess is small, then it is necessary to make a single fracture in the middle of the head along its width: and the length of the crack should be like two knuckles, until the moisture runs out.
And this is the form of the trepan.
If then the moisture is more increased, and the abscess is larger, then place these two cracks according to this form.
And if the moisture is under the bone, and the sign of this is that you see openings of the skull all around; and water comes out when you press it with your hand from within, and it does not hide itself from you: then it is necessary to make three cracks in the middle of the head according to this method.
And after the incision, remove all the moisture. Then bind the cracks with cloths and wool. Then anoint it above with wine and oil until the fifth day.
Then cut (the) ligament, and care for the wound with sutures and ointments.
And do not release the head without equality. Feed the weak with dry food of little moisture, until (the) limb is strengthened and healed.
Another method of incision is to consider where the abscess appears large and the collection of water (for) irrigation.
Because sometimes it is more in the head or skull, or right, or left.
Therefore ascend with incision where the abscess and filling of water appear to you, and cut it as possible for you.
And observe, do not cut an artery, and let the flow of blood occur and the weak one dies from this flow with evacuation of moisture.
Chapter on incisions of the arteries that are after the ears.
Chapter II.
When catarrhs occur to someone's eyes or chest, and it does not improve with medical treatment, then the final cure is in this, incision of these two arteries.
Therefore when you wish to cut them (the arteries), let the sick one shave his own head. Then rub the place with a rough cloth, so that the arteries appear. Then let the sick one tie his own neck with any cloth of his. Then consider, where the vein pulsates. And the places of both are places that are depressed after the ears, and they are rarely hidden, unless in some men.
Then mark both with hot iron, and cut each one with a thin knife from both sides, the incision reaching the bone, and let it be wide enough for the head.
And if you wish, introduce the thin knife under the artery and cut it from above with the incision.
The length of the incision should be like that of two fingers joined.
When a vein is cut, blood flows out by pulsating exudation, which leaps to the interior by frequent jumps.
If however an artery is not apparent to the sense, then one should measure the quantity of space with three fingers. Then mark [the place] with wax and cut up to the bone.
And that which must be let out from the blood is six ounces, and perhaps you will let out more or less from it. Do that [letting out of blood] according to the quantity which appears to you due to the strength of the patient and the filling of the artery.
Then, consider the wound. If there remains something on the bone from the flesh, then cut it, so that no warm abscess occurs; then stitch the wound with linen strips.
Then care for him with an ointment until he is healed.
Chapter on the extraction of arteries, which are in the temples.
Chapter III.
When an old hemicranium (migraine) or acute catarrh due to acidic humidities and warmth in the temples, or an old soad (scrofula), violent, and similar conditions occur in a man; and it is treated with modes of curative medicine, but it does not help; then we have experience in these afflictions in extracting arteries from the temples, or cauterizing them, as we have related.
The method of operation for extracting (them) is that the sick person shaves hairs which are on the temples, and stretches himself to the visible artery in the temple. It is indeed shown to you by its pulse and it is rarely hidden except in a few men or in case of violent coldness.
If it is hidden from you, then the sick person should tighten his head with any cloth of his and then scratch the place with a rough cloth. Or fumigate the place with hot water until it appears to you in a clear manifestation. Then take the spatula which I have prepared earlier. Then scrape off the skin with it easily until you reach the artery. Then plunge a hook into it and pull it out towards the top until you pull it out from the skin, and make it exit from the tunics that are beneath it on all sides.
If the artery is fine: then fold it with the tip of the hook. Then cut from it a portion according to the length its ends extend and contract, so as not to cause bleeding. Because if it is not cut and if it is not severed, blood will not rise up deeply.
Then evacuate six ounces of blood, up to the third.
If the artery is large: it is necessary to tie it in two places with thick thread made of silk or twine; or with gut-string, so that putrefaction does not approach it before the wound consolidates and there is bleeding.
Then cut off the redundancy, which is between two ligaments. Do this at that hour or another hour.
And if you wish, cauterize it with the cautery until it reaches the bone, using a sharp-pointed cautery: until its ends are cut off and it remains in place for that same operation.
And this work is better unless the patient has a fever or is of chilly constitution. Because the cautery is from those things that help to stop moisture (bleeding). Therefore, it is better as a remedy.
And after the extraction of arteries, the place should be filled with hot ashes; and fine pulverized charcoal should be placed on it.
And after the dissolution (of gangrene), it is to be scraped with dry medicines that cause new flesh to grow and with linen until it heals.
If during the operation there is bleeding from an artery, then hasten to cut it off with a cautery or to fill the place with wax; and press your hand until the bleeding stops. If none of those is present to you, then place your finger on it until the blood freezes. And apply a cold compress to the place with water of intense cold until the pain ceases and it is pressed according to what is necessary.
And of that which is easier and less difficult for the extraction of an artery, it is to cauterize the vein with this cautery having two points: let the point of the two points be similar to an almond (small round object). However, they are much less sharp than two needles. Because if they are as sharp as two needles, there will be frost for both; and they will not cut through the flesh quickly. When there is a certain amount of thickness [in the diseased part], it is necessary to apply heat from fire and quickly cut off the flesh; for this operation is better than any other, and easier, and more straightforward.
And this is the shape of a cautery.
And the space that is between two knives should be a thickness of one finger's breadth, after you have marked two places with hot iron; and lay both heated ones down until they reach the bone, and cut the vein in two places: so that what lies between the extremities may be removed. For this cautery does not heal [the wound] completely.
Chapter IV.
Chapter on the treatment of chronic, sharp tears from the eyes.
When tears are persistent and flow from the veins on the outside of the skull: and no medication for treatment is applied to them with medicines, and the face of the sick person becomes red, and sensation is felt in the forehead as if it were ants crawling: and the eyes are exhausted, wet, so that the hairs of them are already corroded by the corrosion: and the eyelids have been heated due to the sharpness of the tears: then, in their treatment, ancient physicians resorted to this operation, which they called the Cure with a Sword.
And it is to instruct the sick person to shave the hairs that are on their forehead. Then make three incisions on the forehead of equal length, and let the length of each incision be approximately two fingers, and one incision be equal in length to the nose in the middle of the forehead, and the second slightly beyond the movement of the arms, and the third on the opposite side: and be careful not to cut through the arteries that are on both sides: and extend your hand from the continuation of the two jaws, and let the entire length of the incision be three fingers' width apart: and prepare for yourself a piece of sponge or dry cloth with which to absorb blood.
Then insert two sharp points, following their form. From the first incision to the second, scrape off the skin that is between the two incisions, along with the forehead above it. Then do the same from the middle incision to the second incision. Then remove the sharp points, and insert another instrument called a sharp knife, with one edge, not sharp on both sides, into the first incision. And this is its form.
And place the pointed side of it facing the skin attached with flesh, and the blunt side facing the bone; then push it until it reaches the middle fissure; and cut along with it all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes, except that the incision should be continued up to where it appears on the skin.
Then make it in the middle fissure up to another fissure.
And when an equal quantity of blood flows out from it, squeeze the places from the clotted blood's stumps.
Then put linen cloth from an old cooking pot into every fissure, and place over them wetted wool soaked in oil, or vinegar. And see to it that no warm abscess occurs.
And on the third day loosen the bandage, and administer a large infusion with warm water. Then take care of it with a basilicon ointment and the other things that heal wounds until it heals.
Chapter V.
Chapter on the treatment of sharp tears and catarrhs of the eyes from internal parts of the head.
When someone gets sharp, severe, continuous catarrhs, and you see their eyes are stretched, small, and already weakened in appearance; and the eyelids are ulcerated, and hairs fall out from them, and there is acute pain deep in the head, causing discomfort and sneezing; then take from these symptoms, that those substances and catarrhs do not come unless from many veins.
A better treatment for them is this. And it is to command the sick person to shave his forehead. Then make one cut in the middle of the forehead, or slightly to one side for less width, and start with the cut from the left temple to the right temple; let the incision go as deep as the bone: extend your hand away from the moving temples until the bone is exposed: and absorb all the blood with a sponge.
Then separate the cut between the two lips of the wound with tweezers or linen strips. Then bind it on top with thread: and soak the threads in wine and oil to prevent a hot abscess.
And when you loosen it and see that the abscess is about to subside: then break the bone, until new flesh begins to grow in it.
Then treat the patient with a drying regimen that promotes new flesh growth; as if you were taking two parts of wheat flour and four parts of pitch; and prepare an ointment from them, and apply it to promote new flesh growth in these wounds.
Chapter VI.
Chapter on the treatment of wounds that fall into the ear.
Everything that falls into the ear is one of four species: either a mineral stone, or something resembling a stone such as iron and glass: or it is from a plant, like peas and beans: or it is liquid, such as water, vinegar, and similar things: or it is some animal.
When a stone falls into the ear or anything similar that does not grow in the ear and is not added to it, expose the ear alone: if you see a stone then pour something from violated oil or sesame into the ear. Then administer the extraction of it and make him sneeze with snuff mixed with powdered charcoal, and obstruct the nostrils near the moment of sneezing, after you place around the ear fragments from cloths or wool, and stretch the ear upward.
Many times it escapes with this treatment.
If it does not escape, then administer the extraction of it with Guidon's method (that is, subtle Pizigarol), whose form is this.
If it escapes with Guidon's method, it is good.
And if it does not, then administer the extraction of it with a fine hook, several times repeated.
If it does not escape through that, then make a tube from brass and insert the end of the tube into the ear opening widely, and obstruct what is around the tube with beeswax softened with oil so that there is no way out except the tube: then draw it out with your strong attraction.
Many times it escapes with what we have said. If it does not escape by that method: then take some helkalimbated or water (that is, prepared gluten), a small amount, which birds are caught with: and place it at the end of the radius when you have properly placed a sieve on it: then insert it into the ear opening gently, after you have removed the ear from moisture.
If therefore it does not come out with all that I have mentioned, then hasten to cut, before a hot abscess or spasm occurs.
The method of lancing is as follows: first draw blood from the patient with a lancet; and remove according to the power of the lancet from his blood. Then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear towards above and make a small lancet-like incision at the base of the ear in its fatty tissue where it is depressed; let the lancet be of lunar shape until you reach the stone; then remove it along with it, as far as possible with your instruments.
Then make the lancet incision from your side quickly and take care of it until it heals.
If what falls into the ear is one grain or more which grow and swell; then administer its extraction.
But if it does not obey you to come out, then take a fine, thin probe shaped as follows.
And administer with it the excision of that species from the grains which fall into the ear and do not do this when you think that that grain is already moistened by the steam of the ear, until you place many fragments upon it; then remove it with tweezers, or with a fine probe, or with suction, as we have said; for its extraction is eased.
In water which enters the ear, the patient should use sneezing when he is forced to do so first; and already his ear has filled itself with some hot old liquid; and it lies on that ear where the water is. If therefore it comes out through this, it is good.
But if not: then take many small, soft stones of the length of a finger and heat them slightly with fire; and let the patient insert one from these into the ear's opening; and let him spit on his foot from that side, and strike with a stone upon the stone in the ear. Therefore, it should not cease to be done with stone and stone until all water comes out.
And now the water comes out in such a way that you take one from parchment or reed, and insert its end into the ear; and light the other end with fire until it is burned as much as possible. Then take another reed and do this many times until all water comes out; and draw it out with a tube as previously mentioned in the stone.
In the extraction of an animal entering into it (if it is small in body, like a louse, and similar to it), care should be taken of it as previously mentioned in division.
But if it is of a large body, which appears to the senses: then administer its extraction with forceps and hooks; and its nature is easier for all who hold it in the ear.
In the extraction of worms generated in the ear, when you care for it as we have previously said in division and in the treatment of distillations, and your care does not help: then you should look at the ear in sunlight. If therefore something appears there from worms, then draw it out with forceps or fine hooks.
If however nothing appears there, then take a tube with this shape, narrow below and wide above; and insert its fine end into the ear according to how much weak it can tolerate; then draw it out forcefully with that suction. Do this many times until all worms come out.
If however they do not obey you to leave, then bind them with the tube of poppy seeds as previously mentioned in the stone.
If they do not come out with what was said, then administer the distillations which the ancients have already experienced in the destruction of worms; and you will find it in the treatment of distillations.
And let your flow (be) with oil and medications into the ear using this tool, whose form is depicted here. As you see, make it from silver or brass, narrower below, with a small hole at the bottom and a larger one on top.
Therefore, let the implement that is within the concavity of the tube be made of brass properly. And if you wish, take radium (a type of brass) and wind its end with a suitable coil; then pour oil, juice or whatever medicine you desire into the tube; let this be in the ear; then insert the radium with the coiled part on top and press it with your hand until the oil is forced into the concavity of the ear, and let the sick person feel it inside; and whatever is poured into the ear should already be slightly heated by fire; but take care that what distills into it is not too cold; for medicines cannot tolerate this.
Chapter VII.
[Section on the treatment of aural impaction]
When some infants are born from the wombs of their mothers without perforated ears.
And it happens to some people that impaction occurs in the ear due to a wound or flesh born there.
And this impaction sometimes occurs in the deep hole of the ear which is not visible to the eye; and sometimes it occurs near the outer hole of the ear which can be seen.
Therefore, that which happens in the deep part of the ear and is not within the reach of sight, is difficult to cure in many ways.
And in that which can be seen, it is necessary to place the ear of the sick person in the sun and examine it; then if you see the impaction appearing, open it with a thin spatula whose form is as follows, its end having a small notch, part of which is sharp; and the rest of the spatula should be of two flat sides so as not to harm the ear.
If therefore the excision is born from the flesh within the ear: then hold it with a fine hook, and cut it with great force, until all the flesh is removed.
If therefore the boil is deep within the ear: then take a fine and gentle probe, heat it slightly with fire; then insert it into the ear.
If you feel the boil with it, that it comes accompanied by weakness and loss of hearing, try to open it gently; and beware, lest you injure the nerves of the ear.
Then place linen within the ear according to the size of the hole you have made, having wrapped it in Egyptian ointment; do this for several days until you are certain about the healing of the wound.
Or take linen, and immerse it in rose water, and grind upon it alum powder, and use it.
If you see the ear already discharging: then you must draw out the linen, and allow it to be with another linen that you wrap in a pot made with rose oil, until the abscess becomes warm; then care for it until it is healed.
If there is bleeding, however: then immerse sponge or cloths in cold water and place it on the ear; and use the rest of the treatment that removes the mentioned bleeding by means of distillations.
Chapter on Althaea's care for the eyelids.
Chapter VIII.
These are the Thehelil that occur in the eyelids when they are sometimes moist and sometimes dry.
Therefore, it is necessary to hold them with tweezers or with a hook, and cut them at their roots. Then place on top of the wound a piece of linen cloth that has been ground up.
If however blood flows from them, then cauterize them with a fine lens-shaped cautery.
And to cauterize them is better after an incision. They often return when something remains from their roots. And when they are cauterized with fire, those roots will burn away and they will not return.
Chapter on the care of swellings in the eyelids of the eye.
Chapter IX.
Often something happens in the eyelids that is similar to a swelling in its hardness and toughness, and it is called a Crandin because it is an accumulation of coarse moisture on the upper eyelid and the lower one.
Therefore, the operation is to determine if it is a Crandin that appears on the eyelid and moves to all parts, and its substance is soft.
Make an incision over it in width. Then remove it from all sides with ease until it comes out. Then hang it with a hook and cut it off.
If the removal of it is not prepared for you unless after you have made an incision into the eyelid a little, then it may harm someone weak with that.
If the incision is large: then stitch it up with sutures: and care for it until it heals.
And if it is small, no harm will come to you from it. For an ointment restores it and fills it in.
If a foreign body is directed towards the inner parts of the ear and turned against the intrinsic surface, then invert the eyelid and hang up the foreign body with a hook; besides which you will need incision, and press it from all sides.
If the eyelid is stretched by incision, it does not harm anything.
Then clean the eye after the incision of the foreign body with salt water; and take care of the place where it was, until the affected part heals.
Chapter on the treatment of eyelids.
Chapter X.
The Axirnath is a growth that arises in the upper eyelid tissues; and it mostly happens to children; it burdens their eyes, and they get cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot see the light of the sun, because tears flow towards them, and therefore you can always see them lying on their faces, and sleeping on them, and their eyelids are always wet under the eyebrows, which has already been covered by swelling; and the appearance of Axirnath protruding is visible to the eye, and when you press the place with your fingers, you feel Axirnath between them.
And the method of treatment for it is that the patient places his head in your lap.
Then take a clean cloth, and prepare a linen bandage on it, and make a circle from the linen around Axirnath to its entire size. Then place it on the bandage and press with your fingers all around it, so that Axirnath gathers in the middle of the circle.
Then find in the middle of that moisture with a spatula-like instrument and make shallow cracks parallel to its width, but do not make the crack larger than what is done in phlebotomy in depth.
It is necessary that you find the entire skin, until you reach Axirnath, for in many dispositions, Axirnath proceeds from the fracture according to the shape of a white plum's pit.
Draw it out with a cloth that you have moistened between your fingers to the outside: and you rotate your hand to the right and left, until it is dispersed; and be careful not to add anything in the fracture, so that you do not reach the spittle to the eye, and harm it.
If, however, Axirnath does not appear to you at the beginning of the fracture, you shall add a little in the fracture with ease, until Axirnath proceeds. Then draw it out as we said.
Then immerse the cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the place, and bind it with small stones.
And among men there are those who grind salt and put it into the hollow of the fracture, so that it melts what remains from that moisture.
Then take care of it until it is healed.
If, however, a boil hot appears in the place, then take care of it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
Chapter on the modes of Ataxmir (eyes), that is, when the eyelid softens, so that it weeps as it should not.
Chapter XI.
When hairs grow in the eyelids beyond the course of natural hairs and become old; then they harm the eye, and cause the occurrence of diseases such as constant weeping, softening of the eyelid, and whitish film, until it becomes the cause of the destruction of the eye.
And indeed the eyes are treated according to four modes (methods) of Ataxmir. Through cauterization with fire. With sharp medicine, according to what has been mentioned in the chapter on cauterization. The ataxmir is cured by incision and suturing. With reeds, according to what I shall say.
You must place the head of the sick person on your lap. Then, turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand.
If it is thus turned, that is good. And if not: insert the point into it, where there is a thread from below the eyelid, and make the point penetrate with the thread above, and let it be close to the hairs themselves, that is, close to the edge of the eyelid, where the hairs grow: and pull the thread upwards with the eyelid, and turn it with a rod.
Then, find on the inside of the eyelid under the added hairs with a spatula slipping from the greater lacrimal gland to the lesser one.
Then draw out the thread and put a small feather under the eyelid from cooked wool or cloth; then mark on the eyelid with wax, as the figure of a myrtle leaf.
However, it should be made according to the size and elevation of the eyelid, because it is diversified among humans.
From those who require that an incision be made according to the size of the eyelid, in proportion to its softening.
Then with the spatula find on top of the two lines which you marked, and start from the greater lacrimal gland to the lesser one, and let there be a split near the natural hairs, as the width of a rod.
Then insert the hook into one of the two angles of the skin. Then scrape it all. Then gather together with suture two lips, with a sharp needle and fine woolen thread: and clean the blood, and make adhere what excesses from the threads on the two eyebrows, with some adhesives if you wish to do so: and if not, do not care.
Then release the suture and threads for three or four days, afterwards take care of it.
If you wish, release the wound without suture and take care of it as it dries and contracts. For the eyelid is to be raised during sealing of the wound and its bandaging, but it will be better later.
This method of treatment was taught by the ancients Ataxmir.
However, there is worry about the sick person in it, and it is from a good operation, and there is no fear in it.
And another method is also in Ataxmir, and it is that signs are made on the eyelid in the form of a myrtle leaf, as we have told.
Then raise the eyelid with three separated or joined combs according to the following form, then cut what exceeds with small scissors according to this form, with equal incisions.
If it is not possible for you to hold the comb and it does not fit equally, then take a needle with thread on it, and insert it into the middle of the figure: and insert another thread near the larger tear duct, and another thread near the smaller tear duct: and gather the threads between your fingers equally.
Then raise your hand evenly with an elevation, and lift the skin where it is marked by the incision, as we have told.
Then gather together two lips of the wound with suture: and take care of it until it heals.
If a boil or an ulcer occurs at your incision or your wound, swab it with linen and wax, and apply ointments that soothe such things.
And sometimes the eyelashes may also turn inwards.
Therefore, it is necessary to use the method mentioned above for this case, but stitching both parts should be more artificial. Chapter on the care of the bite of a mad dog.
And it is necessary to turn the eyelid and cut the wound that is on the inside, as I have explained. Then make two needles or thin pieces of wood whose length is the same as that of the eyelid and their width less than the width of the eyelash; and you have now cut into the ends of both, from both sides where you hold the thread.
Then bring each one together with fine material over the surplus of the eyelid of the eye and sew two needles tightly from both sides with a strong stitch and leave it for some days. For skin that is sutured will die, become darker, rot and fall off by itself.
If it does not heal quickly, then cut it with scissors. Then take care of it until it heals.
When it has healed, the eyelid is lifted and no hairs are plucked.
And this is the shape of two needles that you should make according to this pattern and size in length and width.
Chapter 12.
Chapter on removing hair from the eye with a needle.
The operation is to take a fine needle and insert a thin thread from silk into it gently. Then bring the ends together and knot them tightly with a fine knot; let the length of the threads be one palm.
Then, on the Alinxotati thread, make another slender one beneath it in short length, and knot its ends if you wish.
Then let the sick person put his head in your lap and the operation be near the sun for it to be visible: since it is a subtle or minute operation.
Then insert the needle along with Alinxotati into the root of the eyelid and make it penetrate into the eyelid quickly until you pull out the natural hair from above.
Then pull out the hair above Alinxotati and insert this hair into Alinxotati: if there is one or two or three, but not more than that.
Then pull your hand with it until the hair comes out together with Alinxotati from the eyelid along with the natural hair.
If Alinxotati is pulled out and no hair comes out with it, pull Alinxotati towards the bottom while keeping the thread you made in it until Alinxotati comes out from the upper hole, and you see it through the eye: then pull Alinxotati and the thread; remove both and close the eye; leave the closed one for two or three days until hair grows back at its place and flesh covers it.
If the hair is short, then join a long hair from the natural hairs with it and lift them up together; or leave it alone until it grows longer, and then lift it up.
Chapter 13.
When this Xatrat happens to the eye, it is called Leporina.
And this Xatrat is either natural or accidental.
Therefore, the accidental Xatrat arises from a congealing of wounds, cuts, cauterizations and similar things.
The method of operation is for you to locate that consolidation, and to separate its lips, and to place in it a linen cloth within, and to tie it until it heals.
And it is not appropriate to use in the treatment of it things that dry and constrict: for if you do that, Alxatratus becomes worse than it was: rather use in it things that soften, such as fenugreek; and embrocation with water, in which althea has been cooked, linseed seeds; and dyaquilon ointment, which has been made liquid with some oil; and wrap it with linen cloth, and treat it with it.
The treasure of your cure is that you strive with all your skill, so that it does not become consolidated again, in its original form first.
And indeed this operation that I have said is nothing but a correction of Alxatratus, so that the form of the place does not return to what it was entirely.
Chapter on the care of Alxatratus that is performed in the lower eyelid, and it is a swelling or contraction upward to the right and left.
Chapter XIII.
This Alxatratus that occurs below is what is truly called Alxatratus. It is natural and it is accidental.
And the accidental Alxatratus is made from a wound, or a split, or cautery, and similar things.
The method of operation in it is that you take a sharp probe with a double thread, and stain it in the flesh, and make it penetrate from the left tear duct to the right tear duct until the thread reaches both ends of the flesh.
Then extend the flesh upwards with the probe and cut it with a broad spatula. If therefore the form of the eyelid returns as it should be, it is good.
And if not, take radish, and place it in the fissure, and turn it with it the eyelid; and make two fissures in the interior side of the eyelid, and let their ends be from two angles of the incision, until they converge and form an angle: until when they are gathered together, let the figure be this figure, and it is the Greek letter Lambda.
Then remove that flesh to the extent of its sharp lower part, from what follows the eyelid. Then gather the separated parts; or join it with a thread of wool.
Then care for them with that which I said, with softening medicines and linen, until they heal.
If Al-Zaturat occurs from the fissure or suture, or cautery: then it is necessary to make a flat incision below the eyelashes, according to what has preceded. Then separate between two lips with linen, as I said.
The summary of the treatment for Al-Zaturat, whether it is above or below, is that the operation should be carried out on it, according to the preparation of the Al-Zaturat's form.
For indeed it is of many varieties in its shape: and the skilled artisan prepares his skill with whatever means is possible for him, until he returns the figure to its natural form or close to it, and himself the sick person, according to what suits him from the operation and instruments in many different positions.
Chapter XV.
Chapter on the adherence of the eyelid with conjunctiva or cornea.
Sometimes this consolidation occurs in many people, so that the upper eyelid adheres to the whites of the eye and prevents it from performing its natural functions.
Therefore, it is necessary that you introduce the extremity of the radius beneath the eyelid, and lift it up: or extend it with a hook: then cut the adhesion with a subtle spatula, which should not be with the sharpness of spatula incisions, but rather blunt slightly: so as not to disturb the weak during the operation, and remove the spatula, and injure the eye with its sharpness: and let your incision be as if you are scraping off that adhesion with ease, until when the eyelid returns to its natural form, and the adhesion heals completely.
Pour salty water into the eye, while washing it: or distill onto it from seive made, with dissolved zinc mixed with water.
Then separate between eyelid and eye with a linen cloth: and place warm wool soaked in egg white over the eye: and for three days use zinc, and with ointments, until it heals.
[Chapter] On Incision of the Nail and Protrusion of Skin of Tear Ducts.
Chapter XVI.
Know that the nail is according to two modes. Or it is nerve-like: and it is like a horn, subtle. Or it is not nerve-like, similar to the hardness of frozen milk, which when touched with iron, or attempted to be taken with a hook, is cut off, and the hook does not stick to it.
And neither of these types start, unless from the greater tear duct, up to where it gradually penetrates, until it covers the vision, and prevents light, and movement of the eye.
And the method of operation in its incision is: that you place the head of the weak in your armpit. Then open the eyes of his, and lift the eyelid with your hand. Then gather the nail with a few-fold hook and stretch it upwards. Then take the awl and insert a hair from a horse, ox or sheep into it; let it be a thread and slightly double the tip of the awl and fix it in the middle of the nail; pierce with the awl and tie the nail with the thread and stretch it upwards. Scrape off the side of the nail that follows the pupil, as if you were pulling it with the hair until the end of its root.
Then cut the remainder at the root of the lacrimal duct with a fine spatula or small forceps; and let the natural tissue of the lacrimal gland remain, so that no constant flow of tears results from the incision.
And sometimes the nail is extended with a hook alone; or with thread, as we have said. Then scrape it with a soft spatula, which has this shape:
Be careful not to touch the spatula on the horny layer and cause a break there, and pierce the pupil.
After the incision, throw into the eye something of ground salt or made from cinnabar and leave it until another day. Then care for the eye as necessary until it heals.
If the nail is not nerve-rich and you cannot insert the awl into it or the hook does not take hold there, then this type of nail is repeatedly treated with medicines until it heals as I have said in the division.
If you wish to cut it, then open the eye of the sick person and take a soft, fine, delicate spatula of low hardness in this shape: And scrape the nail from above with fineness. If you see that it becomes hard and crumbles and presses the nail with the scraper, then pour from your hour into the eye from cinnabar made from zinc or red cinnabar or ground salt; and close the eye until another day.
Then repeat the operation until the entire thing is removed. If a warm abscess is not present in the eye, then leave it alone and take care of the abscess until it heals.
Then repeat the operation on it with reason, until it heals.
A protrusion of flesh from the lacrimal duct, if it causes great harm to the eye, is suspended with a hook and cut out from there; do not make a deep cut so that the flow of tears is not interrupted.
Then let blood from the lacrimal sac or ruby-red wine, or use silver nitrate, until it heals.
Chapter on Alguardenic's Incision and the flesh born in the eye.
Chapter XVII.
There sometimes arises in the eyes of humans a red flesh composed or laid over, which covers the pupil, approaches it, or presses on the eyelids and possibly turns the eyelids outwards; it resembles a rosebud on a pillar.
And the operation in it is also to place the sick head in your armpit. Then open his eyes and gather all that flesh together with appropriate forceps; and hold it with a single pair of forceps or tweezers.
Then cut the flesh first, to finish everything with a knife (or lancet). And be careful not to cut the eye itself during the operation; and let your incision be where you are cutting, or with a lancet as we have mentioned in the chapter on toe amputation, or with small forceps, such as those used for probing an abscess, according to its form after this chapter.
When your incision is complete and all the alguardenic (pus) has been removed, then fill the eye with a solution of ground salt or distill red powder and similar medicines from corrosive substances; and place on top of the eye outside a piece of cotton with white fat of an egg, to protect it from hot inflammation.
If there remains some pus and you are dominated by hot blood and fear a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone, and treat the same with what calms an abscess.
Then repeat the operation over him until he is healed.
And likewise do with the flesh that occurs around the eye of this type.
However, it is necessary that any weak eye from natural or accidental causes be treated without iron, and you should not insert your hand into any of these operations until you see that the limb can endure this treatment.
Chapter on draining an abscess from the eye.
Chapter XVIII.
Abscesses are red veins that surround the eye and prevent visual function; they weaken the eye with the passage of days.
It is necessary for you first to consider whether the eye where the Sebel (cataract) is present, is strong and there is no other illness except the cataract. Then collect the cataract from it.
And it is to command the weak (patient), that he puts his head in your lap.
Then hang those veins with one or two needles according to your judgement. And let the needle be fine of double-thread thickness, or there should be two needles graduated within one body according to this shape.
Then collect those veins with fine forceps and cautiously, remove the blood by the hour, until you see the veins removed from the eye and dissolved; and be careful not to harm the eye with the points of the forceps.
And let your procedure be at midday before the sun, and be very firm in your procedure; so that you do not cut except those veins.
And when you have finished (the procedure), then distill into the eye, either green or red; so that with its own acidity it burns what remains of the cataract.
If it is not possible for you to collect it all in that hour, then apply a plaster to the eye with what alleviates the pain of the eye; and leave it for some days until the pain subsides; and secure it with warm compresses; afterwards repeat over it according to the same method until it heals.
And this is the shape of the forceps.
Chapter on reducing Arissa (nasal polyps) to the nose.
Chapter XIX.
The physician named Arisate treats a Fistula, which he cares for with a cautery or with a sharp medicine burning, as his narrative precedes.
If it is not cured, then there is no skill in it; except that you should open above the abscess at its birth, and extract all the moisture that is in it and the pus, until the bone is exposed.
When the bone is exposed, and you see corruption or blackness in it, then grind it with this tool, whose shape is as follows.
And it is called an Asperi capitis (Aspergillus capitis).
Make it from iron indo, and let its head be round like an azir (a type of abrasive stone), which is punctured with a file or with the subtle point of aliskilfer (another type of abrasive stone): and place it over the corrupted bone.
Then turn it with your fingers, and press your hand a little, until you know that the corruption is already ground down; and do this several times.
Then restore the place with most powerful healing balms.
If the place consolidates and flesh grows there, and a flow of pus is cut off; and it remains for 40 days without being renewed, without developing an abscess, and no accident happens in it; then you will know that it is cured.
If not, then there is no skill in it, except to reduce the fistula to the nostril opening, according to this shape.
And it is to expose the bone of the second bone (presumably a toe) with iron or with sharp medicine; and when the bone is exposed, then take the trephine according to this shape, its end should be iron, triangular: and the wood of it should be pyramid-shaped, extended to the end, as you see.
Then place it on the very same skin: and let it be near the tear-duct: and stretch out your hand slightly from the eye. Then turn your hand with the lancet until it penetrates the bone, and feel it weaken: through this you will know that air is escaping from it, when he holds his hand over his nose.
Therefore, then restore the place with medicines drying, as I have taught you.
When the flesh grows and hardens, then the matter which was flowing out goes back to the nose; therefore it is lighter over the sick place.
[Chapter Title: Reducing protrusion of the Eye.]
Chapter 20.
When the eye protrudes completely and there is no visual harm or reduction, then it is necessary to dissolve the weakened part. Then apply leeches [phlebotomes] to it. After that, place warm fumigations on the neck without scarification but with suction.
Then apply a poultice made from acacia, aloe, frankincense [olibanum], and colophony [sarcocollyra] on the eye. Then bind the eye above with a plaster containing many small beetles [pulvillas].
The method of the beetles is: take soft cloths many, and fold all the cloths over four; make many [of them]; then place one on top of another according to the quantity that the eye needs; then bind them tightly with a strong bandage.
And repeat the fumigations without scarification but with suction.
Then remove the fumigations and let the eye be bound day and night.
If the binding becomes soft again, then it is necessary to bind it tightly; then remove the binding after a day and night as we have said.
If therefore you see the eye already returned to its sheath, it is good: and if not, then repeat the ointment, leeches, tightening bandage, and fumigations until it heals.
Chapter on the Incision of the Sheath.
Chapter XXI.
When there is a rupture of the sheath of the eye, then it protrudes and comes out beyond the eyelids like a grain of sand, and it fouls up the human form due to this, and one wishes to cut it: at that time, an operation should be performed on it, as I have said; and it is to insert the needle into the root of the eye from the bottom to the top.
Then insert another needle with a double thread from the tear duct side, and make it penetrate; and release the first needle according to its position.
Then cut the place of the double thread, and tie a piece of it around the eye with the needle; and tighten it strongly.
Then remove the needle, and place wool soaked in oil over the eye on the white part: and leave it until the thread falls with the eye.
Then care for the eye with what strengthens it, until the wound heals.
And sometimes the eye is tightened from all sides with a circle made of cloth, until the eye protrudes greatly.
Then it is pierced with a fine cannula that reaches deep into the eye, and moistens the white part; and the eye sinks down, and enters immediately; then tighten it until it heals.
Chapter on the Treatment of Conjunctivitis.
Chapter XXII.
This malady called Alcomnati is nothing but pus gathered in the eye, similar to descending water, and it is not itself.
The method of operation in this case is to make the patient sit on a prepared seat or straight chair.
Then take his head with both your hands and move it until you see the pus descend to the lower part of the eyes. Then make it stop and do not let it descend, and the vision shall be cleared; and let the patient see as he did before: and if it does not descend to the lower part, know that it is water.
If, however, there is no descent of pus as mentioned above, then make the patient sit between your hands. Then take a sharp probe and puncture it above the corneal membrane a little near the junction with the cornea in the corona (rim) until pus comes out.
When the pus comes out, then pour warm water mixed with honey into the eye, or warm water in which you have already boiled fenugreek and honey; afterwards treat it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
Treatment for water that descends into the eye or cataract.
Chapter XXIII.
We have already said the type of water in division, and which is suitable for perforation in discussion and explaining; then take it according to its health.
Then you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the light, near the sun; and bind the healthy eye and compress it strongly; then with your right hand close the eyelid of the eye in which there is water, or with your left hand if the eye is on the right side.
Then take your right hand (if the eye is in the left), or your left hand (if the eye is in the right).
Then place the forceps called almagdah near the corona (cornea) by the thickness of a radius within the white part of the eye that appears as the lesser lachrymal; then push the almagdah with force, and you will turn your hand with it until it penetrates into the white part of the eye, and you will feel that the almagdah has already reached the empty space.
The measurement of the journey of the almagdah to depth should be the measurement of the space from the pupil up until the end of the blackness; and that is the cornea of the eye. You will see it (the almagdah) within the pupil vision of the eye, because of the clarity of the cornea membrane.
Then place the forceps called almagdah up to the place where there is water (in the anterior chamber). Then press it (the almagdah) downward with a slight push after another.
If the water then descends immediately, then the patient sees what is before him immediately, and the forceps in his eye (the almagdah).
Then wait for a little while. If the water descends, then remove it (the forceps) after it has come out of the almagdah.
When it is fixed and does not rise again: then remove the forceps with ease; and you turn your hand slowly.
Then dissolve something from salt in clear water (saline solution) and wash the eye inside with it. Then place a pad of wool soaked in rose oil or linen over the white part of the eye and tie it to the healthy eye.
We, as well as those who are in our time, place camphor powder over him with the white part of the eye.
If the forceps called almagdah does not obey you to enter the eye due to its hardness because it is a human eye that is very hard; then it is necessary for you to take spatulia called Alberid, whose shape is as follows:
Perforate [the abscess] only with the same [incision], and do not insert your finger into the hole: it is only to make a way to a subtle place.
Then insert the probe, as we have said.
Furthermore, for the completion of your work, prepare a well-made bed for the sick person, in which he may sleep on his back in a dark room; and let him be kept from all movement, and from coughing; and let food be given to him that soothes his nature; and let him not move his head to either side at all.
And let the binding be according to its placement until the third day.
Then loosen that [the bandage] in the dark room and test his sight; and make him see things. Then bind it again until the seventh day.
It is not necessary that he perform it at the hour of treatment, or immediately after the incision; on the contrary, it should be left to others, because water rises quickly through a heated opening.
If however an abscess becomes hot: then it is necessary to loosen the eye before the seventh day; and straighten that which soothes the abscess, until it is soothed; then without his sight, and place a device for regulating his vision over his face, for several days, while he remains in the dark room.
Then he should leave the house gradually and change into his clothes.
And know that a student is not excused from watching [the operation] on several occasions; then he will dare to perform [the operation].

Therefore, I have not seen anyone in your land who has done that; nor have I read it in any of the ancient books. It is possible that it is new.
These are forms of species from Magda, to stand over her who does not know them.
