Chapter XXIV.
Chapter on care of the newborn flesh in the nose.
Whenever newborn flesh of various kinds grows in the nose, some of which resembles a scorpion with many feet; and from this is the cancerous meat, stony, dark brown in color; and from this is that which is tender, not dark brown.
Therefore, regarding that tender flesh which is not fraudulent or cancerous, it is necessary for the weak person to sit opposite your hands on the ground; and open his nostrils, and thrust the hook into those fleshes; then pull them towards the outside, and cut what you have caught with a fine, sharp spatula from one side, until you know that all of the flesh has been removed.
If something remains of that from whose removal is not possible; then shave it with a subtle tool with ease until nothing remains of it. If blood dominates over you, or a hot abscess occurs; then apply to it what is necessary: or if it is from malignant abscesses, then run towards cauterizing him until the blood is separated, and all fleshes are removed.
Then pour vinegar, water or wine into the nose after the incision. If the nose opens and moisture comes out until it reaches the palate; then you will know that he is already healthy.
If the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you know that within it is flesh born in the upper bones of the nose, which did not reach with the cutting instrument.
Then it is necessary that you insert a thread of flax with some thickness and knots in it; and place between each knot an amount equal to a finger or less; and bind the weak one, so that he sends out one end of the thread into the nose with a probe, or with whatever is possible for him after he has made it similar to a syringe; and draw out the odor, until it reaches the cavity, and exit onto the throat.
And indeed many times do the boys in school perform this like Atomus; and it is an easy matter for him who wants to.
Then place the two ends of the thread, one end which exits on the nose, and the other which remains in the nose. Then as a servant, you tie up the flesh with the knots that are in the thread. Do this until you know that the flesh is now with the knots of the thread.
Then extract the thread; and place linen inside the nose after bloodletting, which you have soaked in Egyptian ointment; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has eaten away all that remains of the flesh.
Then place a lead pipe at the end into the nose for some days until it heals.
If, however, it requires drying treatment, use that.
For the purge to be made with olive oil and other medicines poured into the nose, make it of silver or copper; that it be similar to a small lamp, open like a shell; and its channel likewise.
And if you wish to make a closed pipe, as with a reed.
And prepare the instrument for caputpurgery, let it be filled, exposed: to which belongs a handle at its end, with which you hold it, when you heat oil or what you wish from suction and flowing things in it.
Chapter XXV.
Many times a Thelul is born at the end of the nose, and it grows and increases with days until its appearance becomes disgusting.
And therefore, when it appears at the beginning, it is necessary to cut it off completely. Then place upon its place either a cautery, or a burning medicine that stays in its place.
If the cutting is delayed until it grows and becomes large, then consider whether it is made of stone, hard, dark in color, with few senses: then do not touch it with iron because it is a cancerous ulcer.
For many times I have seen that one has cut an apoma and evil has happened to him who possessed it.
And if the apoma is soft, not dark in color, and you see that cutting can be possible throughout it, then evacuate the weakened part, and cut it without fear or worry: and care for the place with it which drains and contracts until it heals.
Chapter XXVI.
Paragraph on the suture of the nose, lip, and ear.
Know that when discontinuity of a one of these cartilages occurs, little help is provided by the operation except in certain people.
Therefore, when something happens to anyone from it, consider whether it is a recent wound with blood flowing from it: and then apply two bandages to the wound with suture: then care for it until it heals.
If the continuity of the solution has already been separated and each part is healthy, then it is necessary to scrape off all parts appearing from the skin until it bleeds. Then gather together the two lips with sutures and bind them, and sprinkle draconian powder over the bleeding dragon's blood, and finely powdered olibanum: and place above the powders a piece of emplastrum diafinicon, and any other consolidated plaster: and leave it bound for two or three days. Then dissolve it, and change the medicine: and leave it until the threads separate on their own. Then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
The method of stitching is to gather together the solution of continuity, or with needles, as we have described in the suturing of the abdomen: or gather together the solution with thread, as I have taught you.
Chapter XXVII.
Chapter on the Extraction of Lumps on the Lips.
Many people indeed have hard nodules similar to grains of grass appearing on the inner parts of their lips; some of them smaller, and some larger.
Therefore, it is necessary to turn the lip over, and make an incision over every node of it, and hang it with a hook, and cut it off from all sides.
Then fill the place after the incision with zega finely powdered, until the blood separates.
Then wash it with vinegar and treat the place where there is a stoppage until the wounds heal.
Chapter XXVIII.
Chapter on the Incision of Born Flesh on the Gums.
Often flesh grows on the gums which is called abuluss by the ancients.
Therefore, it is necessary to hang it with a hook or hold it with forceps and cut it off near its root, and allow the pus or blood to flow out.
Then place over the place [that is] crushed, or other astringent powders, drying ones.
If the flesh returns after treatment, for it often returns, then cut [it] again and cauterize it; for it does not return after cauterization.
Chapter XXIX.
Chapter on Tooth Extraction with Iron.
When [teeth] collect on the surfaces of Teeth from within and without, and between rough gums, rotten, and sometimes turn yellow or greenish until corruption reaches the gum, and teeth become foul because of this.
Therefore, it is necessary that you make the sick person sit between your hands and put his head in your lap, and file the root and tooth where the gums appear to you, and grind it until there remains nothing of them; similarly for blackness, greenishness, yellowishness, and others, until they are cleaned.
If what is in them [teeth] is removed at the beginning of the filing, that is good; and if not, then repeat the filing on them on another day, the second, and the third, until finally the purpose is reached in what you wish.
And know that a tooth requires rasors of various shapes and figures; according to what is prepared for your operation, because the rasp used to file the tooth from below is another than the rasp used to file between teeth, according to other shapes.
And these shapes of rasps should be prepared by you, which you see.
Chapter XXX.
Chapter on Extracting Tooth Pain.
It is necessary to heal the Tooth from its pain with all skill, and proceed slowly in extracting it. For it is not that another substance can replace [the tooth] when it is extracted; because it is a lofty substance; until there is no excuse for extracting it, then if the sick person must extract it, it should be firmly held and assured by you that the painful tooth will be extracted.
Many times pain deceives the sick person and makes him think that it is in a tooth called Saha and removes it; then the pain does not subside until the diseased tooth is removed.
We have already seen this from the operation of phlebotomists.
When the tooth itself is certified as painful with you, then it is necessary that you incise around the tooth with a spatula, in which there is something of virtue, until the gums are loosened from all sides; then move it with your fingers, or with delicate forceps first of all gently, until you shake it.
Then place large forceps in the location on it and hold the head of the diseased tooth between your knees; what you have firmly grasped, so that it does not move; then pull out the tooth straight away, so as not to break it.
If it does not come out, then take one of those instruments and insert it beneath it from all sides with ease, and try to move it as you did at first.
If the tooth is perforated or eroded, then it is necessary that you fill the hole with cloth; and tighten it with the end of a small radius so that it does not break during your compression with forceps on top of it.
And it is necessary that you make a careful incision around the gums from all sides.
And maintain your strength so that you do not break it and leave a piece of it to return over the diseased tooth with the greater pain that was first present.
And be careful not to do what ignorant phlebotomists do in haste and the overconfidence of their own removal, exceeding what we have mentioned.
Many times they cause great ailments to occur in people, whose difficulties it is more difficult for them to be broken and all roots remain, or some of them; or to pull it out with some bones of the jaw, as we have often witnessed this.
Then, it is to be softened after excision (of the tumor) with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
If there is bleeding from the place (for it often happens), then rub something made of pomegranate peel and fill the place with it; and if you do not have this, cauterize it yourself without the pomegranate peel.
The handles of the delicate forceps, which move the tooth, should be long at the ends and short at the gripping part, thick so that they do not split when pressed against the tooth; they should resemble the handles of large forceps, until you are squeezing with them and they do not bite themselves or split; the ends of the handles should be sharp, made of steel or well-made iron, directed at an angle; and there should be teeth in their ends, some of which enter into some and tighten by a suitable constriction, strong.
And at times the ends are shaped like the beak of an eagle's mouth, which is called a ciconia, and they are strong in constriction.
Chapter XXXI.
Chapter on the Extraction of Teeth and Removal of Fractured Jaw Bones.
When some part remains in the extraction of a tooth that breaks off, then it should be placed on the spot with warm cow butter for one or two days until the place softens; then introduce into it the algasti or forceps whose ends are shaped like the beak of an eagle's mouth called ciconia. The form (of the forceps) is as follows:
The ends should be made in the shape of a file or like an aliskilfe.
If the tooth does not come out with these forceps, then you must cauterize on the root and strip the flesh completely and introduce an instrument called the small palanca whose form is as follows:
The end should be short and somewhat thick: and it should not be filled, so as not to break.
If the root comes out through that, it is good: and if not, it needs to be helped with these other instruments whose shapes are such.
The shape of the first triangle's end has a certain thickness.
The shape of the triangle's end is delicate.
And with other instruments and tools that have come before for the reason of teeth.
It is also helped with this instrument resembling a large hook, having the shape of a triangular twisted end, which has some thickness, so as not to break, and it should not be filled.
And know that there are many instruments for teeth: and similarly the remaining instruments are not counted, and the skilled craftsman, subtle in his art, finds for himself an instrument according to what the operation and the illness themselves signify.
Since there are illnesses for which the ancients did not make an instrument due to the diversity of their forms.
If the bone is broken from the jaw or from other bones of the face, or it rots: then examine it at its place with that which suits it among the instruments and pliers I mentioned for extraction of roots, and help it whose shape is this.
Let there be some thickness gradually, so that the bone can be pulled or held with it and does not run away and move, until the bone comes out: and restore the place with appropriate medications for that.
If there is minor rottenness in the bone, then scrape it from its rottenness, and treat it until it heals.
Head XXXII.
About locking of protruding teeth over others.
When teeth emerge not according to their natural course, the appearance becomes foul; and particularly when this happens in women and girls, namely in those who are in menstruation.
Therefore it is necessary that you consider. If a tooth is born after another tooth and does not settle or can be closed, nor can it be filed itself; then uproot it; and if it is attached with another tooth, then cut it with this instrument, of which this is the form.
It resembles a small beak, and is made of iron point, having an extremely sharp tip.
And let your cut be such that you cut it on many days, and because of the hardness of the tooth, and so as not to disturb another tooth.
If it is protruding exposed for filing; then file it with a rasp from iron, of which this is the form.
Let it be made of iron, and its handle small, with many sharp points like a rasp with which teeth are filed; with which you grind the tooth gradually on many days with ease, so as not to disturb another tooth, and let it fall; then smooth it gently, and finally sand it down with some rasps.
If it is a tooth that breaks off and injures the tongue; then it must be filed even more so until the roughness of the fracture is removed and it is made smooth; and it shall not injure the tongue nor corrupt speech.
Head XXXIII.
Chapter on the filing of teeth with gold threads.
When the anterior teeth are shaken and dislocated by blow or accident; and a weak person cannot hold down what he eats so that it does not fall out; and you have treated them with medicinal adhesives, but the treatment has not been effective; then they should be sewn with gold thread; because silver becomes corroded and putrefies after days; but gold never changes.
And let there be a thread of middle fineness and thickness according to its quantity that can pass between Teeth.
The form of the rete is such that you take a thread and pass it through the gaps between two healthy teeth; then you weave with both ends of the thread the movable teeth, whether one or more, until you reach with the needle to the healthy tooth on the other side. Then repeat the weaving until you reach the part from which you started; and hold your hand with subtlety and wisdom until it is not removed completely; let your constriction be at the roots of the teeth so that it does not come out.
Then cut the excessive ends of the thread with scissors; and bind both together and turn them towards each other; and hide the bound ones between the healthy tooth and the movable tooth, so as not to hurt the tongue; then release it when it is sufficiently tight.
If it loosens or breaks, bind it with another thread, and it will remain thus for the entire time.
And this is the form of teeth, and the figure of the rete of two healthy teeth, and two movable teeth, as you see.
And sometimes it happens that a tooth or two return to their places after a loss, and remain as we have said, and this does not happen unless the skillful and experienced artisan does it.
And sometimes a tooth from the bones of a cow is shaped; and it is placed in the place where the tooth is guarded and tightened, as we said; and it remains and serves for a long time.
Chapter XLIII.
When this ligament that occurs under the tongue is natural, it is born with a man; or it happens accidentally, from a healed wound.
The operation on him is that you open the sick man's skull in your hollow, and elevate his tongue; then cut through the nerve-ligament across its width, until the tongue is released from its hold.
If there is something hard and knotted in him, and it is due to consolidation of the wound; then strike with a hook on it, and bore through it across its width until you cut the ligament, and the knot is released.
And beware, lest there be a cleft in deep flesh, and you cut an artery there, and there be a flow of blood.
Then it is scraped in the wound-track with rosewater, or with vinegar, or cold water.
Then place a flax cloth beneath the tongue, which the sick man holds all night; so that it does not consolidate again.
If however there is a flow of blood, then place over the place zege tritum (perhaps meant to be zege tribitum, meaning crushed or powdered zege). But if the blood holds you back, then cauterize the place with a lentiginous cautery, which is suitable for it; then care for him with the rest of the cure until he is healed.
Chapter XXXV.
Sometimes there occurs an aposteme beneath the tongue resembling a small frog, hindering the tongue from its natural function; and perhaps it swells so much that it fills the bone.
The operation on him is that you open the sick man's jaw facing the sun, and examine the aposteme.
If you see it black or dark colored, hard and insensitive: then do not touch it, because it is cancer.
And if it is hollowed out towards whiteness where there is moisture, then throw in the hook and cut into it with a fine chisel, and release it from all sides. If your blood is confined by it during your operation, then place on top of it a piece of zecha ground, until the blood is released; then return to your operation until you extract it along with its entirety.
Then wash it with vinegar and salt, and take care of it according to the appropriate treatment until it is healed.
Chapter on the treatment of two tumors (amygdala).
Chapter 36:
Whenever there occur swellings in the throat resembling goiters (thyroid), namely glands that appear outside: and they are called the two amygdalae: when treated with what we have said regarding division, and they do not heal, then consider.
If it is a hard aposteme of dark color with few senses, do not touch it with iron.
And if it is of red color and the root is thick: then do not touch it even with iron, fearing blood flow, indeed let it be, until it matures. Then either pierce it (the swelling) or it will burst on its own.
And if it is of white color and round and the root is subtle: then it should be cut (incised).
And the operation on it is to consider before the operation if the aposteme has been quiet for a long time and has grown smaller by some diminution: then let the sick person sit facing the sun, and hold his head in your lap: and open his mouth, and have a servant take hold of his lower jaw with one hand, and press down on his tongue with an instrument whose shape is as follows.
Let it be made of silver or brass that is thin like a knife (cultellus).
When you press the tongue with it (the instrument), and the aposteme is revealed to you, and falls upon it through your sight: then take a hook, and pierce it in the amygdala, and pull it out as far as possible towards the outside, taking along with it something from the tunics.
Then cut it (the amygdala) with an instrument whose shape is as follows. It resembles pincers: but its extremities are curved, so that each of them has an acute orifice facing the other, ensuring that it is made of iron (indium) or brass coated with alum.
If however this instrument is not present, then cut it with a lancet, whose form is as follows. It is pointed at one end and not pointed at the other.
And after you have cut one almond, cut the other according to the same shape of the incision.
Then, after the incision, let the sick person gargle with cold water or with vinegar and water.
If there is bleeding, let him gargle with water in which the rinds of pomegranates have been boiled or the leaves of myrtle and similar ones from poplar trees until the bleeding stops; then take care of him until he recovers.
And sometimes boils other than the two almonds appear in the throat. Therefore, cut them as I said in the incision of the two almonds equally.
I myself have been cured of a woman who had a boil that was born in her throat which drew towards the swelling, with a few senses, which had almost closed her throat; and the woman breathed from a narrow opening, and already forbidden her eating, and drinking water; and it had come close to death if it remained one day or two.
The boil had risen so much that it had expelled two branches until they came out through the two nostrils.
I therefore ran quickly and inserted a hook into one of them. Then I pulled it out, and a large piece came out with it.
Then I cut off the piece where it was grasped from the nostril.
Then I made that which came out from the other nostril.
Then I opened his mouth, and pressed his tongue; and afterwards inserted a hook into the boil; then cut off a piece of it, and no more came out except a little blood; so the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water immediately, then she started eating.
I did not cease to cut from that ulcer many times in a long period of time: and the ulcer followed the place which I was cutting until it became too extended and with that [the thing] itself.
I have cauterized the ulcer between the throat.
Therefore, it stood still after [the operation]: then I walked on that side, and I did not know what God did with it after me.
Chapter on the incision of a mouth ulcer.
Chapter XXXVII.
When catarrh descends to the mouth and it ulcerates and is long: then it is called perpendicular; and if it is thick and round in the lower part, then it is called a boil.
When it is cured along with what I have said in the division, and treatment does not help: and you see that the ulcer is warm and has stopped, and is soft: then it should be cut.
And that which is gathered round it and is not long, and is red or dark colored or black, and has no sensation: then it should be cut out. For there is fear for the weak [patient] in it.
Therefore, when you see it according to the way I have said from its whiteness and its length, you should make the weak [person] sit before the sun: and press his tongue with the instrument that was previously mentioned: then fasten a hook in the mouth, and pull it downwards: and cut it with one of two instruments that were mentioned in the incision of two molars.
And it should not be cut from it, unless what is added goes beyond the natural limit without additional [factors].
For if you cut from it more, you will harm the voice and speech.
Then after the incision, use what was said in the incision of two molars: and treat it until it heals.
If the patient is afraid of incision: then it is necessary to use skill in cauterizing him without fear and dread.
The method of cauterization is not other than with sharp water: and it is to place the head of the patient in your lap. Then press his tongue with the instrument as we said. Then take water as I said in the chapter on cauterization and make a not-extinguished lime, do not make it thick nor thin, fill its concavity with this instrument which has this shape.
Let the end of it where the medicine is placed be concave, as concave as the cochlea of a radius.
Place the instrument with the medicine upon the ulcer itself: and let the patient lie down on his side, so that saliva from his mouth runs out of his inner medicine, and something does not fall from it into his throat and harm him.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. And you from above apply it on the ulcer for a first time with the quantity of half an hour until you see it already blackened and quieted by the bite of the medicine.
And if you wish to take a hot iron and roll it over the end of the radius, pour the iron with medicine into the socket above, and insert the radius with the heated iron into the pipe from above until it sticks to the ulcer.
Do this several times until you achieve what you desire from the cauterization of the ulcer. Then let it be: for indeed it burns and falls off after three or four days.
If you need to repeat the medicine, repeat it: and after cauterization wipe the area around the ulcer with a hot iron dipped in butter, and clean the area around it with what remains from the medicine: and let it be washed with cold water.
And it shall be treated from without with cupping glasses, and from within with gargles, until it is healed.
This kind of treatment is more healthful than cutting and farther away from fear.
And sometimes the ulcer is also treated with something more subtle than cautery and cutting; it is treated with fumigation in this manner. Take calaminthe, hyssop, origanum, rutus, thyme, chamomile, abrotanum and similar herbs: and mix them all together, or some of them in a pot, and submerge them with vinegar, and boil; and the pot should be well coated with clay; and there should be a hole in the middle of the pot, over which a concave instrument is placed in this manner.
Make it of silver or brass; and insert the end, where there is a grain, into the mouth of the sick person, until the vapor rises to the ulcer through the tube, until the ulcer is filled with a great deal of smoke.
Then repeat this several times, until it burns.
And beware, do not perform this treatment at the beginning of an abscess. For in most cases, pus is added to an abscess; and it should not be done unless near the decline of the heat of that abscess.
If this instrument is not present to you, then take a reed, and prepare the bark of an ox at its end; so that the bone of the sick person is not burned; because the bark of an ox prevents steam from burning the bone; and this is one of the good treatments with safety.
Chapter on the extraction of thorns and bones from the throat.
Chapter XXXVIII.
Often a bone or a fish spine adheres to the throat, or something else.
Therefore, it is necessary that you extract what appears on it upon which sight falls, after pressing the tongue with an instrument in the sunlight, and it becomes clear to you that it is in the throat.
What is not apparent to you and hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make it vomit before the food is digested in the stomach. Perhaps therefore it will come out the attached thing through vomiting.
Or the sick one swallows a piece of nap or radish root, or a mouthful of dry bread; or takes a piece of soft dried sea sponge and ties it up; then he swallows it. When therefore it reaches the place where there are thorns or bone, and it is extracted, then it comes out.
If therefore it does not come out as we have said: then use an instrument made of lead in this shape.
Let it be thicker than a finger, but have a rounded tip at its end, which he introduces into the throat easily; and let it have its head raised upward.
And let him beware of touching his epiglottis, so that he does not cough, and push with it bone or thorn, or the physician introduces it with his hand.
But what the sick one introduces, that is better: because of his knowledge of the place where the attached thing is located; and he pushes it downward or pulls his hand with the instrument upward, all of it according to its quantity which is prepared for him, until it comes out.
[Section on Extraction of Leeches]
Chapter XXXIX.
When the leech is treated with what I have said in the section on cure with medicines, and it does not work, then consider if in the throat of the sick person, before or after exposure to sunlight, when you press his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
If your vision falls upon the leech, remove it with a small hook or with thin forceps properly.
If it is not possible with those (instruments): then take a concave cannula and insert it into the sick person's throat up to his neck; then insert hot iron into the concavity of the cannula. Do this often, and let the sick person abstain from water all day.
Then let him take a vessel filled with cold water, and open his mouth in it; and rinse his mouth with it, but do not swallow anything from it; and move the water with his hand for an hour after an hour. For the leech immediately lets go when it feels water.
If it does not come out with what I have said, then fumigate the sick person with bedbugs or with camphor with the instrument that I told you about in fumigating the throat.
Do this often, for it will let go by itself.
The method of fumigation is that you take a pot, in which there are live prunes with fire; and the pot should be covered with a lid, in the middle of which there is an opening; and the end of the instrument should be placed in that opening.
Then throw the fumigation and let the sick person place his mouth at the end of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the fumigation does not escape before you know that the fumigation has reached the leech. For the leech will immediately let go.
If it does not fall (the tumor), then repeat the fumigation many times.
The sick man will bear thirst, eat salt and other foods, but drink no water.
Therefore it is necessary for him to go out (leave the house) with this regime.
This is the shape of the instrument with which a leech is drawn from the throat, when it falls upon the eye.
It is like forceps, as you can see, except that this hook which goes into the throat is curved. And its end resembles the mouth of a bird called stork, which has roughness like a file; when it captures something, it does not let it go at all.
Chapter on opening abscesses and their section, and care in general.
Chapter XL (Fortieth chapter).
The species of abscesses are many, according to the remembrance (description) of each one, that is to say, there is one for one in this book; and they differ in their perforation, and cutting open (section) from two kinds.
One of them is of the species of an abscess within itself, and because it encompasses moistness.
The second method is due to places where it occurs from the body.
Since an abscess occurring on the head is another than an abscess occurring in the anus; and an abscess occurring in a fleshy place is another than an abscess occurring in joints: and each of them has its own judgment through operation.
And from abscesses there are those that should not be punctured unless after the maturation of pus in them, and its completion; and from these there are those that should be punctured while raw, and do not mature according to their completion.
As abscesses which are near joints.
Since when an abscess occurs near a joint and prolongs itself until it becomes rotten what is around its circumference perhaps corrupts the ligaments or the nerve of that joint; therefore it is the cause of closer contraction of that member.
Or it is an abscess near the main member; because if you delay puncturing it until it matures, it will harm either the one himself or through the main member.
Or it is near the anus, so puncture it immature; and it is not necessary to puncture a raw abscess, not completed digestion, unless it is near the anus, so that it does not rot deeply, and prolong towards the inner parts of the anus, and become a fistula, or it will be in its end which will not heal.
It is necessary that you know the hour of puncturing an abscess, which has matured according to its completion; and it is in sedation of pain, retreat of fever, and reduction of redness, and pulsation, and acuity of head of the abscess; and the remaining signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same perforation in the lower part of the abscess, and of more prominent protrusion: and let the perforation be directed in the length of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of hands and feet, and places of arms, and tendons, and nerves, and arteries, and finally in all places where there is no reflection.
In those which are reflected, proceed with the perforation according to that limb.
If however the abscess is in fleshy places: then it is better to defer the perforation of it until its digestion has been confirmed, as we said in the supplement.
Because if you perforate it before that, the course of the virus from it is prolonged, and there are many filths and foulnesses, and perhaps its edges harden and its depth increases.
And some abscesses are perforated according to the width of the body due to necessity, or according to that part which the limb requires.
And it is necessary to administer a small perforation for small abscesses, and a large one for large abscesses; or many incisions in proportion to the size of the abscess.
And among abscesses there are some in which the skin must be concave: and it is cut when it has become like a cloth, and it has reached the end that is already dead; such as happens with many, as in buboes.
And among them there are some which are to be cut by a section having three angles. And from this one is cut like the figure of the myrtle leaf.
Like an inguinal abscess.
And among them there are some in which a round incision or crescent-shaped incision is administered, and ones similar to these from the incisions.
That which does not have a head, such as suppurating superficial ulcers, should be pierced with a shallow penetration or only superficially.
When an abscess is large and has collected much pus, it should be pierced so that it does not spread and all the pus is removed at once: rather, remove a portion of it from it. Then, open an abscess until the next day. Then remove some more pus.
Do this repeatedly according to degree, until it comes out: particularly if the patient is weak in strength, or a woman pregnant, or a small child, or an old person decrepit: for animal spirit often dissolves with the release of pus; and perhaps the weak one will die, and you will not receive payment.
Be careful, therefore, to take great precautions in this chapter.
After your piercing, which you perform on these abscesses, it is necessary to clean the wound and think about it. If the wound of the abscess is small or a plain incision, then administer linen strips or an old bandage. If the abscess is large and there are many openings of the piercing, then insert linen into each opening until they meet.
If you have removed part of the skin from an abscess or hollowed it out, then it is necessary to fill it with old bandage, or as when a cloth is sewn, or shorn with linen wool without wetness; and bind it for three days.
Then expel it, and take care of it with what is necessary from ointment until it heals.
If there is bleeding during your operation hour, then administer cold water and vinegar, after which a cloth is soaked; and place it on the site of bleeding many times.
If the bleeding persists, then it is necessary to administer treatment, care, and powders, as I have described in many places of this book, and by division.
If it is winter time and the place of the abscess involves many nerves: then it is necessary to pour hot poultices with wine and oil onto those areas.
And if it is summer and the areas are fleshy: then it is necessary to place hot poultices that have been soaked in water, oil, or wine and oil, and let everything get cold. Until the third day, as we have said, then it is necessary to open and clean the abscess, and administer treatment suitable for its healing until it heals.
Therefore, this is what is generally required for the knowledge of treating abscesses.
According to the method of division, I have already said about every kind of abscess, how it is the pathway for its treatment one by one.
Chapter XL.
Chapter on cutting abscesses that occur on the skin of the head.
Pustules small, resembling nodules, occur on the skin of the head, and are contained by the tunics that resemble pouches, as if they were swollen like a hen's glands.
And their types are many.
Some of them are fatty: some contain a similar moisture to clay: and some contain a similar moisture to ointment and poultices: and those resembling, and some are hard like stone.
And in the cutting of all [of them], and their removal, there is no fear, as long as it does not create opposition to an artery during its cutting.
The operation in their cutting is that you try it with the instrument whose shape comes later, which is called Introductus, until you know what it contains.
For if it contains moisture, then cut it along its length with a surface incision in this manner.
Begin with an incision along the line b to line g. When the moisture is evacuated, then excise the cyst that contains this moisture, and do not leave anything inside it.
For many times it returns if something remains in it.
Then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment if it is present; and if not, in water and salt; fill the wound with it, and leave it until another day. For that which remains from the cyst will corrode itself.
Then again repeat over the wound with the second Egyptian ointment, and the third, if necessary; until you are confident that nothing remains from the cyst, then care for the wound with ointment until it heals.
If the pustule contains a fat nodule: then cut it according to this shape, having the form of a cross; and throw out the uncinis between the two openings of the incision, and excise it from all sides; and strive for your strength in the extraction of the tunica that contains it.
If however an artery opposes you, then do what I shall tell you afterwards.
And similarly [do the same] in an abscess, if it is stone-like, through cutting and treatment as we have said before.
The cutting of a stone-like abscess is easier: since it contains little blood and moisture. And sometimes there are such abscesses [in the head] of certain men, without deep moisture.
This is what it means: because I have cut over an abscess on the head of an old woman, and I found the abscess to be like a solid and hard stone, rough and white, which could not be broken: and if someone struck it with something, he would wound himself.
However, in other abscess cases on the head, except for these abscesses which occur on the heads of children and at the roots of ears, the cutting [of them] should be a surface cut.
Or place a perforation in them always from their lower part, to divert the flow of pus downwards.
Then treat it with what is suitable for its cure.
Chapter on cutting of the Straphules (glands) in the neck.
Chapter XLIX.
These abscesses often occur in the neck and under the armpits and groins: and sometimes they occur in the rest of the body.
And on those which occur in the neck, there is one [type], and many: and they are generated from one another: and every Straphule from them is within its own layer, like in the knots and abscesses of the head, as we have said before.
And the types of these Straphules are many. For from them there are stone-like ones: and from them there are those which contain moisture: and from them there are malicious ones, which do not obey treatment.
In that which you see good arrangement in touch, whose color is evidently close to the skin's and moves throughout all parts, and is not attached with the neck nerves, nor with the tendon, nor with an artery, nor deep: it must be separated by a superficial incision from the upper part to the lower part of the body along line b to line g. And scrape off its entire surface with a knife, or with multiple knives if needed, as we said regarding tumors of the head, and extract it gradually.
And it is advisable not to cut vein or nerve.
Let the forceps not be very sharp, so that it does not injure your hand with the incision or disturb the sick one, and cut what is not necessary.
If you cut vein or artery, it prevents you from operation, then place in the wound sieve crushed or certain powders that dissolve blood, and tie up the wound, and let it be until the sharpness of the tumor subsides and the wound becomes soft or begins to rot.
For the blood is dissolved by tuncica (linen) Redi then to your operation until you finish.
Then ask with your index finger if anything remains of the Strophulus (a small stone) or similar small ones. If so, cut and clean them.
If it is in the root of the Strophulus a large vein: then it must not be cut from its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall by itself without harm.
Then fill the wound with an old cloth that you have already soaked in Egyptian ointment. Then take care of it (the patient).
If the Strophulus is completely cut off, then gather the edges of the wound and sew it immediately when you see that there remains no unnecessary excess.
If you see that there remains superfluousness due to the size of the Suture, then it is necessary to stretch towards cutting its root and pulling it out: and administer the suture as we said.
And that which contains the humidities of the Suture, perforate it with a superficial perforation: so that its maturity appears to you: and place the perforation from what follows below the body, as we said.
Then administer after the perforation linen with ointment, and similar things, so that what remains from corruption corrodes, until when you see the wound already clean: then care for it with ointment of healing flesh, until it heals.
Chapter XLIII.
[Title: Surgery on the Epiglottis due to an ulcer within the throat.]
The ancients said this surgery on the Epiglottis, and I did not see anyone in our land who has done it: and this is their writing.
In those who have a synanchia [a condition where the epiglottis is fixed to the base of the tongue], it is necessary to avoid surgery on the Epiglottis: since no benefit comes from this, because all the veins and lung are weak.
But in those who have a hot ulcer in the mouth, or throat, or both tonsils, when there is no sickness in the channel, it is necessary to use surgery on the Epiglottis, to avoid destruction which occurs from strangulation.
Therefore, when we want to cut the Epiglottis, it is necessary to cut under three or four rings of the Epiglottis, with a small section in width, where it is between two rings in depth, which is the cut in cartilage, not in bone: and this place is suitable for cutting, since it is devoid of flesh, and the vessels of blood are distant.
If the surgeon is afraid, then it is necessary that he should spread the skin of the throat with a hook. Then let him find the skin until he reaches the channel: if he sees anything from it, he should stop the blood vessel.
Then cut what I have mentioned (the channel): it is indicated that from the mucus which comes out of it and with what is torn apart, and with cutting off the voice.
And leave an open wound for some time.
When the danger of suffocation is removed, join together two lips of the wound skin, and sew only the skin without cartilage.
Then administer medicines which make flesh grow, until it heals.
Says Albucasis. This is the summary of the conversation I have told, the explanation is not given unless when they see that one of these abscesses of the throat of the sick has burst open: and the sick person is raised up near death and wants to be cut open to breathe: they go to cut the Epiglottis so that the sick person may breathe over the place of the wound with a certain breathing, and thus be saved from death: and for this reason they commanded to leave the wound open, until the malignancy of the illness is consumed, and the malignancy is this for three days, and as it were itself: then therefore they commanded to sew up the wound, and to take care of it, until it heals.
And this that I have seen myself is that a maidservant took a knife and sent it into her throat, and cut a part of the trachea of the lungs.
And I was called to care for her, and found her moaning, as is the moan of the dead.
So I opened up the wound, and found blood which had come out from the wound to be small. The wound had not drained pus, nor did it suppurate; and the wind issued forth from the wound.
I became anxious over my own wound and treated it until it healed; nothing happened to the servant except a coughing fit when speaking; and she returned after several days to her usual condition.
From this I say: there is no fear in cutting the Epiglottis.
Chapter on the sectioning of a hernia in the throat.
Chapter XLIV.
This protrusion called a hernia of the throat is a large abscess, resembling the body's color; and it occurs much in women.
It is of two types: either it is natural or it is accidental.
In the case of a natural one, there is no congenital defect.
An accidental one is also of two types: one of which resembles fatty knots. And the other type, is similar to an abscess caused by a node in an artery. There is fear associated with it, and it should not be presumed to be cut with iron unless it is small; examine it yourself and probe it with a sharp instrument. If you find it resembling a fatty knot and is not suspended by any veins; then cut it, just as knots are cut; and extract it along with what contains it from the cyst, if it is in a cyst; and if not, then thoroughly examine the entire area. Then care for the place where it was with what is required for treatment until it heals.
Chapter XLV.
Chapter on cutting across nodes.
There are many types of nodes, and I have already mentioned all their kinds in the division; it is necessary that here I explain the difference between a node and an exitus, when there is confusion.
I say therefore, when the heat departs, and the fever, and the strong pains, until the effervescence of superfluity subsides, and the rotting is completed: then indeed the fever and the heat cease.
When indeed the heat is not present, nor the fever, nor the pains, and they are confined by a bag known as kistis, which is their proper container, and it is according to the color of the body; it begins like a chickpea, and it becomes like bataga, and both major and minor.
And they are of two kinds: either fatty: or containing moisture. And the colors of moisture are many, according to what I said in the division.
Therefore, when you arrive at the treatment of the Node, it is necessary to try it out and examine it with the tool called Introscope, according to its form as it will come in the chapter that follows this one.
And the method of examining abscesses and all nodes is to take this tool and insert it into the more moist place that you find in the abscess; then move your fingers slowly with it until you know that the tool has already pierced the skin. Then, lay your last hand according to the measure of the size of the abscess.
Then, remove the Introscope, and observe what comes out with it.
If therefore the running moisture comes out, whatever its color may be: then cut it with a surface incision, according to what I said in the other abscesses.
And if the moisture does not come out in the footprint of the Introscope, then you will know that it is fatty; cut it with a surface incision having the shape of a cross, according to this form, as I have taught you; and suspend it with hooks, and scrape the skin from all sides with ease; and keep the kistis over it if you can so that you may extract it along with the node while it is still healthy.
If a cyst bursts during an operation and it cannot be safely extracted whole, as often happens, then extract it piecemeal until nothing remains of it.
If something remains of it, whether little or much, a node (inflammation) will return more often than not.
If it (the inflammation) conquers you and leaves something remaining: then fill the wound during your treatment with some corrosive, sharp powders; tie up the wound; place upon it a warm poultice of an abscess and care for it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
If the node (inflammation) is large, then make two flaps of its skin and care for it along with that which becomes solidified.
If it (the node) is pulsating or non-pulsating artery, then rush and fill the place with powdered vinegar and leave it tied up for two or three days until the wound begins to rot and the boiling of blood subsides; then return to cut what remains from the node.
Chapter 46.
Chapter on external instruments for cutting and puncturing.
These (instruments) have shapes of probes, and there are three types.
Among them is the large one, among them is the medium-sized one, and among them is the small one.
Make them from iron with squared ends well-centered so that they may enter quickly into an abscess.
And these (probes) are the shapes of experienced ones, and those which pierce or penetrate; one of them is called beris (piercer), and they are three types.
From these are great, middle, and small [ones].
They join together to be incised for abscesses, wounds, fistulas, and buboes from what is between the bones.
And others are round, smooth, and flexible, like the large needles that chairs have, made of citron, or brass, or iron, or silver.
Those that are better are the ones made from citron.
And also (ones) are made of black lead, which join together to test fistulas, whose concave part reflects with their flexibility, so that they reflect with the smoothness of those reflections.
They are again of three kinds. Because there are long ones, medium ones, and short ones, according to the size of the fistula and its narrowness.
The form (of forceps) is of the shape of a pair of scissors, and it has many kinds.
Because there are simple ones, that is, those with one curvature: and they have three kinds as you see, large, medium, and small.
And (there are) blind forceps: and they have three kinds.
And there are forceps with two curvatures: and they have three kinds; and from these there are forceps with three curvatures, and they have three kinds; and all of these are necessary in their place.
And these are the forms of scalpels, with which knots and abscesses are cut and scraped: and they have three kinds; because there are large, middle, and small [ones].
The ends where the cutting is made are sharp, the other ends are not sharp; they are not placed thus except to provide help in scraping knots near fear of incision of vein or nerve: and that the weak may be healed through them, and may find a little relief from burning which he finds during the scraping of abscesses.
They are made of air and resemble Radix (root) from which alcohol is made; at its tip there is a hidden point called Spathulum (spatula), which penetrates to the inner and outer parts as desired, just as you see.
The shape of spatulae hidden among the fingers for incision of abscesses; these are not perceived by the weak; they come in three species: large, medium and small.
The forms of ventosa (sponge) with which blood flow is cut off; they come in three species: large, medium and small.
Make them of air or citron wood, round, shorter than what you see, delicate.
It is necessary that the forms of ventosa are large and small in your possession so that when required you may quickly cut off blood with them and when medicine is not available to you.
However, do not use them for cutting blood in every part of the body, and do not use them except in fleshy parts such as arms, legs, hips, shoulders, breasts, abdomen, groin, and similar areas, from fleshy parts that are wet.
And sometimes they are made into small instruments resembling the core of a fist, according to their shape, which are used for cutting blood when it flows from the place of phlebotomy or incision of vein or artery; and sometimes they are round in this shape.
Chapter XLVII.
Chapter on care for human breasts resembling those of women.
Whenever the nipples of some men swell during sleep (that is, when they begin to dream), until they resemble those of women; and remain corrupt.
Whoever avoids that (swollen nipples during sleep), it is necessary to cut them with a crescent-shaped incision, according to this shape from the line b to the line g. Then scrape off all the grease. Then fill the wound with a medicated ointment. Then gather together two folds of the wound with suture, and care for it until it heals.
If the nipple turns downwards and softens due to its size, as happens with women: then it should be cut into two upper sections, similar in shape to a crescent, each of which is contained by the other at their ends so that the larger line contains the smaller one, according to this shape from the line b to the line g. Then scrape off the skin that is between the folds, remove the grease, and administer what I said about sutures and powders, which is necessary for treatment, until it heals.
If you do not complete the incision that is required of you to cut it (the swollen nipple), either due to the restlessness of the sick person or due to bleeding: then fill the wound with a plaster soaked in a corrosive ointment, and let it be, until it corrodes what remains from the grease. Then care for it until it heals.
Chapter on the Perforation of an Abscess, which occurs under the breast.
Chapter 48.
These abscesses that occur under the breast are of the types of calluses that contain cysts, and those that contain liquids.
Whatever are among those that contain moistures should be scented with a lunar section, according to this form, from line b to line g. When everything that is in the boil is evacuated by pus, then fill it with an old linen cloth and leave it until another day.
Then remove the linen cloth, and treat it with a suitable ointment until it heals.
If the boil is of the kind like knots (Strophules), then cut over it, as we have said in the section on Strophules equally.
If however the wound extends so that it discharges pus, then administer cautery to it, as we have said in what has been mentioned before.
Chapter 49.
Chapter on the incision of boils due to artery and vein.
When an artery bursts and the skin that is above it hardens, a boil often occurs on it; and similarly, a boil and swelling occur in a vein.
And the signs by which it is known that a boil and swelling are due to an artery or vein are as follows: for when a boil is due to an artery, it is long and aggregated in the depth of the body; and when you press the boil with your fingers, it feels like a grating sensation.
And that which is due to a vein is round on the surface of the body.
And an incision on this boil is a mistake, and especially when it is under the armpits, groins, neck, and in many parts of the body; and it is very great. Therefore, its treatment with an iron (i.e., cautery) should be avoided; and what is also present in the limbs or head, it should be avoided.
Cut open the skin incision lengthwise to find that which comes from the swelling of the opening of an Artery. Then open the incision with scissors, afterwards the Artery; and free it from the tunics until it is exposed.
Then insert a probe under it and make it penetrate to the other side; and tie the Artery with doubled thread at two places, according to what I taught you about the extraction of two Arteries that are in the temples.
Then pierce the place between the two ligaments with a lancet until all the blood that is there comes out; and the abscess is dissolved.
Then administer treatment that generates pus until the ligaments fall off; then care for it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If there is an abscess due to a vein incision, then it is necessary that you hold with your hand what is possible from the abscess along with the skin. Then insert a lancet under the place that you hold with your hand and make it penetrate; and let there be a double thread in it until you draw it out from the other side. Then tie the abscess with a good suture; according to what I told you about the suture of the vein, from two parts with two ends of the thread.
If you are afraid that the thread will be drawn out, then insert another lancet with a different thread under the entire abscess near the incision; press, and tie your threads in four places.
Then cut the abscess in half through the middle until what is inside comes out; then cut off the excessive skin and let go of that which is tied to it.
Then place a poultice made of wine and oil on top of the boil that you have immersed. Then administer treatment consisting of liniments and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter L.
On the amputation that occurs from a twisting of the nerves.
As it happens with an aposteme in Artery and Vein, similarly it happens with an aposteme in Nerves: what happens to them by striking, or happens from excessive labor, and similar things: and it most often occurs in places more assisted, or at the heel, and in every place where joints are moved: and the aposteme is severe.
Its color resembles that of the rest of the body, and it is found in various dispositions without pain: and when it is pressed with force, one feels weak, similar to a state of numbness.
And the aposteme is not gathered deep within the body, but it is under the skin, and it moves to every part: it does not reach forward, nor backward, neither towards the front nor the back.
What is on joints from them should not be invaded with iron. Perhaps it may happen that contraction occurs.
However, what is from them on the head or forehead, pierce the skin with a lancet. If it is a small aposteme, then hold it with forceps and remove it from its root.
And if it is large, then bind it with a ligator, and scab it: then remove it, and close the wound with stitches: care for it until it heals.
Chapter LXI.
[Title] On the cutting of an aposteme that occurs in the abdomen.
These grow frequently in the bellies of some men, and in the remaining bodies of them, 'Fungalia', which are called by likeness to mushrooms.
Their root is subtle, and their head is thick, and the lips of them are turned around. It has a small part from it, and there is something from it that is greatly enlarged.
And I myself have seen a man, and in his belly were two 'Fungalia', which resembled mushrooms more than other things: there was no difference between them, they were white and had small roots, the lips of them turned around, and they were swollen, and moisture flowed from them constantly.
I cut them, and one weighed approximately X and VIII ounces, and the other approximately VI ounces. The operation in cutting them is to consider then if he who is sick is weak and humid, and the 'Fungalia' are white, moist, and subtle roots: then cut it with a broad spatula, and have cautionery iron in your presence.
For many times blood is expelled at the cutting of it: therefore beware if blood conquers you, then cauterize it.
If you see one who is sick, fearful and timid about the cutting with iron, then take a well-made wire from lead, and tie it with that 'athelul': its method is as we have said, and release it for two days.
Then add (a substance) to the lead seal. Therefore do not cease tying the lead wire whenever it presses on 'Fungalia', until it is cut off and falls by itself without effort.
If 'Fungalia' is large at its root, then there is some fear and terror in the cutting of it: especially because it is in the belly.
It is possible to cut through its middle. Then cauterize it, so that it does not return.
Then treat it until the wound heals.
And beware not to cut what is of a dark purple color, few senses, foul appearance; for it is a cancerous apostema, and I will come again with the reminder of Cancer after this.
Chapter LII (102 in modern numbering).
Chapter on the treatment of umbilical hernia.
An umbilical hernia occurs for various reasons. Or from fissures that are above the abdomen, from which comes out either the althub (small worm) or intestine, according to what happens in other ruptures. Or from blood that flows from the vein, or from the artery, according to what was mentioned earlier. Or from constipation that has been blocked there.
If it is due to a fissure of the sifac (anterior abdominal wall) and outflow of pus: then its color resembles that of an apostema; it is loose, without pain; and the position appears diverse. If it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then its position is more violently diverse with what we have stated. When you press it with your fingers, it is hidden; then it returns, and possibly there is a sound; and it swells greatly at the opening of the bath, and the pain is severe.
But if it is due to moisture, it is soft; then it does not hide when you press it with your hand, nor does it contract, nor does it swell.
If it is due to blood, then with these signs an abscess appears dark red from the heel.
But if it is due to fleshy matter, then the abscess is heavy, large, hard, and pierces through by a certain quantity.
If it is due to windiness, then when touched, it is soft.
And the operation in this case is to consider if the protrusion of the navel is due to bleeding from an artery, vein, or windiness; then it is necessary to prohibit treatment of it. For there is fear and terror, as I have taught you in the chapter where I said abscesses due to an artery or vein.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to the intestine or tumor; then you must command the sick person to hold his breath and stand extended. Then mark with a cautery around the entire navel. Then command him to lie on his back between your hands. Then circle around with a broad spatula around the navel over the place which you marked with the cautery. Then extend the middle of the abscess to above, with a large hook. Then bind him around firmly with thread or with a silk cord: and let the knot of the bandage be tied in an alenxotate manner.
Then open up the extended middle part (of the abscess) above the ligament. If you find (it) already caught by the ligament: then extract the alenxotati, and insert your finger into it, and push intestine towards the inner part of the belly; and if you find a stone, then take it with a hook, and cut off its excess.
If however, an artery or vein is against (it): then bind it much. Then return to your operation. And take two needles and insert strong threads into them; and insert the needles into the stitches you made around the abscess in the shape of a cross, which you make penetrate (them).
Then stitch the abscess in four places around the needles; and if you wish, remove the needles and leave room for the rotten flesh to extend; and let it fall by itself; or cut it when it becomes soft and rots.
Then take care of (it) with what is necessary from ointments until it heals.
If the protrusion of the umbilicus is from raw flesh or moisture on it, then you must hollow out the abscess as we said before. And remove blood or moisture that you find in it.
Then take care of (it) to close the place.
Chapter LIII.
Chapter on cancer care.
We have said about the species of Cancer (cancer) in division, and how its treatment is with medicines; it must be cautioned against it during its treatment with iron, so as not to ulcerate it. We have also said that Cancer is generated in the matrix (womb), and a cauterization should be avoided in its treatment.
The ancients said that sometimes cancer is in a place where it can be eradicated; such as cancer which is in the breast or hip and similar parts, from detachable limbs; particularly when it is starting small.
But when it grows old (advanced) and becomes large, it should not be approached.
For I could not heal anyone from that; nor have I seen anyone else before me who has succeeded in treating it (the advanced cancer).
And the operation on it, when it is placed as we said, is to go before (excise), and to release a weak one from black choler several times. Then, if you find phlebotomy (bloodletting) in it with obvious fullness.
Then prepare the weak one with a preparation, in which it is located during the operation.
Then cast hooks into Cancer (cancer) that match it. Then hollow out the whole thing from every part with skin (layer), according to examination, until there remains nothing of its roots; and let blood run, and do not cut it quickly, rather press the places, and remove all coarse blood with your hand or as possible there with instruments.
But if a flow of coarse blood from the incision of an artery or vein opposes you; then cauterize the vein until the blood is cut off. Then care for it with the remaining treatment until it heals.
Chapter on Hydrophysis (hydrocele).
Head LIV. We have now spoken about the types of Hydropsis and how water collects; and the signs of all its types, and their treatment with medicines.
That which is cured with iron is only the type of ascites alone; it does not approach iron in the case of tympanitis; neither deeply in the case of hypoascarcia, for that is fatal.
When you have already been treated with this kind of Hydropsis due to tympanitis with medications, and the treatment has not helped, then consider. For if weakness has already come upon the sick person, or there is another illness in addition to Hydropsis, such as cough, or loose stools, and similar ones; then beware not to treat him with iron, for it is dangerous.
If however you see the sick person overflowing with strength, and there is no other illness in addition to Hydropsis alone; and if he is not a child nor an old man; then the method of operation for him is as follows: you should raise the weak person who stands before your hands, and afterwards let another press his abdomen by hand, pushing water down towards the lower part of the chest.
Then take a pointed lancet. Let it have two sharp points, long, and with an acute tip like a lancet. However, it should have something short about it, so as not to penetrate through it during the operation up to the intestine and injure it.
Then think about this. For if the hydropsis is due to the intestines, then you must make an incision of three fingers' length from the navel downwards, along its upper part above the chest.
If however the hydropsis is due to liver disease, then your incision should be three fingers' length on the left side from the navel.
And if its generation is due to the spleen, then let the section be in the right side: and it is not necessary even that it should be a section on the side over which the sick person wishes to lie, so that superfluities do not run to that weak place.
Perforate the entire skin with the instrument. Then insert your hand into that incision and dissect it with the spatula between the skin and the underlying tissue, as if you are excoriating it; let the quantity that is excoriated be equal to a fingernail or approximately so.
Then perforate the underlying tissue until the spatula reaches an empty place; and that is the place of water. Then remove it (the spleen) and insert an instrument into the opening, whose form is this: (Here follows a diagram or description of the instrument.) It is similar to a cannula: it is made of silver, copper or brass, cleaned; at the lower part of it there is a small hole; and on its sides there are three holes, two from one side and one from the other; and the end of it is cut in the manner of an incision like that of a reed, as you see; on the upper end of it is a strap.
For when the instrument reaches water, then it (the spleen) immediately descends upon the instrument; therefore evacuate from the water a quantity of about half an hour.
Because if you evacuate more than is necessary from it, perhaps the sick person dies through resolution of his animal spirit; or he gets a syncope approaching death.
But evacuate from it according to its virtue and according to what the signs of the sick person's condition indicate to you from the force of his pulse and the quality of his complexion.
Then remove the instrument and retain the water.
This is because it (the water) is immediately retained due to the skin which keeps the hole that is on the underlying tissue; about which I said that you should perforate it in this way.
Then repeat the instrument on the second day, if you see that the patient can endure it; and extract also a small amount from water.
Carry out that procedure for some days without fear, and be careful to avoid error; until there remains in the water only a little.
If you fear for the patient and let a large amount of liquid remain; then take care of him with hot sand, much sweating in the bath and sun, and let him fast; and take care of him with strong medicines, until he is cured; and cauterize over the stomach, liver, and spleen, after the extraction of water; as I told you in what went before.
Treatment for infants born in places where their urinary tracts have not been perforated.
Chapter LV.
When a child is born from the womb of its mother, and its head is not pierced, or there is a narrow opening, or it is not in its proper place.
Therefore, it is necessary to help with the piercing of it immediately when it is born, with a sharp spatula very much, according to this form.
Then place a fine nail made of lead into the opening and tie it; hold it for three or four days.

Chapter 62.

A watery hernia is not, unless a collection of moisture in the scrotum white, which is under the skin of the testicle containing eggs; and it is called scrotum.

Chapter 65.
Chapter on the care of intestinal roots.
The outlet of these roots is from the incision which occurs on the extended sifach above the abdomen in the inguinal part of the liver.

These two types of ruptures occur for many reasons: either from a blow, a jump, a shout, raising a heavy object, and similar things.
And the sign is when it is due to the extension of the sifach. It happens gradually over a long time and does not happen suddenly: and it is an abscess turned deep: therefore, because the sifach compresses the intestine.
And its sign is when it is from the section of the sifach, because it causes a sudden intense pain from the beginning: and it is an abscess different, appearing below the skin close by: and this is due to the outlet of the intestine, and its course to the exterior sifach.
And sometimes it comes out with the intestine called zirbum: and this root is called intestinal root, and zirbia: and sometimes it occurs with wind.
And at times feces run into the intestine and are retained there; it is with great danger for the sick, because it causes severe pain, especially when pressed.
And in the treatment of this kind of illness with iron, there is fear; therefore one must be careful about accidents happening in it.
The method of the operation is to order the sick person to bring their intestine back with their own hand to the hollow within themselves, if they obey the return. Then he shall lie on his back upon his neck between your hands; and lift up his legs.
Then extend the skin that follows the skin upward, and cut the skin of the testicles entirely along its length. Then fix two hooks on the lips of the incision, according to what you need to open the incision with them; and let the incision be according to the size, so that it is possible for the egg to come out of it.
Then scrape the scrotum, and what is beneath the skin of the testicles, until the albumen of the scrotum becomes hard from all sides; then insert your index finger into what follows the testicle, into that which is between the albumen of the scrotum, which is under the skin of the egg, and between the scrotums according to, and without adherence to it in the posterior part of the egg.
Then move the right hand toward the inner skin of the testicles; and while doing this, stretch the albumen of the scrotum upward with the left hand; and lift out the egg with the scrotum to the part of the incision, and command the assistant to extend the egg upward; and you separate the adherence that is behind the complete solution.
And search with your fingers whether there is something inside the scrotum from the rolled-up intestine in hard albumen. If you find anything from it, then push it downward to the lower stomach.
Then take a probe with a thick thread made of linen from ten strands, and insert it at the last sifach, that is, the tunica underneath the skin of the testicles following the incision: then cut the ends that project from the thread until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them above others in a cross-like fashion and tie the sifach, which we mentioned is the ligament beneath the skin of the testicles, so that no pus from those vessels can be sent to them: to prevent the development of a hot abscess there. And place another ligament beyond the first one, at least two fingers away from it. And after these two ligaments, release a piece from the sifach beneath the skin of the testicles, as big as a finger. Then cut the rest in a circular manner and remove the egg-like substance.
Then make a cut on the lower part of the scrotal skin from which blood and pus flows, as we described in that which was mentioned before.
Then apply wool soaked in oil to the wound and place the ligament we mentioned. And sometimes burn the white sifach which we described after its incision, to prevent bleeding. It often happens that this occurs. Release the ligament until it falls off by itself.
If the condition does not improve, then fumigate it with hot water, and place on top of what we described until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with the usual treatment for wounds until it heals.
Chapter 66.
Chapter on Ventose Hernia.
In this ventose hernia, I did not see anyone who dared to treat it with an iron.
And indeed they first said, that it is done as we have narrated in Ramice which is with Vite. That is to tie vessels after the section with ease below it; then cut in the middle, and care for it afterwards with what opens itself, until the vessels fall out; and care for the wound, as we have said, until it heals.
Chapter LXVII.
On the disruption that happens in the groins.
When rupture happens in the groins, as we have said, and the place becomes open, and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles; and if it does descend, it is little, and returns at all hours; but if prolonged with it, a fissure is added in sifach until the intestines descend into sifach.
And this happens due to the extension of sifach, which is in the groins, as we have said. That is because sifach extends; then it softens, and the place is massaged, and it comes out.
And its care is with a cautery, as its previous narrative has described.
And sometimes it is cured with iron, according to this method; and it is to lie weak on his back between your hands. Then cut the place of the rupture and protruding, with a cut across its width, according to the size of three fingers.
Then tie off the alisifak and what is beneath the skin until white sifach, which is beneath the skin that follows it, appears.
Then take the cautery and place it on the protruding place from sifach, and press it deeply into the abdomen.
Then take two protruding places on the extremity of the radius from sifach, and join them with a suture; then remove the extremity of the radius.
Do not cut the anus at all, nor stretch the egg, nor anything else, as I have taught you to know in the treatment of intestinal branches.
Then treat that with the remedy for wounds. When you cut the thread, clean it, and restore the wound until it heals.
For indeed, a sisycos (a kind of tumor) is contracted, and there is no swelling due to rupture.
And cautery is better in this place because it is closer to healing.
Chapter LXVIII.
Chapter on the softening of scrotal skin.
The scrotal skin is often softened in some men because the flesh between them becomes soft and its appearance is disfigured.
Therefore it is necessary for the person who is asked to treat this condition to have him lie down on his back, and to cut through all the softened skin over the natural skin.
Then gather the two lips together with suture: and if you wish, or especially if there is excess of softened skin, trim it off using three or four stitches, and sew firmly.
Then cut between the sutures.
Then treat the remaining wounds with remedies until they heal and the thread falls out.
Chapter LXIX.
Chapter on castration.
You should know that castration is prohibited by our law, and because of this I may omit it in my book and there is no need to remember it except for two methods.
One reason is that this knowledge should be in the medical profession when asked about it: and so that he may know the treatment for the condition when it occurs.
And there is another method that we often need for the castration of some animals, due to our needs from it, as for example sheep, goats, cats and similar ones among animals.
I say therefore that castration is done in two ways. Or by attrition. Or by making a cut and dividing it (i.e., surgical castration).
In the case of castration by attrition, the method of operation is: that we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles soften and relax and hang down; then rub them with your hand until they resolve and no longer appear under touch.
In surgical castration, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the scrotum and cut through it entirely over every egg until two eggs come out: then cut where you have scraped off both, and do not leave anything besides the chyle (seminal fluid) that is on the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than the one by attrition: because attrition perhaps leaves something from the testicles, therefore the animal desires intercourse.
Then care for the wound until it heals.
Chapter 70.
Chapter on the care of Hermaphrodites (intersex individuals) in two ways.
A hermaphrodite is male according to two modes. One of them is because there appears in it what follows the space, or in the skin of the testicles, in that which is between two testicles, a figure resembling a female wolf, in which hairs are found: and sometimes urine flows from it, which is in the skin of the testicles.
But in women there is one species, and it is a female wolf on the forehead like small testicles of a man, projecting to the outside: of which one is like Priapus (a mythological figure with an exaggerated male sexual organ) of a man, and two are like two testicles.
And the treatment of the three species (threes types), two from men, and the one species from women, is: because it is necessary to cut into the flesh added, until the impression of them escapes. Then cure them with the treatment of other wounds.
But in the second species of men from which urine flows out, which is on the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is its treatment at all.
Chapter LXXI.
Chapter on the incision of tentigo (an inflammatory disease) and the flesh projecting in female wolves.
Tentigo (an inflammatory disease) is perhaps added superficially until it becomes ugly and the appearance of it becomes foul: and sometimes it swells so much in some women that it extends like it does in men, and reaches to coitus (sexual intercourse).
Therefore it is necessary to hold the superfluity of tentigo with the hand or with a hook and cut into it: and not to go too deep in cutting, especially at the root, so that bleeding does not occur.
Then cure it with the treatment of wounds until it heals.
The flesh that arises is the flesh that is born in the orifice of the womb until it fills itself: and perhaps it comes out to the outside, resembling the tail: and because of this some call the disease "caudatus". It is necessary that we make an incision in it as we do with a tumor, and treat it until it heals.
On the treatment of the Alraqic ulcer, which is not penetrated by the vagina.
Chapter LXXII.
The arteria is that it should be a female's unperforated wound, or it should have a small opening. And it is either natural or accidental.
