Accidental is caused by the preceding illness; and it itself is made either from flesh naturally added, or ifach subtle, or thick; and it is made either in the deep of the womb, or in its sides, or on its top, or bottom; and it prevents coitus and impregnation, and parturition, and perhaps prohibits menstrua.
And the knowledge of this is obtained through the examination of an obstetrician, if the membrane is visible nearby.
If it is not visible, then search for it with your fingers, or with a probe.
If the membrane is from ifach subtle and is near two lips; then, pull it and break it apart.
And it is to place two small pills on top of the lips.
Then place your thumb and index fingers together, and the woman lies on her back with legs apart. Then spread the two lips with force until the ifach subtle is torn and the membrane is opened.
Then take wool and wet it with oil, and place it on the site; let the woman anoint it every day so that the site does not heal in another way.
If the ifach is thick and large; then it must be cut with a broad-bladed leaf of myrtle.
If the membrane is from flesh naturally added; then hang it with hooks and cut it; and have medicines that stop blood flow without constriction, such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and cedar resin mixed with egg white.
Then administer a wide cannula of lead to prevent the wound from healing quickly; hold it for several days; then apply linen cloth, and then care for the rest of the treatment until it heals.
And sometimes a birth in the womb of flesh from other parts occurs: it is therefore necessary that they be cut according to this manner: before there is no abscess, for an abscess that is cancerous in the womb, should not be opposed at all with iron.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the care of hemorrhoids, Attechel and Bothet regarding redness in women's ulcers.
Hemorrhoids indeed are the opening of vein orifices, until much blood runs out of them continually.
Therefore when hemorrhoids persist, they become piles; and I have already said about their species and the signs of them in the division, and now I will say which ones receive a cure, and which do not.
I say therefore that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the womb and are not felt by touch, then there is no cure for them with iron.
But those which are on the opening of the womb, over which there is touch, these are those which can be cured.
Therefore it is necessary to introduce a woman into a cold house. Then extend Attechel with forceps or rough cloth and cut them from their roots.
Then powder over them near the flow of blood from one powder of incision without biting: such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and alum, and similar ones.
Then press his feet to the wall at noon. Then lay her down in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumach, and rind of pomegranates, and vinegar, and similar ones.
Then take barley flour, knead it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on his back.
If therefore blood is cut with it, good; and if not, make the back adhere to bladders, and nipples, without scarification.
Then take wool, and dip it in the juice of tarathit or arnoglossa or alaulat branches (aglanter), Pontic wine, and make it adhere to the loin.
When therefore the abscess is quiet, then care for the place with ointments until it heals.
However, the red one resembles the heads of alhaasse and has a rough appearance.
Therefore it is necessary that you cut what appears from it, according to what I said in thehelil equally; and care for it until it heals.
Chapter LXXIIII.
On the Perforation of the Dead Fetus that occurs in the Womb.
Many species of abscesses occur in the womb, such as cancer, stone abscess, ulcers, adubelati and alekilati (herpes), fistulae, hemorrhoids, ragadiae, thelil, and hot abscess.
And I myself have already said all these diseases and their species, the signs of them, and their treatments in division: it is necessary that I say in this treatise about the hot abscess that occurs in the womb when it is one of the abscesses that collect pus; and know how to make its opening with iron.
Therefore it is necessary that you consider. If then the pain of the abscess in its incision is sharp with striking, and burning, and fever; and you see it turn red; if it falls on sensation, then do not rush with perforation of it: and care for it with that which helps for maturation until when the acuteness of the symptoms subsides.
Then it is necessary that you make the woman sit on a bench which has two arms, and she should recline or lean upon her back, and bring her feet to the lower part of the abdomen: and her hips should be spread open, and she places her arms below her knees, and tie each with a band corresponding to that.
The midwife should sit by the right side, and administer the instrument for opening the womb's opening.
And it is necessary that when you administer this instrument, you mark with the deepest part of the rod of the woman's womb: so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the womb and harms the weak.
If the instrument is deeper than the depth of the womb, then it is necessary that you place pillows on the top of the deep part of the woman's womb: to prevent the entire entry of the instrument into the depth of the womb and to make a loop, which runs in the instrument, from the upper side: and to hold the instrument and for the attendant to turn the loop until the depth of the woman's womb is opened.
When it appears that the baby is about to be born and it is touched with a hand, and it is soft and smooth, then it is necessary that you remove her to the head with a broad spatula.
When the pus is expelled, then it is necessary to place a linen cloth soaked in rose oil or green oil, containing some sticky substance, on the wound: and to place the cloth and make an incision in the depth of the womb.
Place a clean woolen cloth soaked in water boiled with mallow over the womb and the comb.
Then it is cured for two days with an ointment suitable for that until it heals.
And sometimes the matrix (womb) and wound are washed, so that they are cleansed with water and honey: then, with water in which the root of the lily has been boiled, or long aristolochia, return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden internally within the matrix (womb), then it is necessary that you refrain from treating it with iron, rather treat it with what I said in the division section.
Chapter 70.
Part of Obstetrics: How to treat living embryos that have been born abnormally.
It is necessary for an obstetrician to first know the shape of a normal birth.
From these signs it is that when you see a woman being pressed towards the lower part and desires to smell air, and there is lochia on her who is in labor, and she hurries the birth of the embryo: then you know that this birth is according to its natural shape, and its exit is over the head and the second one with it: either suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When you see these signs, then it is necessary to press her abdomen so that the embryo descends quickly.
For when it descends over its head, the second one also descends with it, and it is cleaned from these excesses with good cleansing.
But whoever is beyond this birth, is unnatural, unlawful.
Because sometimes the fetus comes out over its feet, and its body comes out before its head, and its feet and hands one or both: or the head and hands come out: or the navel comes out: and perhaps it turns on its neck, and similar unlawful figures.
Therefore it is necessary for an obstetrician to be wise and cautious in all these matters, and to avoid errors and deception: and I am showing every figure of them, and how there is intelligence in it, and it is indicated by that, and it will stand on top of it.
When the fetus comes out on its own head during natural delivery and it becomes powerful over the woman, and birth becomes difficult for her, and you see that his strength is already weakened: then make her sit on a chair, or women hold her; and fumigate her windpipe with fennel boiled, and with moist oils.
The midwife introduces a small spatula between the fingers and cuts the second finger, and snips it with her nail until what is within her becomes dry; then she presses the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then it is necessary that the woman be cleansed with a fennel mucilage, with sesame oil.
Then command her after the cleansing to be bound; and make her sneeze with pepper and hold her nose for an hour. For the fetus will immediately come out.
If two hands of the fetus come out first, then it is necessary to reduce them gently and slowly with a reed. If it does not obey when introducing, then put the woman on a chair and raise her feet upwards; then strike the chair on the ground; and hold her so that she does not fall during the shock.
If then the hands do not come out and the fetus dies; cut them off, and extract the remaining fetus; tie her hand with cloth, and extract him evenly; for he will come out.
The emergence of the embryo is on its foot. When the fetus comes out on its feet, then push them upwards; then turn the fetus gradually; afterwards extract him evenly.
Then take one foot of his and stretch it gradually.
When they (the instruments) come out up to the hips, then command him (the patient), let it be pressed, and make it sneeze with a powder: it will come out if God wishes.
If it does not come out as we have told (described), then gradually draw back the fetus until you place it in its natural position. For it will then come out easily through delivery.
If it is prevented from coming out as we have told (described): then take althea mucilage, sesame oil and dissolved gum: grind all together well in a mortar using good pounding; afterwards, apply the mixture with a thread to the woman's womb and lower abdomen. Then make her sit in warm water until the afterbirth follows.
When you see that the lower parts (of the woman) are now warmed up, then give her some (substance) from myrrh: and place it under her. When an hour has passed since you gave her the substance, then make her sit on a chair. Then make her sneeze: and hold open her mouth and nose: and press the lower part of her abdomen gently. For the fetus will come out immediately.
The exit of the fetus above the knees and hands. When it comes out in this manner (described), then make her give birth gradually by introducing her hands little by little. Then the woman lies on her back with her feet hanging down: and she lies down on a bed and wraps her hands (around the fetus). Then press gently on her abdomen little by little. Then remove whatever is under the woman's feet from the pudendum, until it is prepared below (in the vagina). If the fetus does not come out, then take her feet and move them forcefully. Then press gently what is above the hypochondrium gradually, until the fetus rises upwards. Then insert your hands and gently press the fetus: and instruct the woman to compress herself until the fetus exits.
The exit of the fetus is wide-spread hanging from the hands. Make an incision for reducing the hand (of the fetus). If it cannot be reduced, then lift the woman and make her walk.
But if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed: and strike her legs violently.
Then apply the ointment you prepared from glue.
But if she receives her labor, then make her sit on a chair. Then strive for the reduction of the hand and gently press the fetus according to its natural shape: and make the woman sneeze, and instruct her to compress herself until it exits.
The exit of the fetus is on its neck, with spread hands, and its face is towards the back of the mother. The midwife must hold the hand of the fetus, then gradually turn it and press it gently with ease.
When it is turned, then place it on the wound that we have mentioned, made of oil and glue.
Then instruct her to move slowly. When you have done that, then make her sit on a chair and instruct her to lean to the right side. Then instruct her to compress herself: and make her sneeze with powder.
The exit of the prepared fetus is on the side. When it descends to the woman's opening in this manner with the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your nail until it is expelled due to moisture.
If the fetus is suspended over the face and its neck, then cut it from the navel so that it is not retained and dies.
Then push the fetus towards the inside until you place it as required; and tell the woman to compress herself several times; for it will exit easily.
Section on Twins or Multiple Fetuses. Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or even four. However, such a thing is rare and unusual.
But five are absolutely beyond nature and do not survive long; and contain them, although they multiply, by the second one; and separate them through a surgical incision (sifach) that distinguishes the connected cord at the navel of each of them.
And sometimes they exit like a single fetus through a natural, easy birth canal; and they exit in an extraordinary way, as we have told.
If some of them are difficult at birth and reach the condition that I have said in unnatural ways (from the figures), then care for them as we have described; and let a skilled midwife be there, and she should do what she does with ease and slowness, and invent according to all possible shapes to prepare herself to save them.
Section on the Recollection of That Which is Formed in the Womb from Embryos, and Miscarries.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or even more than ten embryos are formed in the womb and miscarry; and it has already been proven to me that a woman, while miscarrying, has expelled seven, and another fifteen, all fully-formed.
That which was done by the measurement of a wise man.
Therefore, this entire matter should be known by an Obstetrician. Perhaps it will reach that one similar to it: Therefore oppose to it what is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus, as previously stated in the division of medication, and it does not come out, and you are forced to use surgery with your hand, then it is necessary for you to consider.
If the woman is of good health and not with any accident from which destruction may be feared over her: then it is necessary for the woman to lie on a bed, on her back, and her head should be inclined downward, and her legs raised: and the attendant should hold her from both sides, or she should be tied to the bed, so that her body does not come out during the extraction of the fetus.
Then the mouth of the womb should be moistened with oils, almond gum, and flaxseed.
Then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and gums: then she should insert it into the womb easily. Then she should seek with her the place where she will fix the hooks on the fetus, and places suitable for that.
Therefore consider then, if the fetus is prepared to descend onto its head: then fix hooks in its eyes, or its neck, or its mouth, or its palate itself, or under its beard, or in its armpits, or near the ribs, and under the breasts.
If, however, it is a descent onto its feet: then fix hooks in its chest and the middle of its ribs.
And it is necessary that the hook should be held with the right hand: and she should place her thumb on what is between the fingers of the left hand: and insert with the hand easily, and fix the hook in one of those places which we said, until it reaches an empty space.
Then fix another hook or a third one, if necessary: so that the constriction is equal, and it does not lean to one side.
Then it should be extended with an equal extension, and it should not be an extension only in a straight direction, rather it should be moved to all parts, so that its outlet is relieved: just as it happens when a tooth is extracted for its removal.
And it is necessary for what is between it [the extended part], that the extension be made soft. If a part is retained from it [the extended part], then it is necessary that the midwife insert certain fingers with oil and turn it with them, which is retained.
If, therefore, a part of the fetus emerges, then the hooks should be moved to another higher place: do this until the entire fetus has emerged.
If, therefore, a hand emerges before other parts and it is not possible to return it because of its twisting: then a cloth should be wound around it. Then extract it until when the entire [part] has emerged, cut it at the joint of the foot or the elbow: and thus you should do so with the other hand, and in two feet.
If the head of the fetus is large or it has a twisting in its emergence, or water is collected around its head: then a sharp pointed spatula called Spatumile should be inserted between the fingers and pierce its head and extract the water; or break it with the instrument called Almisdac, whose shape comes with the shapes of the other instruments in the chapter following this.
Similarly, do as follows if the fetus is of large head nature: then pierce it with a cautery called Algengematu; or extract it with misdach, as mentioned before. Then draw the bones with forceps.
If the head emerges and twists at the neck: then it is punctured until the moisture inside the chest is released.
If it is not complicated and does not obey to exit: then cut the head roughly, as much as possible for you.
If below the abdomen is an apostema or it is in him hydropisis: then you must pierce it, until the moisture runs out from it.
If indeed the fetus is above his feet, then the drawing of it will be easy, and its direction to the bone of the matrix will be light.
If however it is twisted in the abdomen or chest: then you must draw it out along with a cloth which you have wrapped over your hand; and pierce the abdomen or chest until what is within them runs out.
If however the remaining limbs are removed and the head returns: then the midwife should insert her left hand. If therefore the bone of the matrix is open, then insert your hand into the depth of the matrix and search for the head with it, and draw it out with your fingers up to the bone of the matrix; then insert a hook in it or hooks two, and draw it out with them.
If the bone of the matrix is twisted, because of a hot apostema which has happened to it: then you should not work on it, but rather administer a solution of moist things, oily; and administer poultices; and sit in waters that soften and moisten.
If the fetus is on its side, then it may be equalized: then administer what we have said for a living fetus.
If that cannot be done, then cut it roughly and draw it out.
And it is necessary not to leave anything from the second part inside at all.
When you complete your operation, then administer what we have said for hot apostemas which occur in the matrix.
If bleeding occurs, then lower [the patient] into warm water and administer the remaining treatment.
I myself have seen a woman, whose womb was dead due to one fetus; afterwards she became pregnant again with another fetus, and that fetus also died. Therefore, after a long time, an abscess occurred in his navel and it became swollen until it opened; and he began to discharge pus.
I was therefore called upon for his treatment, and he was treated over a long period; but the wound did not heal.
I then applied to him some strong adhesive plasters; and bone came out from the place. Then, after a few days had passed, another bone came out. I was therefore amazed when no bone was found in the womb.
Therefore, I thought that the dead fetuses were made of bones.
I therefore asked the wound, and took out many bones, when the woman was in good condition; and she lived for a long time in this state, but emitted little pus from the place.
I did not apply this foreign substance here unless there was knowledge and help for the treatment that is given by the medical artist with his hand.
Chapter LXXVII.
Â§ On the shapes of necessary instruments for extracting fetuses.
The form of the Spiral that opens the matrix.
Here is the form of a Stricture Instrument, by which books are evened, having equally two spiral threads at the ends of two pieces of wood. Nevertheless, this Spiral must be finer than the Stricture Instrument; and it should be made either of Ebony or Boxwood.
And let the thickness of all the wood be about two fingers; and the edge of each of them is like one finger, and the length of each of them is a palm and a half; and in the middle of two pieces of wood there are two additions of the same kind of wood, which have already been fastened to both, whose length is half a palm or less; and the width of each is about two fingers or less.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the matrix, to open it when you turn two Spirals with them.
Another form similar to it, but finer and lighter.
Let it be made of Ebony or Boxwood, according to the likeness of forceps. Nevertheless, at the end of it there are two additions, as you see here above; and the length of each addition is about a palm; and the width of each is about two fingers.
When therefore you wish to open the matrix with it, then make the woman sit on a bed, with her legs apart, opening what is between her thighs. Then insert these two additions together into the matrix; and you hold the end of the instrument below her hips. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with forceps, equally according to the amount by which you wish the opening of the matrix; until the Midwife does what she wishes.
Form of Vertigo other than what the ancients called Form of Pushing, by which the fetus is pushed.
The shape of the Molar-grinder, by which the large head is crushed: and it resembles a pair of forceps, having teeth at its end, as you see.
And sometimes it becomes hook-shaped, like a pair of forceps according to this shape, as you see, having teeth like the teeth of a saw, by which it cuts and crushes.
The shape of the Scissors having one spine.
The shape of the Scissors having two spines.
The shape of the Spatula having two ends for severing the head.
The shape of two Spatulas also broad.
All these instruments are applied, and the more their forms multiply, and the more they are prepared by the craftsman, it is quicker for its operation, and higher in the eyes of men, due to its quantity.
Therefore, do not disregard any instrument, as it may be prepared for you. Indeed, their necessity is unavoidable.
Chapter LXXVIII (78).
Chapter on the Second Extraction (Cesarean section).
When the Second Extraction (Cesarean section) retains during childbirth, then order the weak to hold their breath. Then make her sneeze with powder and press your hand over her mouth and nose. If it comes out through this (the incision), that is good.
If not: then take the pot and pierce a hole in the covering (uterus): and put in there opening herbs, such as camomile, rue, anise, chamomile, wood-ear, centauray: take all these herbs, or some of them, and submerge them with water, and place them on fire.
Then place the bulb of the reed on the opening of the pot's cover, and the other end into the bone of the matrix; and hold it until the vapor reaches the concavity of the matrix.
Then make her sneeze, as we said. For sublingual secondaries, it will come out easily.
If it remains after this treatment and does not come out, then order the Midwife to immerse her hand in sesame oil or marshmallow juice. Then insert [the hand] into the cervix and seek out the Sublingual. When it is found, then take it and gently pull it out gradually.
If it is attached deeply in the matrix, then insert [the hand], as we said, until when you find the Sublingual and draw it out gradually along the correct path to avoid the strong attraction of falling into the matrix; indeed, it should be moved gently to the right and left sides: afterwards, add to the amount of the attraction. It then subsides and is saved, and escapes from the adhesion.
If the bone of the matrix is twisted, as we have already said: treat it with sneezing and medication from the pot with herbs.
If it does not come out with everything that we have said, then take care not to tire yourself by repeatedly attempting the extraction.
However, whatever comes out of the bone of the matrix from there, tie it to the woman's hip. Then enema her with the four-ingredient ointment. It will rot and dissolve after a few days, and it will come out.
Nevertheless, when it rots, the foul smell is raised to the stomach and head, and harms the weak one. Therefore, it is necessary that suitable fumigations are administered for that purpose.
Some of the ancients have already experienced the fumigation of nasturtium and dried figs.
The shape of the instrument used to fumigate a woman during retention of the second birth and menstruation.
Make an instrument similar to an alembic, or from a jar. Place its wide end over the fire, and place the fumigation on plums. Hold it until the fumigation is consumed, then take another one.
Chapter LXXIX (79).
Chapter on the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many boys are born, and the anus of some of them is not perforated, which has already been cauterized with a sharp probe. Therefore, the midwife must perforate it with her finger; and if she cannot, she should perforate it with a pointed spatula, but be careful not to touch it (the rectum) with her hand.
Then put wool soaked in wine and oil on top of it. Then treat it with an ointment until it is healed.
If you are afraid that it will be cauterized (healed), then put a leaden tube into the opening and remove it when the boy wants to defecate.
And now, cauterization of the anus also occurs due to the consolidation of a wound or abscess. Therefore, that consolidation must be cut, then treated with the remedy as we have said for the treatment and lead.
Chapter LXXX (80).
Chapter on the treatment of fistulas that occur in the lower part (of the body).
The fistulas that occur in the lower part are nodes (lumps), and swellings that occur near the anus outside; or in a space of one part; and there is one fistula or more than one.
When therefore the ancient knot is untied, watery whiteness or subtle pus flows out from it.
And sometimes there are penetrating ones among these fistulas. Therefore, those that penetrate are recognized by what comes out during discharge, and its gaseous nature, when the sick person uses discharge; and perhaps a worm comes out from them.
And there are fistulas among these when they penetrate into the space up to the bladder, and up to the meat of the penis. And there are those that penetrate up to the hip joint, and up to the coccygeal node.
From this it is recognized that the penetrating fistula up to the anus can also be recognized by the non-penetrating one, by inserting your index finger into the anus; and inserting a probe made of thin copper or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
If there is tortuosity in it, then insert a thin lead probe or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or hair on your finger.
If you do not feel it all the way through, nor does anything come out of it during discharge, nor gaseousness, nor a worm as I said; then you will know that it is not penetrating; approach then for treatment.
And when the fistula is penetrating up to the bladder or the urethra; then its sign is the outflow of urine from it, and its prohibition is that the location should not be closed with medicine.
But if it is penetrating up to the hip joint or the pelvis; then its sign is that the probe reaches there, if there is no tortuosity up to the bone; and pain in the surrounding area can be found, and pus always comes out from it; and medication cannot be applied in it, nor closed with an ointment.
In these fistulas that penetrate, there is no treatment at all; and their cure is toil and futility for him, upon whom they are formed, by foolish physicians.
In those not penetrating and also not ancient, healing is hoped for with a knife; as I tell you, and I have already tested it; and there lies the sick one between your hands upon his back; and raise his legs up to above his hips, and let his hips be inclined towards his own belly. Then introduce a lead or copper rod if there is a twist in the fistula, until you know where the probe has reached.
If the sick one feels it around the anus, then you must insert your finger into the anus.
If you feel the probe already penetrate itself through the detected fistula, except that you also feel it between your finger and the fistula or flesh; then you will certainly know that it penetrates; therefore do not labor in it, because there is no healing for it, as we have said.
They say that flesh heals in some people and that the remedy by which they hope for help consists of applying a fine cautery to the size of the fistula, as previously described, and then introducing the burning cautery into the fistula until it reaches around the anus. Then repeat this twice or thrice until you know that all the flesh added by filtration, which is similar to a bird's quill, has been burnt up.
Then treat it with linen strips soaked in butter until the burnt flesh emerges; then treat it with ointments that produce and heal skin and make it firm.
If it heals, it is good.
If not, then it will never heal with any other treatment.
If it exits [the anus] and does not reach your finger, which is within [the anus], and there is a thick membrane of flesh or sifak between it and the anus, and you see a fistula in what follows the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you go cutting with the fistula what is in the fistula, until the incision reaches where the edge of the membrane ends, and the membrane is released and falls.
Then clean those fleshy parts resembling the quill of a bird's feather, so that there remains nothing of them.
If blood overpowers you and dissolves between you and your operation so that the fleshy parts cannot be separated, then it is better for what is being done, and more expediently helped, to cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
Because the cautery with fire brings about good results in searing those fleshy parts, burning of these added caruncles, and drying up of blood and moisture.
Then treat it with bandages rolled in butter or softened cabbages until the place emits pus and those seared fleshy parts emerge in the pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments that produce tough flesh; there are medicines containing styptics and astringents.
For when it is restored, then it heals; and do not fear the repetition.
If the fistula has already reached the depth of the anus and is prolonged from the body's excess: then insert your finger into the anus and examine it.
If therefore you feel a membrane, and there is between you and it a membrane from sifak or flesh, and it is close to perforation: then there is no operation on this, unless according to the way of trust and hope.
The substance is, because it is administered in him one of the three methods: either to cauterize it itself, as we said; or to excise it, until you reach its concavity, so that it is possible for you to insert a linen, and cure it from nearby. And do not proceed much with the excision, so as not to cut the muscle containing the anus, and a harmful outcome of evacuation occurs without its will. Then cure that with what I said.
For perhaps it will be cured: or you elongate the skin itself, and clean it after you cut it up to near the anus, as I said, either with a pouch or with another sharp-pointed instrument. Then clean those fleshy parts filtered which are in the excision, up to where you can with examination.
Then try the healing of the whole wound with the excision, and at the superior orifice where it consolidates; and remains a hole opened in the inner part of the anus, and it will be lighter for the sick one.
And sometimes a fistula is sucked out by this method: and it is when you insert the pouch in the fistula: and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with skin and margin of the anus; then take the perforated tip of the pouch, which is like the point of the awl, that is, prepared from calfskin, according to this shape. And insert into it a thread rolled up from five threads, and around there. Then insert the pouch with the thread in the fistula, until you reach its concavity.
If it penetrates into the inner margin of the anus near, then extract the thread from that hole; so that you insert your finger in the anus and extract the tip of the thread, and gather both ends together: and tighten both, and leave it for one day or two days: and as much as the thread cuts into the flesh, tighten it well, until those fleshy parts which are between the two ends of the thread fall down; then care for the wound, until it consolidates and heals.
If, however, the opening of the Fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate in whatever way you prepare, unless it is very deep. For you there is no need to do this for the arm, so that you may not cut it yourself.
Then proceed with it as we have said, until it heals.
The form of the Spatulinis spiny is used to cut the Fistula whose sharpness is very keen, and one part is not keen so that it does not cut what is unnecessary, as you can see.
Chapter LXXXI.
On the suturing of hemorrhoids from which blood flows from their incision, and on the care of fissures.
There are hemorrhoids according to two modes. They are either within the anus, similar to coal-like blisters or prunes, or they are like grains of wheat themselves. And among them there are small ones and large ones; and blood flows from them always, and some are single, and others are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those which are outside the anus are for the most part dry, from which yellow water or little blood flows persistently, and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of that which is within the anus is to order the sick person to fast and rest: and it is pressed out, until it appears from the anus, and is seen by you. Therefore, either suspend them with hooks, or hold them with your nails. Then cut them at their roots.
If they are not held in them by the hooks due to their moisture and softening: then grasp them with a rough cloth or with a comb made of double wool, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them (the vessels), and sprinkle some warm powders over them after the incision to remain in the place of cautionery. Cauterize them according to what was mentioned in the chapter on cauterization. Then care for them with the rest of the treatment until they are healed.
If the anus does not obey to evacuation, then administer a gentle enema to the sick one containing a small amount of purgative, so that it cleanses what is in the anus, and let the sick person evacuate quickly when he releases it.
If the objects are external from the anus, then their nature is light and easy: it is as if you seize them with your nail, or seize them with a tweezers, and cut them. Then care for them with what I have said until they are healed.
And whoever abhors the incision with iron, then it is necessary that you administer suture for them in this way. Take a thread wound around, and insert it into the point. Then extract the objects towards the upper part, and let it penetrate with the point into the root from the other side: and wind up two ends of the thread, on the lower part of the point, and let them be broad: and tie the objects tightly with a strong ligature. Then knot the thread, and extract the point.
Do this with all the objects, and leave one of them: do not seize it yourself, so that excess of blood may flow from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or pitch on the anus and place it on the anus: and command the sick person to rest. Then let him go until he falls asleep.
When the objects fall out, care for them with ointments and the rest of the treatment until they are healed.
On the treatment of fissures. For they often occur due to evacuation of feces and constriction of nature.
When they have been long standing and no medicine is of use for them: then it is necessary to shave with spatula or nail until they become moist, and the upper layer which prevents their consolidation should be removed from them. Then take care of them until they heal as required.
If they do not heal: then sharpen them more forcefully than before, until they bleed much and are opened again, then take care of them until they heal.
On the treatment of sores that are not inverted and those that are inverted, and about scrofula and ants.
Chapter LXXXII.
Know that Almirmar is not anything but a round knot similar to the color of the body, like a nail head: it occurs throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and fingers: and pain arises from them during walking.
Therefore it is necessary to cut what surrounds the nail head and hold it with forceps or a tweezers, and extract it from its root.
Then take care of that, and if you wish to cauterize it as described in the previous chapter.
From scrofula, there is one raised part, a small and rough, filtered, round swelling above the surface of the body. And they often occur on boys' hands.
The treatment for it is to stretch the scrofula and cut into it, or sew it with silk thread, or with hair until it falls off. If you wish, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine, as mentioned before; and now the inverted scrofula and the non-inverted scrofula are removed with an instrument which I will describe.
Formica is also a small pimple that is filtered and coarse on the surface of the body, penetrating deeply; and when it is found cold, it feels like a bite of an ant in it, and it becomes throughout the body; and it mostly happens in hands.
And the treatment of it is that you take a reed from a goose's feather or a strong bird's feather; and place the reed on the pimple, until the circle of the reed contains its parts. Then turn your hand with the reed until it separates what is in the pimple's circuit; and place it in the flesh's depth, and pull out the pimple from its root.
And if you wish, do this with a reed of air or iron, in this manner.
Let the upper end of the reed be pulled to its limit, wrapped in something soft, so that it may be relieved when grasped by the finger and its rotation.
And if you wish to cauterize the pimple according to what was mentioned before in the caution of Athelil, in the chapter on cautery.
Chapter LXXXIII.
Chapter on instruments for administering to fumigations for diseases of the anus, and solutions of the stomach, and colics.
When fumigations are made of silver, gold, copper, or tin-bronze (malachite).
And sometimes one of these instruments is small, and large, according to those in whom it is used.
Therefore, that which is administered for the treatment of small children should be small. And as regards those with weak anuses or painful ones, so too should their clysters.
Large clyster.
The head of the cannula, i.e., the upper part where it is tied to the uterus, should be wide according to this method. It should have a distinction so that it can be tied to the uterus as you see, and its lower end, which is inserted into the anus, should be closed, i.e., not open, soft, very flexible, drawing towards subtlety. And on one of its sides there should be two holes, and in the other side there should be one hole.
And let the size of the hole be according to the thickness of the radishes, and slightly larger than that, and let the uterus in which medicines are placed be that made from the bladder of an animal or from goatskin, which should be small like an asphorate with a root of one palm.
And it should be perforated by many holes as is customary, and the space between each hole should be the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those holes a thread, perhaps made of raw silk, which should be from ten threads or about that, and bind it with it like an asphorate. When the cannula is placed in the uterus, tie the clyster at its head with a strong constriction between two of its distinctions. Then clysterize it (the uterus) with that.
And this is the shape of a circle and holes as depicted here.
The quality of clysterizing with it is: to fill the uterus or bladder with medicine which should be heated according to the tolerance of the sick person, and take care that it is not too hot or too cold.
Then the sick person lies down on his back and raises his legs towards above: and place under him a skin or linen, that is, a hide upon which people lie, or a cloth.
Then pour oil, or lard, or fenugreek mucilage on the extremity of the Clisteris (clisterium). Then insert it gently into the anus. Then let the assistant take the bladder with both his hands and squeeze it strongly until all that is in the clisterium (clisterium) has passed into the intestine.
Then remove the clisterium, and let the sick person raise his legs towards the wall.
If the medicine causes him to discharge, then hold as much as possible. And if he sleeps all night with it, it is more helpful in his recovery.
If the clisterium does not help him with abdominal diseases and he quickly discharges: then repeat the clisterium until he is cured.
If there are hemorrhoids or wounds in the anus: then let the clisterium be very subtle, very soft, from those clisteria with which boys are cleansed.
And this should be the shape of a subtle clisterium, upon which the skin is tightened.
Chapter 84.
I have already said in the division of treating wounds that it belongs to a book, and here I will say about their treatment with hands and with medicine as a supplement.
Therefore, I say that wounds are diversified according to the cause of the wound and according to the place where the wound falls.
Therefore, the causes of wounds are as numerous as the thrown stone: cut with a sword or knife: struck with a spear, stick, or arrow: and similar things from various objects.
Wounds that are made according to the parts of the body are, for example, a wound on the head, or the neck, or the chest, or the abdomen, or the back: and similar ones from these members.
And I am telling cures for some wounds, in order to lay down reasoning and rule for the rest of the wounds.
And I shall begin with simple wounds of the head, since the memory of composite wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say. If there is a simple wound on the head and no bone is fractured, consider whether it was caused by a blow from a stone or similar objects, and only the skin has been broken; and if the wound is large, and you fear an imminent abscess of hot pus, then hasten and make a phlebotomy (letting blood) from the head immediately; do not delay this, and draw out as much blood as the strength of the patient allows, provided there is nothing prohibiting a phlebotomy, especially if little blood is flowing out from the wound. And let the phlebotomy be on the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let the phlebotomy be on the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the weak patient avoid being filled with food and drink, and heavy foods.
If anything prevents a reduction (of the wound), then let there be a reduction in food, and avoid approaching meat or wine.
Place on the wound if a hot abscess occurs, warm compresses soaked only in rose oil or with wine in which there is soap.
If you are free from a hot abscess, then place on the wound if it is recent with its own blood and has not been exposed to air, and then wait a little while, and if the air has already changed, then place some ointment on it until it heals.
If the wound is large or from a sword cut and similar ones: and its edges are not brought together by pits, then gather it up with sutures, as I shall speak about in the wounds of the abdomen regarding their suturing.
If the wound has already been exposed by a bone and is hanging, and there is no retention of it except in a small suspension: then cut it. Then take care of the wound with medicines, and restore the hard flesh to its place in the skin, and tell the weak one to eat thick foods such as heads (of animals) and boiled wheat, until it becomes soft; and similar things.
If you find corruption (rot) in the skin and it is not adhering to bone: then cut away the rotten part, and throw it out; then take care of that.
If, however, in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows, and it cannot be separated by medicines, then ask about the artery. If you find it uncut, then cut it with a spatula or tie it. If there is a need and it does not obey what has been said, then cauterize it until the blood separates.
If these wounds are small and simple, then the matter is easy and light; in such a way that you sprinkle this powder on them: because it solidifies them before they change to air.
Recipe puluellum albi, molae de caule aquileae, et bicarbonatum; Take one part of olibanum (frankincense), two parts of dragon's blood (cruor draconis), and three parts of unquents non extinctae (unburnt pitch); grind all together very finely, and strain it; fill the wound with it and tighten it with a good constriction, until it adheres well above it and coagulates with blood.
Then bind it from above with threads, and leave it alone, do not untie it while it remains, so that it does not become undone. The medicine is not to be removed from him until he is well.
And sometimes a plaster made of lime alone is used when there is no olibanum or dragon's blood available at hand. Even dragon's blood performs the same function in many serious wounds when it is necessary to put it on and bind them, and the wounds are fresh with blood that has not been affected by air.
If air has already affected the wound in some way, especially during summertime, then this powder is not effective. Therefore, treat it as we have said, by putting something digestive ointment over it, or applying poultices made of barley flour mixed with water and honey until pus is emitted. Then treat the remaining part of the wound with the rest of the cure until they are healed.
If a fracture occurs with the wound in the bone, and it is small, then extract it with trephine; I will now speak about the treatment of skull fractures, which follows.
Chapter on neck wounds.
If a wound occurs in the neck, there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple skull wound.
If the nerve or artery of the neck has already been cut, if it is a nerve, there is no skill in treating it except to prevent its intense stiffness with remedies such as zinjar and zegeh, and similar ones. Because they harm the nerves and contract them.
And do not put anything cold at all on the wound because the substance of nerves is cold and they are continuous with the brain, which is above the body's organs; let what is applied for treatment be made from soft medicines like lime mixed with sweet water several times infused with oil or rose oil, or with tuthia when it is also washed with sweet water; and other mineral stones, in this way, as well as moist ointments.
If however the wound is large, then administer suture; or sew together its irregular edges with small catgut. Then care for it until it heals.
If however the wound is deep and there occurs a cavity at its lower part which already collects pus, then open it up more deeply in that place.
If an artery has already been cut in the wound and there is bleeding from it; then separate, or cut it off, and tie it; or cauterize it if necessity requires this.
If however the cartilage of the throat has been cut, either entirely or partially, and the windpipe is spared; then bring together the edges of the skin with suture on top of the windpipe, and do not touch the windpipe; instead lift it up, and place it back in its natural shape. Then close it by stitching with a suitable suture, and let it rest for some days. Then care for it with ointments containing styptics and astringents until it heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then explore it; if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all of them or as many as possible; and what cannot be prepared for removal, leave it until the ulcer rots, separates and drains away naturally.
If the wound is recent, then dust powder over it as I have said. If a bone appears in the wound and a fistula forms; then care for it with the remedy that comes up in its own chapter.
Chapter on wounds in plates or shields.
If it is a wound from a spear or knife; and you can see its depth, then examine it. If therefore a wound discharges pus, when, being ill, one breathes from it, then you know that the wound is mortal.
If it does not have depth and is recent with its own blood: then do not put powder in it from the first hour nor tie it up so that blood is not retained in its depth and returns to the heart and kills the sick one; but put on it attracting ointment, and dissolve it twice a day.
If however ointment is not present with you, then put on the wound's opening an old piece of cotton to absorb what discharges from it by humidity; and make the sick one sleep over the wound so that what collects in it may run off.
If however three days or more have passed from the wound, and no spasm occurs to the sick one nor a bad heart tremor nor difficulty in breathing, and you see that his other conditions are good; then know that the wound is healthy. Treat him then with linen cloths and the rest of the treatment until he is healed.
If however his healing breaks open again and it keeps opening, then know that it has become a fistula. Treat the fistula from its own chapter.
And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and simple on the surface of the chest or back; then treat it with that which came before from suture, if it is large; or with powder, if it is small.
If however it has made an impression on the bone and cut off fragments from it; then look for the wound and rush to extract those fragments if they are separated. If however they are not separated, then leave them alone until the wound rots, for extraction is painful.
Judgement for treating other types of wounds on remaining limbs is the same as what we have previously mentioned.
On abdominal wounds and the evacuation of intestines, and their treatment.
A rupture that occurs in the abdomen can be great, medium or small.
From a great rupture, sometimes the intestine or number of intestines evacuate.
Therefore insertion and stitching is necessary for them, and the stitching is more forceful and difficult.
A small rupture also causes difficulty in a different way. Therefore, the reduction of them is more difficult if you do not hurry to insert it into its place immediately; because it inflates, opens and swells, which makes the entrance difficult.
Therefore, a medium rupture is better because with it the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is in these two types [small and great].
Know that the stitching of the abdomen is done according to four methods.
Two types of stitching are common to abdominal stitching and stitching for other body wounds; and two other types of stitching are specific to other wounds. However, they are more specific for abdominal stitching; and I will tell you one by one with an explanation and clarification.
Therefore, if the wound is small and something from the intestine comes out of it and reduction becomes difficult; then that is due to one of two methods. Or because of the smallness of the rupture, as we have said; or because there is inflation in the intestine due to cold air.
When this is the case, then it is necessary to heat it up so that you immerse a sponge or damp cloth in warm water. Boil in water squill (squinant), daisy (cyperus), spike and broom in it, until the swelling is resolved.
Sometimes this decoction makes wine that has a stypic property: and it is better than water alone for resolving swelling.
When therefore you see the swelling already resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which the wormwood (althea or artemisia) has been boiled, or with mallow (malva). For this purpose an opening is prepared for it with a small instrument.
If however the return (reflux) is lost after this treatment, then close the wound slightly with an instrument for hemorrhoids cutting.
And the first cure is better when it is prepared than section; and there should not be compulsion to cut after necessity and lack of instruments.
Let it have one part that is twisted, pointed, and another part not pointed, and the end should not be subtle like a spatula, rather it should be slightly blunt; and it resembles a shoemaker's awl, as you see.
When the wound is enlarged and the intestine enters, then it should return to its natural shape in its own place, if possible above it; because it is better.
But when the wound is wide at the lower part of the belly; then you must make the weak person lie on his back and place his legs higher than his head. And if it is at the upper part of the belly; then raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts.
And similarly if the wound is on one of the two parts of the belly, then keep your attention and consideration always in this: so that the part where the wound is should be higher than the other part.
And thus it is necessary to apply it to large wounds and to medium-sized wounds.
In small wounds, place it accordingly as it has been prepared for you.
Then make sure that a faithful servant is present among your hands, who holds the entire tear with his hand and brings the lips together. Then take something from it for the one who follows to sew, and this is the common method of suture for one.
And it is that you receive a needle or the number of needles according to the size of the wound. Then let go from the edge of the tear a length equal to a finger, that is, the doctor's; and sew in one needle beyond which you insert the thread into both sides of the skin, with both ends of the sifac (that is below the skin) from within, until you make it pass through from the other side, and you have already brought together the two sides of the skin and the two ends of the sifac; and there are four rows.
Then sew with double thread around the point of the needle several times from both sides together, until the two lips of the wound are brought together by a suitable approximation.
Then let go the thickness of a finger and sew again with another needle; then draw it back with thread, as you did with the first needle. Therefore do not cease to do this with the one you need from among the needles until you complete the closure of the entire wound.
And let the needles be of medium thickness between coarseness and finesse; because fine needles penetrate the flesh too quickly, and coarse ones are difficult to enter the skin; therefore, it is necessary that they be medium in finesse and coarseness.
And it is not necessary to sew the needle in the two sides of the skin that are close together; so as not to penetrate the flesh too quickly and open the wound before its consolidation, and not to elongate when sutured, so that the wound is not prevented from consolidating.
Then cut the end of the onion so as not to harm the sick person during his sleep; and place small cloths around its ends, and leave them until you know that the wound is already healed.
And this manner of stitching with onions is indeed more suitable for small wounds. Because one or two onions, or about the same number, are sufficient for their stitching.
The second stitch is common, where you bring together the edges of four: the edges, two of skin, and two of fat (in place of one), with an onion that has the thread wound equally fine and coarse around it.
Then when you pierce with the onion these four edges, remove the onion from the side where you began, so that the thread protruding from the upper part of the wound falls out; in this way the stitch is made, like a stitch with cloths as they sew clothes, and place between every stitch an amount of thickness equal to that of a little finger.
This stitch is known to men.
And with this stitch I sewed up my own wound which had happened to a man in his abdomen, who had been wounded with a knife, and the wound was larger than a span; and about two spans had come out from the small intestine, and the tear was in the middle of the abdomen.
I therefore sewed it up again when his intestines had stopped coming out for twenty-four hours.
The wound had therefore healed in about fifteen days; and I cured him, and he recovered; and he lived for many years afterwards, converted to his own dispositions.
And the physicians judged that he would not recover.
And it was a miracle that I did not cure it with ointment. Since I was in a place where no ointment could be found nor any medicine. I therefore put an old pot over the wound twice a day and kept washing it with water of honey until it was healed.
I will now describe two types of suture according to the narrative of the speech.
And it is, when you begin with sharp stitching: and you insert the needle from the outside to the inside part.
When the needle penetrates the skin and follows the length and width of the entire body: release the end of the thread on the side where you inserted the needle, and make it penetrate the other end from the inside to the outside at the opposite end.
When you have made it penetrate [the thread], then make it penetrate in the same end as follows: from the outside to the inside; and release the end of the thread on the side where you inserted it, and make the needle penetrate the other end from the inside to the outside; and make the penetration go through with your penetration that you are making in the end of the thread, which is in that part, until it penetrates completely.
Then also begin from the same side, and take hold of it with the end which is on the other side of the thread; and remove the needle from the skin that it penetrated.
Then return it to the same skin, and take hold of the other end of the thread with this end; and remove it from the skin that is on its side, and do the same thing again, and the other, and so on until you secure it all outside according to this example.
The summary of this suture is that you should sew the skin of animals such as hides: in such a way that one end of the thread is on one side of the skin, and the other end is released on the opposite side, until you complete it.
Second type of simple suture, as Galenus said.
This speech is told in such a way as some physicians do it, aggregating all parts to their corresponding part by nature; and they apply the end of the sifac to its other end, and the end of the mirach to the end of another part. And that is done according to what I tell you.
It is necessary that you fix the point of the needle near the end of the mirach on the outer side and let it penetrate to the inside only; and leave two ends of the sifac. Then turn the needle and let it penetrate from the outer side to the inside through both ends of the sifac.
Then turn both and let both penetrate from the inside to the outside through two ends of the mirach on the opposite side.
And this method of suture is better than common easy suture, and it is the suture which is mentioned previously.
Therefore, this is also the speech of Galenus.
And some said. The suture of the abdomen is sewn with two needles. Insert the thread into each of them (the two ends of the abdomen to be sewn) and begin with the insertion of the needle from where it is with you, letting it penetrate to the other side according to the equal stitch of those who sew leather equally.
And know that when the break is in the middle of the abdomen, then the suture of it is more difficult than that of other parts of the abdomen.
The judgment of the dressing of wounds is the judgment of all wounds.
When you catch a fresh wound with its own blood before it changes due to air, and you reduce the intestines, tie them, and prepare them; then place it on powdered meat.
If the wound has already changed (for the worse): then place upon it certain ointments which are present to you, until they cause pus; and let the threads fall out, and may it heal well and be closed up. Then care for that wound as one would care for other wounds, until it is healed.
If there are no medications available to you, then immediately place upon it something old and warm; and change it twice a day as I have taught you, until it is healed.
For you do not need other medicines when the wounds are simple.
If you fear that the wound may communicate with the main limbs upon injury, then it is necessary to immerse a soft wool in warm oil or rose oil; and place it around the areas which are between the groins, and under the armpits.
If it feels pain, or punctures, or rotting in the bowels (for this often happens), then cleanse it with warm stiptic wine, black; especially if the rotting has already reached the intestine, and it becomes a penetrating issue as deep as its concavity.
And know this, that what comes from the large intestine is easier to heal; and what comes from the small intestine, is harder to heal.
The intestine which is called Jejunum does not heal from a wound that occurs in it at all; and this is because of the multitude of its veins, and their size, and because of the subtlety of its body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
If what comes out from the wound is pus, and you follow it recently: bring it back according to your normal reduction of the intestines.
If the specified time has passed and it has already turned green or black: then it is necessary to tie it with a thread above the discolored spot, so that there is no bleeding. In it there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligament and place two ends of the thread hanging from below on the wound side, outside it: to relieve the pulling of it toward you, and to draw out at the risk of the instrument the pus from the wound.
Reminder of a wound that occurs in the Intestine.
When there is a rupture in the Intestine and it is small: then it is possible for some people to be restored: because I have seen one who was wounded in his belly with a spear blow, and the wound was on the right of the stomach, and the wound was old: and it became a Fistula, and exuded feces, and gas.
I therefore treated it until I was not doubtful about its healing: nor did I cease to probe it, until it was healed and the place had become solid.
After I saw the place had become solid, I feared for the weak person, that an accidental evil would happen to him in his belly: and it did not happen to him from that accidental evil. And he remained in better conditions for himself, eating and drinking, urinating, and went into the bath, and was active in his regimen.
And some experimentalists said that when a wound occurs in the Intestine and it is small: then it should be tied up according to this method. It is, that you receive large-headed ants. Then join two edges of the wound and place one ant with an open mouth on the two edges of the wound. When therefore [the] head is placed on it, and the head is tightened, cut off its head, for it adheres, and does not loosen.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not cease to perform this until the ant after the ant according to the size of the whole wound.
Then draw it back, and suture the wound. For these heads remain attached in the intestine until it is fed, and healed, and no harm befalls the sick one entirely.
And now it is possible that the intestine can be tied even with a fine thread; what has been removed from the intestine of the animal, being attached to it when inserted into the point.
And it is to take the end of this thread from the intestine and remove a lot of flesh. Then tie a thread of fine linen at its end. Then insert the thread into the point, and suture it with the intestine. Then draw it back to the rupture.
And this method of suturing with ants and intestine, is not but by the way of confidence and hope.
Know that a large wound, wide, especially if it is in one of the thin intestines; then there is no artifice, nor is its healing altogether.
Chapter on Zuchomen (ulcer) care, and fistulas.
Know that every wound, or abscess when it becomes old and decayed, and becomes an ulcer, and does not consolidate, and always emits pus, and does not heal; then it is called universally in whatever member it may be Fistula, and we call it Zuchomen.
And Fistula indeed is according to truth a knot filtered, hard, white; with which there is no pain, which has the hollow of a bird's feather pen; and for this reason some call it Risati, that is, feather.
And there are certain hours that emit pus, which is moist. Perhaps the moisture splits in some hours. And at times this moisture is abundant and at times it is scant; and it is thick and at times it is subtle.
And now I have passed on to the division [of the subject], when I said wounds; for every sore that does not heal and is not generated within it flesh, is not that except because of one of nine causes.
One of these is when it is due to the scarcity of blood in the body; or its badness; or because within and on top of it there is hard flesh, which prevents the generation of flesh; or because there is much dirt and filthiness; or because the sore itself is putrid and the matter that is sent to it is of bad quality; or because the medicine is inappropriate for its healing; or because corruption falling in the region is a kind of pestilence, as happens in Caesaraugusta, where the digestion of diseases is difficult and healing of ulcers through nature is delayed; or because there is one bone or number of bones.
And I have now shown all these causes and their signs, and the cures of them with medicines in the division; it is necessary here that I make you know the cure for fistula and zucchus, which is done by the way of operation with hand.
Therefore, you should know that fistula occurs in all parts of the body. For from these are fistulae that reach to large veins and arteries, nerves or joints; or intestines, bladder, or one of the ribs; or to one of the vertebrae of the back, or to any of the connecting parts composed of them: such as hands and feet; and from these are those that approach the proximity of a main member and similar ones.
That which is of these fistulas according to this method, is difficult for healing, and does not receive cure, and occupation with it is labor and ignorance.
If it is one of the fistulas whose depth does not reach to those places which I said: and you hope, believe in its cure, and wish to attain knowledge about it, then take a probe made from bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, and examine it with it.
If there is a twist in the fistula, then investigate it with a fine probe made of lead. Because lead, due to its flexibility, can be easily bent according to the twist.
If the fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to sign it with a probe. Cauterize therefore from its openings.
For the moisture with which you cauterize it, goes towards other openings and runs out of them.
Then investigate and inquire according to the way that is possible for you: so that you may know if there is a bone or nerve there, and if the fistula has a deep concavity, far or near; or if it is one with many openings, which stands over all of it, with the greatest strength of your hand, when questioning the sick, and discovering pain upon compression with your hand on the spot, and similar signs and causes of injury.
When you have stood steadfast over all of these with true certainty, then proceed to cure according to your confidence: and consider then if the fistula is near an apparent one, or in a distant safe place away from union, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the places which I have told you; then cut the fistula according to what has been said in my narrative, remove what is in it from filtration and rotten flesh, which is born in its opening out of meat, fat, and similar things; and care for it until it heals.
If a fistula is deep-seated and straight: then it should be cut as deeply as possible for you. Then clean it from all the rotten flesh of its own.
Then wrap a linen cloth around the fistula with sharp medicines and insert it as far as you reach the depression of the fistula with iron: do this frequently, until the sharp medicine corrodes everything that remains in the depression of the fistula due to decay.
Then restore it with unguents which promote healthy flesh until it heals.
But if it does not heal through this, then cauterize it as we have said before.
If the cause of the fistula is bone and it has been confirmed to you: then investigate it and cut it as I have told you; if it does not prevent you from cutting anything from the vein, or nerve, or major limb, as we have said before.
If you find bone and there is something decayed and blackened within it: then scrape it until the decay is completely removed. Then care for it with what cures it to make it heal.
But if it does not heal and emits pus like before: then you know that you have not completely removed the decay.
Investigate further over it, and find out the reason for it and clean it with all your might.
Then restore it. If it heals, it is good; and if not, then you know that the decay is in a deep-seated part of the body which you did not reach. Therefore, you do not have skill in it unless you allow nature to take its course.
If a small bone is decayed and can be reached by you, draw it out with fine forceps that fit the place.
If there are many bones, then carefully draw them all out without leaving anything behind with your strength.
If something occurs to you from the moist parts and there is no fear or mistake in cutting them: then cut those moist parts and flesh, if they are there, and free the bones.
If you are not prepared to remove the bones at your time, then place something over the wound that will rot it and let it go until it rots what is around those bones from the flesh and moist parts.
And keep the wound so that it does not harden. And contract the incision which you cut during your operation. Place over it, if you fear, a piece of copper submerged in crushed sulfur with oil; or a piece of copper submerged in Egyptian ointment, or any green ointment.
For when those moist parts rot and the bones separate from them, remove them and draw out the bones.
If there is a single large bone, such as the shin bone or hip bone and similar ones, and what has been corrupted from it is a large part: then shave it with the final rasp, until that blackness and corruption is removed. Then restore the wound.
If what is in it has become a large part and corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to saw it and cut it completely until the corruption stops; then care for it until it hardens.
And I tell you about a woman who had a problem with her leg: place this example and help for your operation.
A young man of about thirty years had pain in his leg due to a cause that moved within it from inside the body until the matter reached the leg and an abscess formed, which was large; there was no external cause.
The incision has therefore been made at the same time as the error of the physicians, until the abscess was opened, and many materials have gathered together with it. And the treatment of it was delayed until the leg ulcerated, and many openings were made in it: which all emitted pus, and moisture of the body.
Therefore, the crowd of physicians treated it for about two years, and there was no skill in healing hands among them until I was called, and I saw his leg, and the materials that were flowing out from those openings at a great speed: even the whole body of the man had already become swollen, and his color was yellow.
I therefore inserted a probe into one of the openings, and it reached the bone.
Then I examined all the openings: and found that they were penetrating each other from all parts of the leg.
I therefore approached, and cut through one of the openings until I exposed a piece of bone: and I found it corroded: which was already corroded, blackened, rotten, pierced, and penetrated up to the marrow.
I therefore sawed what had been exposed to me, and prepared it from the corroded bone.
And I assigned, that there was no part of the bone except for that corruption, which I had cut off and sawed. And I had already removed it.
Then I placed a restoration of the wound with firming medicines at a distance. And it is not solidified.
Then I tried again, and exposed a second bone above the first exposure: and I found continuous corrosion with the bone: and I sawed what appeared to me also from that corrosion.
And then I attempted a restoration of it. And it is not restored.
I therefore examined it again and did not cease to cut the bone piece by piece, and tried to restore it; and it was not restored until I cut about one palm's length of bone and pulled it out with its marrow.
Then I healed it with medicines, and it was quickly consolidated and cured; and this repetition in the operation and section of it was not necessary, except for the disposition of weakness in the patient, the scarcity of his tolerance, and my fear of death; since it often happened to him at all hours from an excess of evacuation syncopes bad.
It was therefore completely cured; and there grew in the place of the bone tough flesh, and good arrangements were made in his body, and his strength returned; and he turned to his own dispositions; and no harm at all was done to him by walking.
If, however, the projecting bone in the body is already broken; then it is necessary that you bind it thus: and this is to take a ligament, and tighten it at the end of the protruding bone; and order someone to stretch it upwards; and place another thicker ligament of wool around it first. Then bind it over the flesh that is on the bone; and extend its end, so that you may pull the flesh downwards; and you will uncover the flesh over the place which you want to sew, so that the saw does not harm the flesh.
Place a stick or board underneath the bone below; because when you do that, it is not forbidden to cut the corrupted flesh.
And it is necessary that the saw is over the corrupted place a little, so that there is no corruption in the hollow of the bone; and it does not appear to the senses when viewed, and forces another to be its substitute for the saw.
If the bone is corrupt and not projecting, but rather continuous with a part of it, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it: then excise all the flesh from every part. Then place the log below (it).
Next, saw that (part) from the affected side where the corruption is, until it reaches the other side of the incision; and let the saw-cut be shorter than the corruption length, as we said before.
If the corruption is at a joint, cut through the affected joint and saw the bone where it connects from the other side.
But if the corruption is between two joints, then it is not a fracture but an abrasion.
If the corruption is at the beak of the hand or foot: then matters in it are very difficult. However, you must examine the corruption to see how it appears to you. And abrade it, and cleanse it according to any possible arrangement for you, and with whatever skill available to you: when it does not cause you opposition from Vein or Nerve.
And know that the saws and saws for cutting these bones are many according to the position of the bones, their preparation, and their size, sharpness, magnitude, smallness, hardness, and scarcity. Therefore, you must prepare every kind of instrument suitable for the operation.
And know that these operations indicate to you the type of instrument you need, when your study has been prolonged. And the knowledge of the methods of this art is a testimony to the methods of illnesses: then you will find for yourself that which suits it from among the instruments for every ailment.
And I confirm to you at the end of this chapter's number of instruments, which you will place examples upon that you cut into, and a proof by which you test on others.
