Chapter on the Incision of Edges and Sawing of Bones.
Extremities become putrefied either from external cause or internal cause.
When you have treated the corruption with medicines and the cure does not improve and you see that corruption is spreading into the member which it did not affect previously: then it is necessary to cut that member as far as where the corruption appears, so that the weak part may escape death or a greater evil due to the defect of the member.
And a sign of this is that the member turns black until it seems rotten; that fire has burned it itself or it becomes putrid after turning black: until the rot is cut as far as the following member and it creeps throughout the whole body.
Approach therefore with the incision of his, and similarly if the cause of corruption is from the strike of certain venomous things such as the marine scorpion, viper, weasel, and similar creatures.
If the corruption or striking is at the extremity of a finger, then incise the finger, and do not leave room for spreading (of the corruption), until it reaches the rest of the hand.
And similarly if it happens in a hand, then incise it from the root of the wrist, and do not leave room for spreading (of the corruption), until it reaches the forearm.
And if it spreads within it (the wound), then incise the arm at the elbow joint.
If the corruption passes through and you see him about an elbow's length, then it is death of a weak person. And beyond that (the treatment), the amount is virtue (of the medicine).
And similarly with a foot, when corruption spreads to the toe, then cut it at one of the joints; and if it reaches the heel of the foot, then cut off the entire foot. If it rises to the knee, then cut off the leg at the knee joint.
If corruption has already reached above the knee, then there is no help except for release and to leave the weak person to die.
And the manner of cutting a limb, or sewing it is that you bind (tie) the ligament at the lower end, which you wish to cut, and tie another ligament above the place. And let one attendant stretch the ligament to the lower part, and let another attendant stretch the other ligament upward. And you separate the flesh that is between the two ligaments with a broad (blade), until all the flesh is exposed. Then it is cut or sewn.
And it is necessary that you place a clean linen cloth over all the parts and not touch a healthy place with the blade; and for a weak person, an additional injury occurs and a hot abscess.
If however bleeding occurs internally while you are operating, then cauterize the place quickly; or place some powders on top of it that absorb blood. Then return to your treatment, until it is completed.
Then tie the wounded member with an appropriate ligature and take care of it, until it heals.
And I tell you what happened to a man in his foot, the same thing that I told you happened.
It is that, because blackness occurs in his foot, resembling the burning of fire; and the rot starts first in one of his toes, until it began to affect the entire foot.
Therefore, the man came out of himself after he saw the rot spreading in his limb with severity, which he found from pain and burning; and he cut it off at the joint, and he healed.
And after a long time had passed for him, the same rot occurred in one of his fingers on his index hand.
Therefore, he came to me and I attempted to recover the amputated part using medicines on his hand after cleansing his body; but the amputation was not recovered, and it began to affect another finger until the rot affected his entire hand.
He therefore called me to cut off his hand; and I refused it, hoping for a recovery of the amputated part in me; and I also feared death itself for him at the cutting of his hand. Because the man was of great strength.
Therefore, after he had given up on me, he returned to his own land; and he came to me again because he was in a hurry, and cut off his entire hand; and he healed.
I did not bring this narrative unless it should be of help for what falls under the genus of this illness; and in order to signify what is meant, and according to which procedure it is to be carried out.
On the treatment of nosebleeds, and the quality of clysterization with medications.
When a boil occurs in some fleshly members and the duration of the boil extends until it collects pus: then it bursts or is perforated and what is inside the boil exits as pus and leaves a hollow place like a vessel: and the skin that is on top of it becomes thin like a cloth that has been softened: and it does not reach its ultimate corruption, nor presses upon a bone, nor a nerve, nor a ligament: it deserves to be called a Sinus: and it is not named a Fistula: however, if the duration of its hollow space extends until corruption spreads into one of these members, then it is named a Fistula or zuken.
And its treatment is that you should cut the entire skin as it is rolled: and especially when it has become thin like cloth: and trust that it will not adhere to the place because of its corruption.
But if you hope that the skin will adhere and this ultimate corruption does not follow: and if there is a thickness in the skin from flesh: then treat it with Clisterium: and know that it concerns a Sinus.
Then if it is large and the pus that is emitted from it has a foul odor: then clisterize it with medicine from Egypt, which is vinegar, oil, and zinnia, taking equal parts, to be mixed in a jar: and boil them over fire until the medicine turns red: and let it come to the consistency of honey.
Then take what is necessary from it: and dissolve it with water and honey, and clisterize the Sinus with it: and compress its opening, and let the medicine be released into it to the quantity of two hours.
Then remove it along with pus expression: make this daily until the sinus is purified and the stink is removed.
Also, when you are not present for this medication, clisterize with ashes water: and it is to receive the ashes of vinewood, or the ashes from holm oak; and throw water over it. Then wash (it) and clisterize with it until you trust that the sinus is now cleaned.
If the patient cannot bear the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then clisterize it with water and honey, which already has something mixed in of crushed gum. Or clisterize it with honey and wine mixed, because honey has the property to purify and wash (it), and wine makes the sinus sticky, especially when there is an excess of dryness and dryness in the wine.
When you do it several times and trust that the sinus corruption has been removed: then clisterize it with what makes flesh grow in it.
And it is to receive from the ointment dyafinicon: and dissolve it with rose oil and stiptic wine; or clisterize it with certain medications and other unguents whose properties I have written in the treatise on unguents.
If the sinus opening is narrow and cannot receive the clisteris cannula: then expand it slightly with iron; or place linen folded in Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment inside until it is expanded.
And similarly, if the opening is also wide, then join its lips with suture: and allow a quantity for the clisteris to enter without addition.
And similarly, if the opening from which pus flows is elevated to the top: then cut it at a lower place that is within it, so that pus runs out below; because when the pus is constricted in the depth of the sinus, it prevents flesh from growing in it.
If it is not possible for you to cut the bladder about below it as you wish: then try, so that you prepare the member for running out pus with ease according to its preparation for you. Try not to retain anything of the pus within it at all: and take remedies that are put on top of the mark, suitable for what you wish. And stretch them over a linen cloth. And let the cloth be of such a size that there is communication with the entire bladder. Then cut with scissors into the opening of the bladder the hole of the bladder more widely than the bladder opening itself. Then stretch out from soft ointments over another cloth according to the size of the hole: and place it on top of itself at a distance long from the bladder opening, so that the exit of the pus is eased: and do not remove the large cloth unless after several days with one exception.
The one who is on the bladder opening, that is the one you remove at every hour, so that what accumulates in it from the pus may exit: and so that you know if what runs out of it is much or little; or digested or undigested.
And with this repeatedly consider the place of the bladder itself, if its master feels pain there or not; and whether there is a tumor there or not.
When your medication is thus extended and you see the matter that exits from the bladder opening, then you know if the bladder already adheres or approaches to adhesion: then soluble it in the morning, or on the third day: and when you soluble the wound, then change the cloth and renew the ointment.
If it exits from the bladder after a long time subtle pus, then do not despair of its adhesion, for its healing is approaching, because there are people who slow down the generation of flesh in their wounds and there are those who act contrary to this.
If however it comes out from the Sinus after many days as an un-digested pus, then you know that the sinus is not adherent.
If the adherence of the sinus is delayed and prolonged, then add moist medicines in the excision. However, physicians should do this, so that the medicines are moist in substance but dry in effect, such as the unguent dyafinicon, when it is added to it, excess should be avoided from zegi.
And from the remedy that is applied last, it is to receive the unguent dyafinicon, and let it be dissolved with rose oil, and let it be rubbed on top of old wine equal in substance.
Then mix it with that, and use it.
And now this action is similar when you do not have the unguent dyafinicon, honey, when you boil it until it thickens, and use it. Or receive myrrh, aloes, and frankincense: grind all of them, and powder it on top of the honey while it is above fire. Then apply a linen cloth over it, and tie it over the sinus: and line with the honey that you have boiled until it thickens, and powder it over it as a layer, and put it on top of the linen cloth, and tie it up.
And sometimes the following is administered in it: long aristolochia root, celestial lily root, and common lily: and flour of herbs, and chamomile. Use these simple substances or mixed ones, grind them and sift the powder: and powder on top of the honey that I mentioned, and use it.
If the sinus prolongs and is not cured by this treatment: then you know that there is corruption in its depth: either it makes an impression on the bones or on other hard members or ligaments: then cure it with fistula treatment, as was previously mentioned.
On the treatment of corns and worn nails, and the incision and section.
Corns are the lesions that occur under the nail of the thumb or big toe, or possibly on other fingers or toes.
When the matter prolongs itself and is neglected in its care and it is treated with a hot cautery, or it corrupts and emits pus until it corrodes the root of the nail; and perhaps it corrodes it completely, and perhaps the corruption reaches the bone, until there is a foul smell to it; and the end of the digit becomes wide, and its color becomes dark.
When the matter is not cared for as mentioned before, then it is necessary to cut with iron the surplus that remains from the nail. Then cauterize the wound after that. Indeed, cautery is very beneficial.
If the bone is healthy and the nail is also healthy, and empty additions of the nail already press the flesh towards the inside, and begin to pierce it, and wound it; then it is necessary to place subtle Radium under the angle of the nail which pierces the flesh, and push it upwards; and cut the flesh with ease, and place on top of what remains of the flesh from medicines that burn, corrosives, until all of it is removed. Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
If the corruption has already pressed into the bone, then it is necessary to cut the bone and remove it; for the corrupted bone will never heal while it remains there.
If you see the corrosion and corruption advancing in the finger, then cut it at one joint, according to what has been mentioned before about its memory. Then care for it until it heals.
If the nail is rubbed or struck and a very strong pain results, then first apply leeches. Then cut off the nail with the sharp Spathamelus incision from above to below.
And beware lest the incision reach the flesh that is beneath the nail, for you will cause a violent pain to occur over it, and it will become a cause of adding flesh at that place.
Then take care of the spot with it (the oil), so that it alleviates the pains.
The finger that is born in some human hands may perhaps be completely fleshy; and perhaps there are bones in some of them, and perhaps there is a nail in it; and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or its birthplace is in some knots of the finger. Therefore, the one that is born in some knots of the finger does not move; and the one that is born at the joint of the finger perhaps moves.
Its incision (of the flesh-like structure) is easy (to perform). What you should do is to make an incision at its root with a broad spatula.
But the treatment of the one whose birthplace is at the root of the joint is difficult. Therefore, refrain from making an incision on it.
In the one that is born in the finger at the end of the knots, then it is necessary to make an incision into the flesh with a round incision up to the bone. Then saw the bone with one of those saws that fit for it. Then take care of it (the area) until it heals.
Consolidation that occurs in the fingers often occurs either from human birth (that is, it is born with the person), or from consolidation of wounds, burns from fire, and similar things.
Therefore, you must remove that consolidation until the fingers return to their natural form. Then place linen or cloth soaked in rose oil between them (the fingers) to prevent rapid consolidation and separate them; or place a thin lead plate between them until the area is healed as required.
And similarly, if consolidation occurs in certain fingers with the palm, then cut off that consolidation, according to how it is prepared and fits the shape of the member.
On the Vices of Incision.
Uites are swollen veins, large and filled with melancholic superfluities that occur in many parts of the body; and their most frequent occurrence is in the legs, especially in those who travel frequently or work hard, and those who carry heavy loads.
Therefore it is necessary to administer the purgation of the body with strong purges from black bile at times.
Then bleed the patient through the basilica vein.
The cure of them with iron is done in two ways. One way is to make an incision and draw out black blood. A different method is to elevate the vein and draw out all of it.
The section, however, is according to this method. First, irrigate the leg with much hot water until the thick, foul blood is resolved. Then tie the affected leg from the upper part of the hip to the lower part of the thigh with bandages. Then cut the vein at one, or two, or three wide sections.
Then drain the blood from your hand from the lower part of the leg upwards, and it is necessary that the leech draws the blood from the affected person first. Then cut off the nail and continue to drain blood until a sufficient quantity comes out that you can see and that the strength of the affected person can withstand.
Next tie it up and tell him to abstain from foods that cause black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are filled, as this is harmful for the affected person.
The elevation of it, however, is according to this method. If the affected leg has many hairs, shave it. Then immerse it in the bath; or irrigate it with hot water in the affected leg until it turns red and the veins swell; or exercise it with strong exercises if there is no bath nearby until the limb warms up.
Then cut open the skin directly over the vein section along its length; or at the end of it near the knee, or at the lower part near the heel.
Then open the skin with scalpels and scrape off the vein from all sides until it becomes visible to the touch; and when it appears, you will see it turn from red to black. When it has come out of the skin, you see that it is white like a cord.
Then insert the Radium under it until it rises and exits from the skin; suspend it with a blind hook, softly.
Then make another cut near that cut with three fingers. Then scrape the skin from above the vein until it appears. Then raise it with Radii and suspend it with another hook as you did before.
Then make another cut or several cuts if needed for that one. Then scrape and cut it at the very end of the sole (calcaneum).
Then pull it out through the cut that is above it.
And do this until you pull it out through the upper cut or any higher cuts until it completely exits; then cut it.
If it does not obey you to pull and raise it: then insert a strong needle with double thread and tie it, and pull it out; or insert a Radium under it and turn your hand over all parts until it exits. And be careful, it is not cut. For if it is cut, it will be very difficult for you to raise it and a harm will enter upon the patient from it.
When you pull it out completely, then place wool soaked in wine and rose oil or olive oil on the wound site and care for it until it heals.
If the vein is contracted with twists and loops, not as we have said according to straightness: then it is necessary that you find all parts of its twists and the places of its loops.
Then suspend it with hooks until you raise it completely; and be careful at your cut on it not to cut the vein or wound: for it will be difficult for you to raise or pull it out. Preserve therefore your prudence.
The form of the wound heals a vine.
The form of the blind pouch.
It is not like other pouches in that it has no scabbing, nor a sharp end which would wound the vein; rather it is of thick and flexible form, soft; for if it were delicate, it would wound the vein by its fineness; but excessive thickness is superfluous as we said.
On the extraction of a leg vein.
This vein is generated in the legs of warm lands, as Al-Zahgi says, and in the lands of Arabs, and in dry, warm, sparsely vegetated areas, that is, where no herb or tree grows.
And perhaps it is generated in other parts of the body besides the legs.
Indeed its generation is due to the putrefaction which occurs beneath the skin, such as happens within snake and ascariasis worms, and worms generated between the skin and flesh.
And a sign of the beginning of this vein's development is that it occurs in a swollen leg. Then it blisters over. Then the vein begins to come out of that blistered spot, as if from the root of a plant or an animal.
When its end appears, then you should wind around it a piece of lead weighing one keil's drachma, up to two and a half drachmas and nodes; and let the lead hang down from the leg.
Whenever something comes out of it to the outside, wind that up in lead, and tie it. If it prolongs itself a lot, then cut off a part of it and wind up the remainder. And do not cut it at the root before it has come out completely. If you cut, it contracts and enters into the flesh; it causes an abscess to appear, and pus in that place, and a bad ulcer.
Therefore it is necessary that it should be treated gently, and drawn out gradually, until it comes out completely, and nothing remains in the body; and from this vein it flows out in some men which is of its length five palms and ten. And now it has come to me, because it came out from a man of twenty palms.
If it is cut at your time of treatment; then insert a radium into its hole and pierce it with a long hole along with the body, until all that is in it from the matter comes out; and administer the rottenness of the place with medicines for several days. Then cure it with the treatment of abscesses.
And this vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself; and openings occur for it, and a branch flows out from every opening.
Therefore care for it as we have said in the division, and with what was previously mentioned.
Section on worms generated under the skin, and this condition is called Bouina.
This condition is called Bouina in a certain land among us; because it often happens to cows, and there is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh.
And it moves throughout the body, ascending and descending; and it is felt by the senses during its movement from limb to limb until it bursts wherever it bursts on the skin and flows out.
And its generation is from the rottenness of some fluids. As worms and snakes, that is to say, earthworms and roundworms, occur in the abdomen.
And it is feared from his malignancy. Because when he himself moves in the body, and is raised to the head, and reaches the place: then perhaps it opens there, and goes out, and destroys the eye: and this happens frequently.
When therefore one desires to cure him and extract him, it is not done except during his walk and his appearance to the sense.
Therefore, it is necessary that you tie what is above him and what is below him with a strong binding. Then cut above him, and extract him.
If it penetrates into the flesh and you do not find it: then place a cautery over the place with fire until it dies.
And a greater thing that is feared is its corruption, which corrupts the eye, as we have said.
If however you see him already arrived at the head near the eye, then tie below it with a good binding of the eyebrows. Then cut above him, and extract him.
And it is necessary that the sick one use purification of his body with medications that dissolve corrupt, bad humors.
Let him beware for himself from foods causing corruption.
Chapter on the incision due to Nakir's disease.
This disease is called in our land Nakir: it is a pain that occurs in certain members; then it changes from one member to another.
And I myself have already seen it, as I tell you. I was called to a sick woman in certain villages. And she extended her arm and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
And when an hour had passed, I saw a swelling moving with a probe, like a worm, ascending more quickly than possible to the shoulder of that man, as silver runs from place to place.
Therefore, pain left from that place, and it was fixed in the shoulder.
Then it sat for an hour, and it ran to the rest of his body until it reached another arm.
Then he told me that it revolved in his entire body, according to what I saw.
I was therefore amazed at the swiftness of its exchange from limb to limb. And indeed, before that I had not seen this disease in my eyes as it happened in such a way. Nevertheless, I saw many who experienced pain exchange from limb to limb; and I did not see it as I saw it in a woman.
And I do not think that it was anything but because she was one of those who are from dry bodies with dilated veins; hence it appears to be the windiness exchanged (from one place to another).
And it is necessary that it does not appear according to this reasoning in those who are delicate and bodies with hidden veins.
When one desires to cure it and the patient feels that pain; then if it appears to you as we have said, then press upon it quickly and below it; and cut above it until that windiness compressed escapes; and cauterize the place.
If however you do not see it with your eyes; then cure it by means of the body's shaking and what drives out windiness, and mix them with foul pills and pills made from resin and similar substances.
On the extraction of arrows.
Arrowheads differ according to their kinds and the places where they enter the body.
The diversity of them is as follows: for there are those which have large points and small ones; and convex and flat-headed. And among them are those with three corners. And among them are those which have tongues. And among them are those with stars.
However, those which fall upon the limbs, are of two kinds. The limbs are hollow like the main organs such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar ones. When one of these limbs falls and you see signs of death that I will tell you about later, then it is necessary to make an extraction of the arrow from it, for death follows where it is, in many cases. And when these signs are not visible to you and the arrow is not hidden deep within the limb, then extract it, and take care of the wound.
Among the signs of the brain when an arrow falls into it and penetrates the bone and exits through the siphac above the brain are: because strong headaches occur, along with scotoma, vertigo, redness in the eyes, swelling, redness of the tongue, spasms, confusion of mind, vomiting of cholera. And perhaps blood may come out from the nose or ears. And perhaps speech may be cut off and the voice destroyed. And whiteness similar to putty comes out from the wound site. And it resembles the consistency of boiled flesh.
If these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment, and extract the arrow if it does not come out on its own.
The signs of the arrow when it falls into the heart are that it is near the left breast and the person feels as if the arrow is fixed in a solid object, not in an empty one. And perhaps there is movement similar to that of a pulse, and blood runs out from the wound black. Then follows coldness in the extremities, cold sweat, and fainting. Know that death is surely approaching.
The mark of an arrow when it wounds the lung is the appearance of foamy blood from the wound; and the vessels that follow the neck should be cut off, and the patient's color changes. Expires a great and deep breath; seeks the attraction of cold air.
If the arrow falls into the lung, which is in the chest; then it is near the ribs slightly; and a great sighing with violent pain occurs along with a movement of all the shoulder joints.
If the arrow falls into the stomach, then perhaps something undigested comes out from the wound.
If the arrow falls into the abdomen and sticks there, something like feces comes out from the wound, or pus, or an intestine that has already been torn apart. Therefore there is no hope for its treatment, nor in the removal of the arrow.
If the arrow falls into the bladder and comes out with urine; and something goes outside from it, and the pain is greater on the patient; then you know that it is mortal.
The rest of the members, such as face, neck, throat, spatula, help, dorsal vertebrae, crosspiece, thigh, leg, and similar limbs are saved in various ways; when the arrow does not hit an artery or nerve, and there is no poisonous arrow.
And I tell you what I saw about these arrows so that you may know it for your treatment.
It is that a man had an arrow shot into his eye socket of the lacrimal duct and nasal root. Therefore I took it out from the other side, under the cheekbone of his ear; and he was cured, and no harm came to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from the Jew, which had fallen into his eyelid below the lower lid; and the arrow was already concealed, and I could not grasp it entirely, but only a small part of it that adhered to its shaft; and the arrow was large among the arrows of the Turks, with a soft iron, in which there were no ears.
The Jew was then healed, and no accidental harm came to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from the throat of a Christian.
The arrow was Arabic and it had feathers. So I cut through the throat along the middle line; and it was already submerged in his throat. I became sharpened with that, until I extracted it; and the Christian was healed.
And I extracted another arrow from a man who it had fallen into his belly; and we thought he would surely die from it.
After thirty days had passed, and nothing had changed in his condition, I made an incision along the arrow; and I opened it up, and extracted it; and he was healed, and no accidental harm came to him.
And I saw a man who an arrow had fallen into his back, and the wound was solidified over it. After seven years, the arrow emerged at the root of his hip.
And I saw a woman who an arrow had fallen into her belly, and the wound was solidified over it, and the arrow remained within her; and there was no change in her condition, and the woman found no harm in any of her natural operations.
And I saw another man who an arrow had fallen into his face; and the wound was solidified, and remained, causing him little pain; and similar cases there were many of these.
And I removed an arrow from a man among the princes of the King, which had fallen into his nose in the middle and was beginning to deviate toward the right side slightly; and the entire arrow was hidden.
Therefore I was called for his treatment after the loss of the arrow for three days. Thus I found the arrow wound very constricted.
So I investigated it with a thin probe and did not feel it; but he himself discovered a puncture and pain from his right ear. Therefore I hoped that the puncture was at the end of the arrow.
I therefore applied the place with a plaster containing an attractant and digestive properties, confident that the wound would heal and appear as a sign of the arrow for me to cut through; but it did not happen at the expected location, indicating that the arrow had passed through that spot.
I therefore attended him for many days with the plaster; but it did not happen as expected, and the wound was consolidating; and he remained weak from the extraction of it for a space of several days until he felt the arrow within his nose one day. And he told me that.
And he told me that. Therefore I placed on that wound a sharp, corrosive medicine for many days until it opened; and when I investigated it with a thin probe, I felt the end of the arrow adhering to wood.
Then I added this sharp medicine in the wound's opening until the end of the arrow appeared to us clearly; and I passed with him a space of time about four months.
Then when the wound was swollen, and it became possible for me to insert forceps into it, and move it, but it did not obey to exit; then I did not cease to investigate and manipulate on it with various techniques, until on one day I began with well-made forceps according to the shape that will come at the end of the chapter, until I extracted it. Then I restored the wound.
And indeed physicians judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored. I therefore restored it, and the wound healed, and the weak recovered with complete health: nothing at all harmed him.
And I tell you the quality of the extraction of some arrows: so that you may place this rule and significance over what I have not said.
Since the parts and distinctions of this art are not grasped when narrated; nor does that book contain it, and a wise craftsman compares with little over much; and with what is present, regarding what is absent: and he discovers a new operation, and a new instrument in the descent of foreign matters of this art when they occur.
I say therefore that arrows do not leave the members to which they are fastened unless in two ways. Or by attraction from the place from which it entered. Or, conversely, by the part of the opposite side.
And that which leaves where it entered is either a proceeding arrow in a soft place: and it attracts and leaves.
If it does not obey to exit at the hour in which it fell: then you must let it alone for several days, until the flesh that is around it becomes putrid: and its attraction diminishes, and its departure takes place.
And similarly if it penetrates into bone, and does not obey to you for an exit, then let it alone even for several days: and you should touch and move it every day until it departs.
If it does not obey to you for an exit after several days, then it is necessary that you bore around the arrow in the very bone from all sides with a fine awl, until the arrows swell up. Then attract it and draw it out.
If the arrow is already hidden in the body's location, concealed and hidden from sensation: then search for it with probing. If you feel it (the arrow), then pull it out with the instruments suitable for its pulling.
If you cannot pull it (the arrow) because of the constriction of the wound and because of the long arrow deep within; and there is no bone, nerve, or vein there: then sew over it until the wound widens and it becomes possible to extract the arrow.
If there are ears attached to it (the arrow): then free the fixed flesh from them on all sides with all the skill you can; and if you cannot free the flesh through dislocation of the ears or by twisting them, then break the ears until it comes out.
And when you apply the extraction of the arrow, wherever it may be, then use the twisting of your hand with tweezers in all directions until you make it come out; and with the greatest subtlety, so as not to break the arrow, and so that its pulling will be difficult for you, and its own extraction.
If you cannot perform it within an hour, then leave it for several days until what is around it putsrefies. Then repeat it: for the tunica will be relieved, but if it causes a flow of blood contrary to you, then administer what was said in the cure chapter, and keep your power from cutting the vein, or nerve, or tendon.
And administer all ways possible for the extraction of the arrow: and let it be with ease, peace, or slowness, firmness, as I have told you.
And it is necessary that when you pull the arrow, it becomes weak as it was at the time of the arrow wound in him. For it is more beneficial. But if that is not possible for you, then administer what is possible from the figures.
The arrow that comes out from the opposite side of another part, or already proceeds to something on the outside, or makes a hump at the end of the arrow by feeling from the upper part of the skin nearby, and you see it protruding: cut above it, and make the incision according to the size so that forceps can grasp it.
Then pull it out: for it will become easy to come out.
But if it is retained in the bone, then twist your hand according to its roundness until the arrow presses into the bone and enlarges itself: then pull it out.
And if not: leave it for several days: then repeat it until it comes out.
If the arrow shaft is in it, then push it out with it.
But if the arrow shaft has fallen out, and you have the intention to administer a push: then insert an instrument with a hollow, so that it enters the hollow of the arrow: then push it out with it.
If however the arrow is concave, then push it with the instrument as it enters into it. The arrow is pushed through it.
If the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to remove the entire concave flesh, where the venom is: if this can be done by you. Then take care of her with what is suitable for that place.
If the arrow falls into the chest, or in the belly, or in the bladder, or on the side and it is near where you touch with your hand and it can be cut above it: then cut it, and be careful not to cut a vein or nerve and remove it.
Then suture the wound, if you see it, and take care of it until it heals.
And this is the form of Forceps used for extracting arrows.
The tips should be like a bird's beak, which are made of iron: when they grasp the arrow, they do not let it go.
And they are made in many forms: large, small, and medium-sized, according to the size of the arrow, its narrowness, the width of the wound, and its depth.
The form of a Concave Pusher.
And the form of a Deaf Pusher.
This is the deaf tip like a Radius, to push it into the concave arrow and advance it.
Chapter on Phlebotomy of Veins.
Veins to be bled, whose custom is in the body, are thirty.
From which [veins] in the head are sixteen: two pulsating veins, which are after the ears, called two Herbs: and two arteries, which are appearing in both temples: and two veins, which are in both tear-ducts of two eyes, called Looking Ones: and the vein prepared in the middle of the forehead: and the vein at the end of the nose. And two Jugular Veins, which are in the neck. And two veins that are in the upper lip of the mouth. And two veins that are in the lower lip. And these are the veins called Algecherich. And two veins that are under the tongue.
The veins which are bled in the arms, are five veins in every arm.
One of them is Cephalic, and it is on the forest side; and the common people call it vein of the head. And Black (one). And Middle (one), and it is composed from a branch of the Basilic, and a branch of the Cephalic; and the common people call it vein of the body. And Basilic, and it is placed on the domestic side; and it is also called Titillicaris. And the common people call it vein of the belly. And Arm-vein, and it is placed above the elbow; and that is the one which is bled, and it appears above the thumb with a clear manifestation.
And Saviatella (one): and it is the vein which is between the ankle and the little finger; and there are two branches for it.
And in the leg and foot, there are three veins. One of them is a curve under the nail on the side of the little finger. The second one is the saphenous vein, and its location is near the heelbone on the domestic side. The vein of Ness: and its location is near the heelbone on the wild side.
And in the other leg there are three veins similar to these.
Chapter on venesection of two veins after the ears.
Venesection of two veins which are after the ears, is a remedy for ancient catarrhs, headache, migraine, and chronic old wounds on the head.
The quality of venesection is according to what I said previously. And it is, to shave the head of the sick: and rub the back part of his head at the location of two veins with a coarse cloth for good friction. Then, the sick man should tighten his neck with a bandage until two veins appear. And their locations are behind the ears in two depressed areas of the head. Therefore seek them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse of these veins under your finger, mark it with hot wax.
Then take a venesection lancet called the Incisor. Then insert it under the vein into the skin until the venesectionist reaches the bone. Then lift your hand with the vein and skin towards the top, and cut the vein with a cutting incision. And let the length of the incision be the size of two joined fingers or approximately this much, and make as much blood come out as you wish.
Then tie it up with threads and let it heal.
And now the cutting of these [veins] and their cauterization has been discussed at the beginning of the book.
The phlebotomy of the two arteries that are in the temples is beneficial for an old-fashioned hemigraine: and for sodam prauam, and obtalmiam constant; and for clearing away excesses and sharpening the eyes.
And the quality of phlebotomy is as I tell you. Let the sick man tighten his neck much, until two veins appear to the feeling by a clear manifestation; and their pulse is shown under your finger. Then, when the signs are with incense.
Then anoint the skin above the vein with your index finger, and insert the lancet from below, and anoint the vein to the surface. And cut it, as you did in the two other veins; and let blood flow according to your need.
Then loosen the sick man's constriction, and place your finger on the vein at the hour of one. Then place a woolen cloth and bandage on it, and tighten it strongly above; and let it go until it is healed.
And now the reminder of them, their cutting, and their extraction has passed at the beginning of the book.
The benefit of the phlebotomy of the vein in the forehead is after the phlebotomy of Cephalic, for old facial ailments; and for hemigraine, and redness; and for ugly sores.
And the quality of its phlebotomy is as I tell you. Let the sick man constrict his neck with a bandage until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called Fossorium.
Place the pointed end that is on the head of the Fossorium upon the vein, and strike it with a pestle or with another such tool; and let the blood flow according to the amount you wish. Then dissolve the wound of the patient, and tie it until it heals.
And sometimes it is opened with a broad lancet. However, it should not be one of sharp-pointed lancets, like the others; rather, it should have a broad end. And cut the lancet across; since it is near the bone; and perhaps the lancet will break if it is too thin.
The remedy for the two veins that are in the two tear-ducts of the eyes is for an eye with scabies and redness; and to clear the eye, and for diseases of the face.
And the quality of cutting these veins is that the patient ties his own neck with a bandage. Then cut them; and you stand over his head.
And the cutting should be across, short, with a thin lancet and a broad one slightly, for there is no flesh in that place. If the lancet is too sharp-pointed, it may break.
Then let as much blood flow out as is necessary for you. Place a cloth over them and tie them up at night and dissolve them.
The cutting of the veins of the nose serves to alleviate acute fever and violent swelling, as well as facial diseases such as migraines and redness that occur on the face; especially when it is chronic.
The quality of phlebotomy [in this case] is such that it tightens the sick man's neck. Then hold his nose with your left hand, and take a fine and long lancet; and fix it in the middle of the leper's nose, between that part which distinguishes the nose according to its straightness. Because the vein does not appear to the senses there, and because blood begins to flow immediately.
It is necessary that you hold your hand with the lancet for a little while; and make the blood flow according to your need. Then bind it at night. For it heals quickly itself.
The benefit of Guy de Chauliac's two phlebotomies is for the constriction of shortness of breath, and the onset of leprosy, and melancholic ailments, and impetigo and bad ulcers, and corrosive, that is, herpes omenis.
And the quality of these phlebotomies is that it tightens a sick man's neck with a ligation on both sides; and the practitioner stands over the head of the sick man, and the sick man sits on a chair.
Then the vein should be incised to a length proportionate with the wide vein phlebotomy. Then draw out an appropriate amount of blood, or according to what you see, according to the need that is at hand. Do the same with the other vein.
Then loosen the ligation, and tighten two veins with a constriction in the middle; so that the sick man does not faint. And release it until morning. The wound heals.
Chapter on the venesection of Albucasis. The venesection of Albucasis has benefit for alcohol consumption in the mouth, and corruption of teeth, and bad ulcers, and fissures of the lips, and bad ulcers, even those that are in the nose, and around it.
And the quality of phlebotomy is that you make the sick person sit before you; and bind his neck with a ligature. Then turn the lips of him and look at the two veins; one is on the right side of the lip, and the second on the left of it; and the demonstration of both is by blackening them. And that is true: because around those [veins] there are small, black veins. Make therefore an incision on both with a cutting incision.
If there is doubt about you and you do not know which one it is; then turn to the larger incision of them, and make it more evident.
And similarly do the same with the two veins which are in the upper lip; and indeed the custom is mostly with it; and make an incision on the two veins that are in the lower lip.
Section on Phlebotomy of the Vein under the Tongue after Cephalic Phlebotomy. However, the help of the two veins that are under the tongue for phlebotomy is that the cephalic phlebotomy is for the inflammations that are in the throat, and the illness of the voice, and the illnesses of the mouth.
And the quality of phlebotomizing them is that the sick person should sit between your hands before the sun; and pull out the tongue of his, and look under the tongue on one side of his, and on the other side of his a vein; and the color of each declines to blackness.
Make therefore an incision on both; and be careful not to go too deep when phlebotomizing them. For under there are the arteries, and perhaps there may be a bleeding from those arteries.
The three veins that are phlebotomized in the elbow are those whose phlebotomy is customary in all men.
And phlebotomy [is performed] according to two modes. Or piercing with a broad leech (myrtinus) and phlebotomy: or draining to the point of subtlety, using a slit: or cutting with a small knife, and this is called Alnesil. And this is its form.
And from these [methods], there are broad and subtle ones according to the width of the veins and their constriction. The form of leech (myrtinus) phlebotomy is broad, as you see. And it [Alnesil] is suitable for opening hollow veins, full, protruding, apparent, thick ones, and those that contain thick, turbid blood.
And this [method] is smaller in width and more subtle for fine veins.
And it [this method] is suitable for the phlebotomy of fine veins that contain subtle, yellowish blood.
In the abdomen ascending [area], and in the head: the basilica (Basilica) is one of these three veins that benefit from phlebotomy. Because it drains blood from illnesses that are below the throat and neck, because it follows the chest and abdomen: it is suitable for the phlebotomist to bleed this vein, provided that he be careful, since beneath it is an artery. Therefore, if [the phlebotomist] errs and adds in the piercing of the phlebotomy, he will cut that artery, and blood will flow out. Therefore, the phlebotomist must not pierce it [the basilica vein]: instead, he should cut with Alnesil.
If the basilica is not apparent by a clear manifestation, then it must be sought elsewhere, or one should exchange it for another, or find one of its branches: or use the arm vein in its place. The operation itself is clear; cut it with Phlebotomus Anesil, as we said.
If however you want to perform phlebotomy on this same [person], then it is necessary before the tightening of the arm, so that you touch the place, until you know the place of the pulse. Then mark the spot with encaustum (pitch), then the arm, and cut the vein with a curved incision by Phlebotomus Alnesil, as we said. And beware that the blow does not fall into the space from the place of the artery.
And when you see, as you tighten the ligament, swelling at the spot which you marked with encaustum (pitch), then that swelling is the swelling of the artery; therefore avoid it.
If you see blood appearing at the phlebotomy site, as if it were urine of a boy, and it is thin, red: then know that it is from the artery's blood. Therefore, approach and place your finger on the spot for a long time, then remove your finger. If therefore the blood is cut (for it is often cut), then tighten the arm and let it go; beware that the weak one does not move from it, and it should be on guard over it.
And do not move it for several days, until it is healed.
If however the blood does not flow and it overcomes you, and medicine is not present for you at that moment, then cut the artery if it appears to you. For its ends contract, and the blood flows out.
Or take the bark of a fig tree and pound it; take half of it and bind it over the place where the vein was tied with a ligament and small pieces until another day.
Then if blood flows out, it is good. And if not (the case): then care for him himself with the one who preceded him, remembering the place of the dust particles causing blood flow removal; and the removal of his blood is not difficult in many positions, due to the small size of the wound, and the possibility of tying from the arm.
The assistance of phlebotomy for the Vein Fusca is that it draws blood from the upper part of the head and lower body; because it is composed of a branch of Basilica, and a branch of Cephalica, as we said.
And it is appropriate for the phlebotomist to know this vein, since there is a nerve under it. If therefore the nerve is touched during phlebotomy and found, stupor occurs, and healing becomes difficult; and perhaps it will not be healed completely.
And this nerve often appears to sensation. If however it is hidden in some people, and is subtle, and does not show; then you should place your phlebotomy where the vein is phlebotomized, with a section like Alnesil's, and avoid the nerve with your strength.
If the vein is between two nerves, then pierce the vein lengthwise.
Of the Vein Cephalica. The assistance of phlebotomy for the Vein Cephalica is that it draws blood from the head, and contributes to eye disorders.
And in this vein, if you want, it is appropriate for the phlebotomist to anoint it with olive oil or myrtle oil when puncturing; because it is safer than all veins, because it is not under an artery, nor a nerve.
It is fitting for you in phlebotomy that you ask the phlebotomist to take only the head of an arm, and seek a softer place: and it does not harm him if it is not found with the first blow, but he should repeat on it several times with phlebotomy.
Perhaps in some people it may be apostematized when not phlebotomized in the first blow, but the apostema does not harm him at all in any case.
Chapter on the utility of Phlebotomy and the precautions to be observed in it. The quality of phlebotomy, and its accidents from which correction is required, about which you should reflect.
First of all, you should know that phlebotomy is not administered except in the preservation of health and its continuance, and with caution to prevent illness.
And phlebotomy should be performed on one of the three veins that are in the arm, namely the Cephalic, the Flexor Tendon (Fusca), and the Basilic. And phlebotomy should be performed at the beginning of spring after fasting, in summer and autumn, or winter following consumption, when signs of fullness appear.
Phlebotomy should be performed on the first or third day, after three hours have passed since the previous day.
But phlebotomy administered in illness has no fixed hour; it should be performed whenever the situation and necessity require it, day or night, and at any hour, and at any time.
Phlebotomy should not be performed on boys until they reach the age of fourteen. A pregnant woman should not be phlebotomized except from the fourth to the seventh month. Old men who have passed sixty years should not be phlebotomized.
If anyone wishes to be bled for any reason, it is necessary that he cleanses his intestines before bleeding with a lenient enema, if much feces has been retained within them: so that no putrid superfluities from the intestines may attract near the veins at the time of bleeding and harm the main organs.
A patient should not be bled when afflicted with toctina, that is, satiety of the stomach; nor in a state of drunkenness or vomiting until it has passed away from them. A man who is ill with dropsy should not be bled.
Caution should be taken from bleeding again after a colic attack, and vomiting, diarrhea, increase in sexual activity, labor, exercise, wakefulness, fasting, and any other thing that weakens the body or animal strength.
Then consider in detail about humors before this, if the blood is thick with food and drinks, and medicines; if it is possible for him to do so.
Then enter a bath, unless something prevents it; or exercise with some exercise, to make the blood thin.
Place the bleeding of this person in the chest on the third day, as we have said; and strive to expel the chest of that person on that day from all animal ailments such as tightness, anger, fear; and from all bodily ailments such as labor, punishment, excess, and similar things.
And let him have present with him the things that are useful to him from aromatics and fragrances, and cheering things, and similar things, according to their availability in quantity.
Then the bloodletter should sit on a stool that is higher than the stool for bleeding; then he should draw out his arm and rub it with his own hand twice or thrice. Then bind the ligament with a cord and wrap it twice.
And let the ligature be moderate, because an uneven ligature, either by excess in the ligature, then it forbids the course of blood; or by softening, even then it also forbids the course of blood.
Then after ligature, it is necessary that the phlebotomist press his hands together alternately until the veins swell and are revealed to the sense.
Then the phlebotomist cleanses the instrument with a little oil, properly ancient.
Then he places his index finger of the left hand upon the same vein at the place where he wants the venesection, a little; so that the vein does not flee and the blow is confined. Because from the veins you find one as fleeing like an escaping cord at venesection; and there is one which is full of wind; and when you place the instrument upon it, it contracts under the phlebotomist, and the phlebotomist is deceived, and does not open the vein; and if he opens it, it is constricted; therefore for this reason the phlebotomist must be firm and careful in all these matters.
Then lay down the instrument (phlebotomum). If then a vein is opened from one side, it is good. And if not, then do the same on the other side at that place a little; or above it with haste, if the place is not displaced.
What if it is displaced, or the weak person starts and trembles, then let him rest for a day, or two days; and do not bind the ligament. Perhaps the abscess attracts the displacement (calidum). Do not enter the bath.
Then repeat the venesection if it is loved (amat).
If the opening is small, or blood flows subtly: fear that the quantity which you desire will not exit; then repeatedly perform venesection in the same opening and add a little more in the procedure.
Do it promptly before the site is closed, for in many people the closed site is difficult during a small operation.
If therefore you see that it has been closed, then do not go over it at all, for nothing will excuse you in your eyes. Place something from oil paste on it: because it alleviates the flow of blood. And it is better at this site than olive oil itself and other oils.
And likewise administer oil paste in every venesection of your own where you are stopping the flow of blood; and they do that in the East, the Tyrian alfarach and the Sagzena, when it is put on the site.
For the blood is made thin and dissolved when it is thick.
If it happens at the site of venesection a large abscess, which often occurs especially in those who are not a venesection expert except that day, or if the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put a sponge soaked in water and salt, heated slightly, on the spot and press it for one hour; because it dissolves.
And it is necessary that you do this after the blood exits from the vein itself, when it has been completed or from another vein.
If something black or green remains at the site after a few days, it does not harm; and if you want, put something of aloe or myrrh dissolved on it; or something from the juice of mint, that is, camphor or similar to it.
And indeed, abscesses and swellings frequently occur at the phlebotomy sites in the Basilica.
Place your hand upon it; if you find a soft spot under the pressure applied to it, then that swelling is harmful. Be careful, so that you place something on it from what I said. For perhaps blood from the artery will flow out of it.
But make an ointment for it with what I said, so that the place hardens. Then take care of it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
It is necessary that blood be let from every person according to the quantity of its virtue. And what appears as a reddish color on top of the blood.
For if the blood is black, then let it come out until it turns red; and similarly, if you see it thick, let it come out until it becomes thin; and similarly, if it is sharp, let it be removed until its sharpness disappears.
It is necessary for one who is full, strong, and needs bloodletting once to be increased in venesection of the vein, and that the venesectioner be on the left side; and for one who is weak, it should be the opposite of this.
It is necessary that it be let out in the veins and that the opening be narrow; and it is better what is given in venesection of the vein that it be a cross-cut, not a prick.
This method of venesection is safe from bleeding and from nerve injury; and it is more praiseworthy and safer than venesection by length and width.
And for one who frequently faints at venesection, it is necessary to give him a little bread soaked in water of honeyed mulberries or sekanjabin (a type of beverage), if he is heated; and let blood from three or four veins.
If it is of a cold constitution, then let it take bread soaked in syrup of honey, or in syrup of scented honey with spices, or in scented and fragrant syrup, before phlebotomy.
If fainting occurs during phlebotomy and the cause is excessive bleeding: then it is necessary that one drink meat water, subtle scented syrup, and use aromatics with seaweed, and let the chest be washed with it; and let the other things mentioned in the division on fainting from evacuation be used.
He who wishes to cut his arm and let out blood in the second stage: it is necessary for him whose phlebotomy is due to a large evacuation, and the strength of whose arm is weak, that he lets out blood gradually according to the strength of his arm over continuous days.
But he who wishes to cut his arm and let out blood in the second stage, and his body is possibly weak: then let him do this after seven or nine hours following his first phlebotomy.
But he who wishes to draw blood from his body towards the opposite side of where it is inclined: it is necessary that this be done on the second or third day.
In a body where blood is already much heated and sharpened, causing fever: it is necessary that the blood comes out once, and a large amount is extracted; and the opening is enlarged until fainting occurs; after you have observed all conditions of phlebotomy: and place your hand over the pulse of his arm during the flow of blood, so that death does not occur in its place instead of fainting. For it often happens that this occurs when the phlebotomist is unaware and falls because of carelessness.
It is not appropriate when you wish to dissolve an arm, and to dissolve blood when the orifice of the vein has already been closed, and the exit of blood becomes difficult, that you apply forcefully upon it, and the injured one be quickly stretched out. That is very bad indeed, rather let it remain, until it can be bled a second time.
Either remove with sharpness the coagulated part from the blood in the vein's opening, and place something of salt dissolved in water upon it. And place something from turpentine, alfrax or sage root on it, and hold it with gentle pressure until the blood comes out.
If the vein has already burst, then let it be, and do not cover it up until the abscess subsides.
If necessity demands the dissolution of blood a second time, and there is no excuse, then either bleed him in the same place or in another vein in the other arm.

The remedy for the phlebotomy of the saphenous vein is for diseases that are in the lower part of the body, such as uterine diseases, retention of menses, kidney weaknesses, old sores of the hips and legs, and similar diseases.
The quality of phlebotomy is that the ill person should immerse his foot into warm water, and make abrasion on it until the veins swell up; and bind above the joint of the foot with a tourniquet. On ventosation and the quality of its use.
They are made from horns, copper, and glass.
Ventosation is done in two ways. With scratching and bloodletting; the other is ventosation without scratching.
And this ventosation which is without scratching, is done in two ways. Or it is with fire. Or it is without fire.
And the places on the body where ventosation with scratching and bloodletting are administered are fourteen. One of them is the ventosation of Alnocrates, and it is the last on the head; Alkehel, and it is in the middle of the neck; Alhagdahim, and they are two plates on the neck from both sides at the same time; ventosations of the brain, and it is under the jaw in the lower part of the mouth; ventosations of two spoons; ventosation of Alachosos above the tail; ventosations of two nuts, and they are in the middle of two arms; ventosations of two legs; ventosations of two calves.
And Venesection does not draw blood from you from the small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and because of that its power is not lost as it is in phlebotomy. It is not necessary to administer venesection either with fire or without it for any diseases caused by overfilling, until the whole body has been evacuated.
If necessity arises for venesection due to illness or custom, it should be administered at the beginning, end, and middle of every month, and at any time necessary.
Because there are some people who, when their blood multiplies too much within them, find a pain and swelling in their head, and a feeling of heaviness in the limbs.
And among them are those who find overfilling and redness on their face, head, and neck. And among them are those who find itching on their face and forehead, and darkness and confusion in their eyes.
And among them is one who scratches the place of his venesection. And among them is one who laughs too much. And among them is one who tastes blood in his mouth: or the tongue is cleansed and the blood is spit out. And among them is one who has excessive sleep. And among them is one who sees blood and redness in his dreams, dead people, wounds, and things similar to those in waking life.
When we see something of those conditions, and more specifically if it is in the third week of the month: we then prescribe venesection to be done after two or three hours have passed since the day.
The benefit of venesection in the neck is that it relieves headache and that which is drained out goes to the eyes. It is necessary that it [the wound] should be after the evacuation of the entire body.
This is indeed a ventose in place of cephalic phlebotomy.
It is not allowed to use it who has cold constitution or who has catarrh. For it causes him great harm.
Therefore, it is not fitting to use it by the elderly and who have cold diseases of the head.
He who continually does it generates oblivion upon him.
Therefore, you must warn the ventosator to lay down his hand with the ventose for a short while at the lower part, fearing lest it generates oblivion.
Ventosation or alkehel is in place of phlebotomy Fusca, and phlebotomy Basilica, and therefore causes asmati, constriction of breath, breathlessness due to the instrument's fissure, coughing, and repletion.
It is necessary to push the ventose alkehel for a short time, because if it is placed lower, it generates weakness of the heart and stomach.
Ventosation alhagdahim causes accidents of pain in the head, migraine, hemigraina, perforation, and tooth root pain; it is in place of phlebotomy Basilica.
You must warn the ventosator not to press his hand with the scarification, lest he cut an artery and cause bleeding.
Ventosation under the chin causes alcohol in the mouth, corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; it stands for phlebotomy alieherich, which are in the two lips.
Ventosation with spatulas causes alchafacha, which comes from compression and heat.
Interior partitions' ventositation provides aid to phlebotomy of three veins, Basilica, Fusca and Cephalica; since it draws blood from all those small veins which are in the flesh, and those small veins draw blood from larger ones unto themselves until the attraction reaches to three veins.
It is necessary that you warn the Ventosator not to proceed too far in scarification; because there is a place denuded of flesh under which are nerves and arteries.
The ventosa that sucks on the anus provides help for hemorrhoids of the anus and for lower ulcers.
It is necessary that you warn the Ventosator to have a large ventosa and made of metal; because the place requires strong suction, and perhaps small ventosas break easily: and it should be scarified with a large scarifier.
The ventosae of the legs diminish clearly; because they draw blood from all over the body, and they bring old pains to kidneys, womb and bladder: they provoke menstruation, and they bring forth wind and phlegm: and they are in place of phlebotomy for two saphenas and alhorcobeni.
However, they weaken the body greatly, and cause fainting in many people.
The help of the ventosae of alhorcobeni is nearly the same as that of the ventosae of two legs.
The quality of the position of the ventosae is that you place the ventosa first in a vacant place and suck with moderate suction: and do not prolong the position of the ventosae, but put them quickly, and remove them quickly, so that fluids come to the location at an equal rate: and do not cease to repeat this and continue until you see the place already redden and swell, and redness of blood appears: then scarify, and repeat the suction gradually. Then consider in the arrangement of bodies.
For a person who is from soft flesh and sparse pores, it is necessary to scarify him once, not more: so that the location does not ulcerate.
And command the Fan to expand the scarification and not to make it too deep: and moderate the suction in ease, speed, and gentle motion.
If there is thickening of blood, then it is necessary to scarify him twice. In the first instance, an opening is made for the subtlety of blood and its thickening: and in the second, a detailed examination is made for the extraction of thick blood.
But if the blood is very fetid, then the scarification should be done in the third instance: so that it follows the last.
And finally, when we wish to draw blood slowly or slightly, a single scarification is sufficient for us. But if we want the extraction of much blood, we scarify with multiple scarifications.
And if we measure that the blood is thick: then it is necessary to be scarified with a deep scarification: and the end equal in the scarification, is the depth of skin.

And if it is in winter time, then use oil of narcissus, or oil of lily, or oil of chamomile, or sarbatinum; and similar things.
If there is excessive fat, cold: then use oil of amaracus, or oil of balsam, or oil of white poppy, or oil of dittany; and similar things.
If the wind-pipe is stopped by narrow passages of flesh: then it should be prohibited from oil, and those places should be washed with rose water, or cold water, or salt water, or water of cucumber, or water of purslane; and similar things.
But the one whose blood has much moisture, should wash the wind-pipes with vinegar or water of myrtle, and sumac; and similar things.
For the one whose excessive fat is coarse, wash the wind-pipes with old wine or water of sage, or infusion of dittany, or chamomile; and similar things.
And it should be cautioned against wind-pipes treatment in the bath or near the bath, indeed it should be administered after leaving the bath for an hour, or for two hours.
And it is not allowed that someone sleeps after wind-pipe treatment.
What is to be done before treating the wind-pipe, or phlebotomy?

It is not necessary to take it in a hot drink.
Chapter on Venesection without Scarification. Venesections which are without scarification are those placed on the liver, spleen, foot, stomach, navel, and flanks of the kidneys, and anus: because these members do not bear scarification upon them.
Nor is it sought through them, except for the drawing of blood from one member to another; such as placing a venesection on the breasts in the sickness of nasal bleeding. And we use them to relieve cold and unbearable venosity in one member by another; such as placing a venesection on the stomach, and navel. For it makes the member thin, warms it, and removes pain because it has resolved that venosity.
Also it is placed on the kidneys, when there occurs in them an abscess or a stone. By virtue of its own attractive force, it possibly opens an abscess, or extracts a stone from its place.
Likewise it does when it is placed over the spleen, and for grinding the liver or spleen on either side in case of windiness.
These [windy conditions] are treated in vacuums during operation only. And at times they are administered with fire.
And at times they are administered with warm water in pleurisy diseases: and this is to fill the vent [cavity], and make it large, with only hot water or water in which herbs suitable for the case have been boiled.
Form of a vent administered with fire.
The width of its [vent's] opening should be two fingers apart, according to what we have constructed; and its depth should be half the size of a palm; and on one side, in a place about halfway along it, there should be a small hole, according to the size that an awl can enter; it should be made of brass, citron wood, smooth, equal sides, cleaned: so as not to injure the part when it is placed upon it; and in its middle there should be a crossbar transverse from brass or iron, where the candle is placed with fire.
And now it becomes this swollen one large, greater than what we spoke of, and not much smaller than that, according to the illnesses and age of the person using [it].
For swellings in boys are different from those in men, and thick-bodied ones as well.
The quality of applying heat to this swelling on a limb is that you should ignite linen with fire from flax or a small tallow candle, and place it on the middle rung of the crossbar which is in the middle of the swelling, so that the fire is about halfway up the swelling, so as not to burn the body of the sick person.
Then it is to be placed on the limb, and a finger should be over the opening I mentioned, until we hold the swelling; when we need it, we remove the finger, and steam will come out through that opening, and the swelling will immediately be solved.
Then apply fire to the linen in its manner, and repeat it if you need it [the heat].
In swellings administered for pleurisy with water, there is no crossbar nor opening; it is not administered except that it is filled with water and placed on the limb only.
And this is its shape.
And a swelling that is larger, so as to hold more water, is better.
Chapter on Suspension of Sanguisugars.
Chapter CXCVIII: Sanguisugas are not administered in many places except where there is no possible position for swellings due to their smallness, such as the lip, gums, and similar parts. Or in a bare member, such as a finger or nose, and similar parts.
And the quality of using them is that you should come from Sanguisugas which are in sweet, clean water, free from putrefaction.
Then they should be kept in sweet water, day and night, until they are hungry and nothing remains in their stomachs. The body shall first be evacuated with bleeding and with blistering. Then clean the sick limb until it turns red. Then they are placed upon it.
When they are filled and fall off, and there is the possibility of sucking out the place with blistering, then it is more beneficial for healing; if not, then clean the place with vinegar. Then wash it with much water, rub and squeeze it.
If the flow of blood persists after a leech application, and this is due to a discharge, then dip the cloth in cold water, place it on top, until the discharge ceases.
If the blood multiplies, then sprinkle on it powder of almonds ground, or gallnuts and similar things from poppy seeds until the bleeding stops.
Or lay halved, peeled beans on the place and let them remain until they adhere to the location, because blood is stopped by this.
And it is necessary that if a repetition of leech application is required, when possible, replace them.
If leeches are forbidden from suspension, then clean the place with fresh blood. Or make an incision in the places, until something comes out of the blood. Then place them, because as soon as they feel something from the blood, they will stick immediately.
When you want them to fall off, sprinkle something from ground aloes, salt or ashes on them; they will fall immediately.
This Chapter is also frequently necessary in the art of Medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations occurring in bones.
Know ye, O Sons, that foolish physicians and the common people boast about this Chapter, and those who have never looked upon the book of the ancients nor read a letter from it.
And for this reason, this method is deprived of knowledge in our land. And I have never encountered it in good form at all, nor have I attained that which I have attained except for the length of reading the ancient books and my devotion to their understanding until I extracted this knowledge from them.
Then I adhered to experiment and study throughout the length of my life.
And now I have described for you from that Chapter all that my knowledge contains: and over what experiment failed me after I explained it to you, and released it from the burden of length, and shortened it from the end of shortening, and showed it from the end of declining; and I formed in it many shapes of instruments which are administered therein, as I did in the two preceding Chapters.
Title II.
It is necessary to say in the preface of this Chapter, the main points and chapters, which must first be understood by the artist at his station concerning their truth: namely that you, and those who are prompt, may know or learn this noble art from you, and others from you.
Therefore I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or fall occurs in someone, then it is necessary to hasten firstly to phlebotomy him, and to be drained or both at the same time: unless something prohibits this, such as weakness of power; or he who suffers from one of these things is a boy or an old man worn out; or there is a time of intense heat or extreme cold.
Then let him be content with his food, cold vegetables, and onions, and beans; and forbid wine, and thick meats, and filling himself with foods and all food that fills the veins with blood. Until he is secure from a hot purge, and no longer fears the flow of matter to a member; then let the sick person return to his own diet first with which his custom was accustomed.
When the broken bone begins to be restored, then it is necessary that the sick person eat nourishing foods in abundance, coarse, heavy, with viscosity; such as food made from cooked flour and water, rice, heads, feet, entrails of cows, eggs, fresh fish, thick wine, and similar. When this regimen is followed, the setting of the fracture occurs more quickly and better.
And know that broken bones, when they are in men who are in the first old age and decrepit, it is not possible for them to be held together and consolidated according to their nature always, on account of the drying up of their limbs; and they consolidate and hold together those which are from them at the end of softness, like the bones of small children.
However, nature connects something similar to glue around the broken bone from all sides, in which there is thickness, by which it adheres and tightens it until they consolidate opposite each other, and are bound together until it comes to the end of strength and firmness, as it was at first, until it does not prohibit anything from its operations; and for this reason it is necessary that you place nourishment for the sick person in foods which have thickness, viscosity, and thickness, as we said.
And know, that the types of fractures are diverse, according to the differences of the members: for a fracture of the leg is different from a fracture of the head bone; and a fracture of the breastbone is different from a fracture of the backbone; and similarly all other members exist differently to each other; and I come with the reminder of every type of fracture explained in its own chapter, distinct from one another. And fractures of bones are also diversified among themselves.
For there is a curved fracture (which occurs) besides the occurrence of stars (stellae). And sometimes there is a fracture along the length of the bone; and these are its cracks (stagiae, or stars), that is, splinters (astellae), as well as additions proceeding from them, such as in a reed, when a knife is sharpened for writing. And not proceeding (from the bone): and there is a fracture with wound and rupture in the head; and there is a small crack (fractura fissura parua).
And every type has a skill or its own tool in its restoration, according to how it will be remembered, distinguished in its places.
And from that which is recognized in a bone fracture, there is its twisting (tortuositas), and its protrusion (ipsius eminentia): and its appearance to the sense, and its sound when it is compressed with your hand.
When therefore there is no apparent twisting, nor sound when it is touched with your hand or compressed with pressure, nor does a weak great pain occur: then there is not fracture in that place; indeed, it may be a twisting (or a small crack): thus, do not move it with your hand and compression at all; instead, lay medicines on top of it, which will be remembered afterwards, after the appropriate time has passed: then the wound will be sutured with a fine string.
And know that when the place is curved and split, except for what happens in it as a result of strangulation, nevertheless, all its parts are separated from their own: then you should begin from your hour for its correction, equalizing it before hot ulcer occurs to it.
If a hot ulcer occurs to it, then let it be for some days until the ulcer subsides. Then equalize it according to whatever method can be done with gentleness and skill.
And know that the restoration of it, and its equalization, is easier than bones, where strangulations occur.
Then tighten it, according to whatever memory comes to you.
If there are strangulations in the bone, then necessary is the extension of this broken member from two parts, if it is a hand or foot: or with your hand, if the member is small: or with two ropes, or with a rope and your hand.
And let your position be when you place the member on a level place according to its natural shape, until the parts of the broken member are extended: then try, with all skill, and according to whatever method you can in their places, to bring back those additions; and be careful, according to your strength, that pain or injury does not occur to the weak due to your operation: and try, according to your strength, to apply one of two bones with its partner, according to the best forms.
And it is necessary that at that hour you try and touch it with your hand. If therefore you see something different there, correct it, and equalize it according to the measure of your strength.
And be careful not to extend violently or compress too forcefully, as do many fools. They often cause to occur by their operation a hot abscess or contraction in the limb; as we have already seen from their operations many times.
Then attach after the amputation, and a suitable operation, and the tightening of that limb, and calmness, and tranquility; and warn the sick person about it. And make him be careful not to move himself in the hour of his watchings and sleep, at his turning and agitation, and during his illness, and all movements of himself with the utmost strength of his power.
